constancy). The bimodule structure is therefore
$(a_1, a_2) \cdot x = a_1 \cdot x \cdot a_2$, which is precisely the
diagonal bimodule ${}_A A_A$. Similarly for $\mathcal{F}(U_-)$, where
the \emph{opposite} orientation of $U_-$ relative to $U_+$ introduces
the $A^{\mathrm{op}}$ factor: the left action from $J_1$ on $U_-$
is the right action on $U_+$, and vice versa. This is the source
of the $A^{\mathrm{op}}$ in
$A^e = A \otimes A^{\mathrm{op}}$.

The tensor product over $A \otimes A$ of two copies of the diagonal
bimodule is, by definition, the algebraic Hochschild chain complex:
\[
A \otimes^{\mathbf{L}}_{A \otimes A^{\mathrm{op}}} A
= A \otimes^{\mathbf{L}}_{A^e} A
=: \mathrm{HH}_{\bullet,\mathrm{alg}}(A).
\]
Here $A \otimes A$ acts on the left copy of~$A$
via $(a_1, a_2) \cdot x = a_1 \cdot x \cdot a_2$
(using the bimodule structure from $J_1$ and $J_2$), and on the
right copy of~$A$ symmetrically; the tensor product over this action
contracts the two bimodules into the cyclic bar complex
$\cdots \to A^{\otimes 3} \to A^{\otimes 2} \to A$ computing
$\mathrm{HH}_{\bullet,\mathrm{alg}}(A)$.

\emph{Step~5} (Passage to the categorical statement).
If $\mathcal{C} = \mathrm{Perf}(A)$ is the dg-category of perfect
$A$-modules, then
$\mathrm{HH}_{\bullet,\mathrm{cat}}(\mathcal{C})$ is defined as
$\mathrm{HH}_{\bullet,\mathrm{alg}}(A)$ via the Morita-invariant
cyclic bar construction. Combining with Step~4 gives the stated
equivalence
$\int_{S^1} \mathcal{F} \simeq
\mathrm{HH}_{\bullet,\mathrm{cat}}(\mathcal{C})$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Provenance]
\label{rem:annulus-provenance}
The identification of factorization homology on $S^1$ with the
circle-trace/Hochschild construction is due (in the spectral
topological setting, where it computes $\mathrm{THH}$) to
Ben-Zvi--Francis--Nadler~\cite{BZFN10} and
Ayala--Francis~\cite{AF15}; in the vertex algebra setting, the
parallel result appears in Costello--Gwilliam~\cite[Chapter~5]{CG17}.
The chain-complex formula recorded here is the algebraic/categorical
shadow of that spectral statement. The excision argument above
follows the treatment in~\cite{AF15}.
\end{remark}

\subsection{The monodromy subtlety: from chiral to locally constant}
\label{subsec:monodromy-subtlety}

\index{monodromy!factorization homology}

The excision argument of Theorem~\ref{thm:circle-fh-hochschild}
requires $\mathcal{F}$ to be a \emph{locally constant} factorization
algebra on $S^1$. In the chiral algebraic setting, the situation is
more delicate: a chiral algebra~$\cA$ on a curve~$X$ is a
factorization algebra on $X$ that is locally constant on small disks
(the $\Eone$-structure on intervals), but the passage from an interval
to the full circle involves identifying the endpoints. This
identification may carry \emph{monodromy}, a nontrivial automorphism
of the $\Eone$-algebra $A = \cA(I)$ arising from parallel transport
around the puncture.

\begin{definition}[Monodromy automorphism]\label{def:monodromy-aut}
\index{monodromy!automorphism|textbf}
Let $\cA$ be a chiral algebra on a punctured disk $D^\times = D
\setminus \{0\}$, and let $I \subset D^\times$ be an interval.
The fundamental group $\pi_1(D^\times) \cong \Z$ acts on the
fiber $A = \cA(I)$ by monodromy. The \emph{monodromy
automorphism} is the generator:
\[
\mathfrak{m}\colon A \;\xrightarrow{\;\sim\;}\; A,
\]
obtained by analytically continuing sections of $\cA$ around the
puncture once counterclockwise.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Monodromy for standard families;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:monodromy-standard}
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Heisenberg $\mathcal{H}_k$.} The monodromy
 automorphism $\mathfrak{m}$ acts on the mode algebra generated
 by $\{J_n\}_{n \in \Z}$ via $\mathfrak{m}(J_n) = J_n$ for all
 $n$. The monodromy is \emph{trivial} on the algebra. However,
 on Fock modules $F_\lambda$, the monodromy acts by the scalar
 $e^{2\pi i \lambda^2 / (2k)}$
 \textup{(}from the conformal weight $h_\lambda = \lambda^2/(2k)$
 contribution to $q^{L_0}$\textup{)}. For the vacuum module
 $F_0$, this is trivial.
\item \emph{Affine $\widehat{\fg}_k$.} The monodromy is trivial on
 the algebra \textup{(}the current modes $J^a_n$ are
 single-valued\textup{)}. On highest-weight modules $V_\Lambda$ at
 integer level, the monodromy acts by
 $e^{2\pi i h_\Lambda}$ where $h_\Lambda = (\Lambda, \Lambda +
 2\rho) / 2(k + h^\vee)$ is the conformal weight.
\item \emph{Lattice VOA $V_\Lambda$.} The vertex operators
 $e^\alpha$ for $\alpha \in \Lambda$ have monodromy
 $\mathfrak{m}(e^\alpha) = e^{2\pi i (\alpha, \alpha)/2}\, e^\alpha$.
 For an even lattice, $(\alpha, \alpha) \in 2\Z$, so the monodromy
 is trivial. For an odd lattice, the monodromy is a sign
 $(-1)^{(\alpha,\alpha)}$ on each sector (note: odd lattices
 define \emph{super} vertex algebras; the sign is the
 fermion parity).
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
In each case, the monodromy is computed from the $L_0$-eigenvalue.
For a primary field $\phi$ of conformal weight~$h$, the operator
product expansion $\phi(e^{2\pi i} z) = e^{2\pi i h} \phi(z)$ gives
the monodromy phase.

(a)~For $\mathcal{H}_k$: the current $J(z) = \sum_n J_n z^{-n-1}$
has conformal weight~$1$, so $J(e^{2\pi i}z) = e^{2\pi i} \cdot
J(z) \cdot e^{-2\pi i} = J(z)$ (the $z^{-n-1}$ factor absorbs the
phase). More precisely, $\mathfrak{m}(J_n) = J_n$ because the modes
are defined as contour integrals $J_n = \oint z^n J(z)\,dz$ over
cycles that are invariant under the monodromy deck transformation.
On $F_\lambda$, the highest-weight vector $|\lambda\rangle$ has
$L_0$-eigenvalue $h_\lambda = \lambda^2/(2k)$, giving the stated
phase.

(b)~Identical argument for $\widehat{\fg}_k$, with $h_\Lambda$
replacing $h_\lambda$.

(c)~For $V_\Lambda$, $e^\alpha$ has conformal weight
$(\alpha,\alpha)/2$, so $\mathfrak{m}(e^\alpha) = e^{2\pi i
(\alpha,\alpha)/2}\, e^\alpha$. For an even lattice,
$(\alpha,\alpha)/2 \in \Z$, so the phase is~$1$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Twisted algebraic Hochschild homology]
\label{rem:twisted-hochschild}
\index{algebraic Hochschild homology!twisted}
When the monodromy $\mathfrak{m}\colon A \to A$ is nontrivial, the
factorization homology on $S^1$ computes the
\emph{$\mathfrak{m}$-twisted algebraic Hochschild homology}:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:twisted-HH}
\int_{S^1} \mathcal{F}
\;\simeq\;
\mathrm{HH}_{\bullet,\mathrm{alg}}(A;\, {}_{\mathfrak{m}}A)
:= A \otimes^{\mathbf{L}}_{A^e} {}_{\mathfrak{m}}A,
\end{equation}
where ${}_{\mathfrak{m}}A$ is $A$ as a right $A$-module but with
left action twisted by $\mathfrak{m}$: $a \cdot_{\mathfrak{m}} x :=
\mathfrak{m}(a) \cdot x$. The excision argument of
Theorem~\ref{thm:circle-fh-hochschild} goes through verbatim with
$U_-$ contributing the twisted bimodule structure: the analytic
continuation around the full circle inserts $\mathfrak{m}$ into one
of the two collar inclusions.

For the standard families of
Proposition~\ref{prop:monodromy-standard}, the monodromy is trivial
on the algebra itself (the algebra modes are single-valued), so the
untwisted identification~\eqref{eq:circle-fh-HH} holds. The twist
becomes visible only at the module level: the torus partition function
$Z_{T^2}(\cA) = \mathrm{Tr}_{\mathcal{H}}(q^{L_0 - c/24})$ traces
over the Hilbert space~$\mathcal{H}$ with the insertion of
$q^{L_0}$, which is precisely the twist by the monodromy of the
cylinder.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The $(g{=}1, k{=}0)$ modular MC component]
\label{rem:mc-hh-identification}
\index{Maurer--Cartan!genus-1 and algebraic Hochschild trace}
The $(g=1, n=0)$ component of the modular MC equation
(Chapter~\ref{ch:en-koszul-duality}) is:
\[
d\Theta_{\cA}^{(1,0)} + \tfrac{1}{2}
 [\Theta_{\cA}^{(0)}, \Theta_{\cA}^{(0)}]^{(1,0)}
 + \Delta_{\mathrm{sew}}\Theta_{\cA}^{(0,2)} = 0.
\]
The sewing operator $\Delta_{\mathrm{sew}}$ contracts two external
legs of $\Theta^{(0,2)}_{\cA}$ using the propagator on the torus.
This is the genus-$1$ algebraic Hochschild differential: the annulus
amplitude $\Theta^{(0,2)}_{\cA}$ evaluated on two inputs and sewn
into a torus is the trace $\mathrm{Tr}(m_2(-,-))$, the standard
generator of $\mathrm{HH}_{0,\mathrm{alg}}(A)$. The identification
of the locally constant interval model
$\int_{S^1}\mathcal F_A$ with
$\mathrm{HH}_{\bullet,\mathrm{alg}}(A)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:circle-fh-hochschild})
is therefore the $n=0$ case of the general MC$\to$sewing
correspondence. It is not a $\cD$-module restriction of the chiral
algebra~$\cA$ to a real circle.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Heisenberg verification}

\begin{example}[Algebraic Hochschild chains of the Heisenberg interval algebra;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{ex:heisenberg-HH-chains}
\index{Heisenberg algebra!algebraic Hochschild chains}
We verify the identification
$\int_{S^1} \mathcal F_{\mathcal{H}_k}^{\mathrm{lc}}
\simeq \mathrm{HH}_{\bullet,\mathrm{alg}}(A_{\mathcal{H}_k})$
against the known genus-$1$ partition function, where
$\mathcal F_{\mathcal{H}_k}^{\mathrm{lc}}$ is the locally constant
interval model extracted from the Heisenberg chiral algebra and
$A_{\mathcal{H}_k}$ is its completed interval algebra.
Here $\mathrm{HH}_{\bullet,\mathrm{alg}}(\mathcal{H}_k)$ is
shorthand for the algebraic Hochschild homology of the interval
algebra extracted from the locally constant Heisenberg
factorization algebra.

The Heisenberg vertex algebra $\mathcal{H}_k$ at level $k \neq 0$
is generated by a single current
$J(z)=\sum_{n\in\mathbb Z}J_nz^{-n-1}$ with OPE
$J(z)J(w)\sim k/(z-w)^2$. The completed interval algebra is the
oscillator algebra with
$[J_m,J_n]=km\,\delta_{m+n,0}$, completed in the Fock topology.
This completion is part of the factorisation-algebra input. It is not
the ordinary algebraic Weyl algebra with its uncompleted bar complex.

The chiral zero-mode calculation of Example~\ref{ex:E2-heisenberg}
gives
\[
\mathrm{HH}_\bullet^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal{H}_k)
= \C[c] \otimes \Lambda(\sigma),
\qquad |c| = 2,\; |\sigma| = 1.
\]
The class $c \in \mathrm{HH}_2$ is the Chern class of the level
(the universal deformation class), and $\sigma \in \mathrm{HH}_1$
is the fundamental class of $S^1$ in the cyclic direction.
This polynomial algebra is a chiral zero-mode/mixed-complex
calculation. It is not an assertion that the ordinary algebraic
Hochschild homology of an uncompleted Weyl algebra is polynomial.

The factorization homology
$\int_{S^1}\mathcal F_{\mathcal{H}_k}^{\mathrm{lc}}
\simeq \mathrm{HH}_{\bullet,\mathrm{alg}}(A_{\mathcal{H}_k})$
computes the completed algebraic Hochschild chains of the locally
constant Heisenberg interval algebra. The torus partition function is the Euler
characteristic of $\int_{T^2}\mathcal{H}_k$,
which by the sewing formula reduces to
$\mathrm{Tr}_{F_0}(q^{L_0 - c/24})$ where $F_0$ is the
vacuum module (the trace inserts the $q$-grading operator
on the space of states):
\[
Z_{T^2}(\mathcal{H}_k)
= \mathrm{Tr}_{F_0}(q^{L_0 - 1/24})
= q^{-1/24} \prod_{n=1}^{\infty} \frac{1}{1 - q^n}
= \frac{1}{\eta(\tau)},
\]
where $\eta(\tau) = q^{1/24} \prod_{n \geq 1}(1-q^n)$ is the
Dedekind eta function.

The uncompleted Weyl algebra gives a useful warning. In any finite
oscillator window $A_N$ one has
$1=(kn)^{-1}[J_n,J_{-n}]$ for $1\le n\le N$, hence the ordinary
abelianization $A_N/[A_N,A_N]$ vanishes. The vacuum trace and the
one-dimensional genus-$1$ conformal block therefore do not come from
the naive algebraic abelianization of an uncompleted Weyl algebra.
They come from the completed factorisation trace and its Fock
continuous trace. With this completion understood,
Theorem~\ref{thm:partition-cyclic} identifies the cyclic degree-$0$
trace with the one-dimensional genus-$1$ conformal-block line. After
Eilenberg--Mac Lane spectrification this completed chain complex is
the rational shadow of the corresponding $\mathrm{THH}$, but the
present computation remains in chain complexes.
\end{example}

\begin{remark}[Annulus vs torus]
\label{rem:annulus-vs-torus}
\index{annulus!vs torus}
The factorization homology $\int_{S^1} \mathcal{F}$ over the circle
gives the algebraic Hochschild chains
$\mathrm{HH}_{\bullet,\mathrm{alg}}(A)$. The partition
function on the torus $T^2 = S^1 \times S^1$ involves a further
circle integral, which gives the cyclic homology
$\mathrm{HC}_\bullet(A)$ (the $S^1$-equivariant version of
$\mathrm{HH}_{\bullet,\mathrm{alg}}$). Schematically:
\[
\int_{S^1} \mathcal{F} = \mathrm{HH}_{\bullet,\mathrm{alg}}(A),
\qquad
\int_{T^2} \mathcal{F}
= \mathrm{HC}_\bullet(A)
= \mathrm{HH}_{\bullet,\mathrm{alg}}(A)_{hS^1}.
\]
The first circle is the spatial circle (excision gives algebraic
Hochschild chains); the second is the thermal circle (the
$S^1$-action on the chain complex gives cyclic homology).
For the Heisenberg:
$\mathrm{HC}_0(\mathcal{H}_k) = \C$, and the character
$\mathrm{Tr}_{F_0}(q^{L_0-c/24}) = 1/\eta(\tau)$ is the
generating function for the graded dimensions of the cyclic complex.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Relation to Theorem~C \textup{(}complementarity\textup{)}]
\label{rem:annulus-complementarity}
\index{complementarity!annulus}
The algebraic Hochschild chain identification provides the genus-$1$ input to
the complementarity theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:quantum-complementarity-main}). At genus~$1$, the
complementarity formula reads
$Q_1(\cA) \oplus Q_1(\cA^!) \cong H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1},
\mathcal{Z}(\cA))$.
The left-hand side is computed by categorical/algebraic Hochschild
chains of $\cA$ and $\cA^!$ respectively (via the annulus
identification in a compact-generator chart); the right-hand side
is the cohomology of the moduli space with coefficients in the
center sheaf. The complementarity is the statement that the two
categorical circle-trace complexes assemble into a complete basis
for the modular functor at genus~$1$.
\end{remark}

\subsection{The Hochschild invariant of the modular Koszul object}

The modular Koszul object attached to a factorisation algebra on a
curve has three visible projections: the bar--cobar adjunction
\textup{(}Theorem~A\textup{)}, inversion on the Koszul locus
\textup{(}Theorem~B\textup{)}, and derived-centre complementarity
\textup{(}Theorem~C\textup{)}. Chiral Hochschild cohomology is its
infinitesimal projection. On the PBW chiral Koszul locus, with the
ordered-to-symmetric averaging hypothesis of
Corollary~\ref{cor:hochschild-averaging-symmetric}, Theorem~H places
$\ChirHoch^\bullet(\cA)$ in cohomological degrees $\{0,1,2\}$; degree
$2$ carries first-order chiral deformations and degree~$3$ is absent
on the curve-level complex.

The modular characteristic~$\kappa(\cA)$ is the linear coefficient of
the same object. The shadow obstruction tower
$\kappa(\cA)\to\Delta_\cA\to\mathfrak C_\cA\to\mathfrak Q_\cA\to\cdots$
records higher finite-order invariants, and its all-degree limit is
the bar-intrinsic Maurer--Cartan class~$\Theta_\cA$.

\section{Chiral Hochschild cohomology of the K3 bialgebra $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$}
\label{sec:hochcoh-supplement}

\begin{remark}[Hochschild concentration for $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$:
the ambient-curve scope]
\label{rem:hochcoh-1}
Theorem~H (Hochschild concentration in degrees $\{0,1,2\}$) is an
\emph{ambient-curve} statement: the amplitude bound $[0,2]$ of
Thm.~\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth} derives from the
$\mathcal D_X$-module de~Rham amplitude $[0, 2\dim_{\mathbb C} X] = [0,2]$
on a smooth projective curve~$X$ ($\dim_{\mathbb C}X = 1$). The K3
chiral bialgebra $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ sits inside this Theorem~H scope
only after it has been restricted to the PBW chiral Koszul
factorisation algebra on the fixed curve~$X$. In that curve-level
ambient Theorem~H asserts the amplitude statement
\[
 \ChirHoch^n(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})=0\qquad(n>2),
\]
under the same completion, averaging, finite-type, and non-critical
hypotheses as for the standard families. It does not identify the
individual groups
$\ChirHoch^0$, $\ChirHoch^1$, and $\ChirHoch^2$ for
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$. Centre, outer-derivation, and Koszul-class
identifications require separate calculations in the K3 Hall model and
cannot be imported from CoHA or DT data.

The CY-$3$ extension is an \emph{orthogonal scope}, not a weakening
of Theorem~H. Under the Vol~III two-stage specialization
$\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}=\SpCh_{\Sigma_2,C}\circ\PhiFA_3$
the transverse CY-$3$ fibre $\mathrm{K3}\times E$ carries an additional
cohomological degree~$3$ class beyond the curve-ambient $\{0,1,2\}$:
the CY-$3$ volume class $[\omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\in
H^6(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$, transported by $\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$ to
\[
 [\chi_3]\;\in\;\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}),
 \qquad
 \chi_3 = \Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}\bigl(K_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}\bigr),
\]
with $K_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}$ the Schiffmann--Vasserot degree-$3$
CoHA generator of the chiral Hall algebra attached to
$\mathrm{K3}\times E$ (Vol~III
Prop.~\ref{V3-prop:SV-e3-sugawara-toroidal}, Cambridge-and-Moscow
convention for free-field form).
The explicit chain-level representative
(Vol~III eq.~\eqref{eq:W18-chi-3-chain-level}) is the Arnold-relation
skew-symmetrised triple product
\[
 \chi_3^{\mathrm{chain}}(a_1, a_2, a_3; z_1, z_2, z_3)
 \;=\;
 \sum_{\sigma\in S_3}
 \mathrm{sgn}(\sigma)\,
 \frac{\langle\mu_3^{\mathrm{CoHA}}(a_{\sigma(1)}, a_{\sigma(2)}, a_{\sigma(3)}),
 \Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}\rangle_{\mathrm{Muk}}}{
 (z_{\sigma(1)} - z_{\sigma(2)})(z_{\sigma(2)} - z_{\sigma(3)})
 (z_{\sigma(3)} - z_{\sigma(1)})},
\]
The non-vanishing assertion is made below only under the
product-ambient convergence and top-entry hypotheses. Its two numerical
normalisations are the triangle-cycle pairing
$\chi_3(\Delta(e_\alpha, f_\alpha, h_\alpha)) =
2\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3$ on a real simple root $\alpha$
of $\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}$ (Vol~III
Prop.~\ref{prop:W18-chi-3-nonvanishing-triangle}), and the
OP-normalized Donaldson--Thomas coefficient
\[
 [p^{-1}q^{-1}y^0]\!\left(-(\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}\right)=1.
\]
After multiplying this normalized coefficient by
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi\mathrm i)^3
=2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$, it agrees with the
Mukai-normalised chiral pairing of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}. The coefficient is a
value-level DT test, not an ordinary curve-level Hochschild class.

\emph{Scope discipline.} The ambient-curve Theorem~H is a theorem of
this volume (Vol~I): $\ChirHoch^\bullet(\cA)$ is supported in
cohomological degrees $\{0,1,2\}$ for $\cA$ on a smooth projective
curve under the PBW generic hypotheses. Before any collapse or
top-entry vanishing, a CY-$d$ product-ambient filtration has curve
degrees $0,1,2$ and fibre degrees $0,\ldots,d$, hence the weak
total-degree ceiling is $d+2$. The stronger pattern
$\{0,1,\ldots,d\}$ belongs to the Vol.~III companion surface and is
conditional here on the product-ambient complex, spectral-sequence
collapse, and top-entry vanishing hypotheses
(Rem.~\ref{V3-rem:hochcalc-theoremH-CY3-scope} of
\texttt{hochschild\_calculus.tex} and
Thm.~\ref{thm:W18-chi3-koszul-obstruction}). Francis $2013$
Adv.\ Math.\ $239$ Thm.\ $1.1$ supplies the higher
Deligne/tangent structure for categorical Hochschild objects, and
Caldararu $2005$ Adv.\ Math.\ $194$ \S4 supplies the CY-$d$ volume
class; neither reference proves the Vol.~I curve-level concentration
statement or the product-ambient vanishing above degree~$d$.
The projection of the CY-$3$ class to the ambient-curve complex
vanishes on the Koszul locus
$\mathcal U_{\mathrm{Kosz}}^{\mathrm{K3}} =
\overline{\mathcal A}_2\setminus(H_1\cup H_4)$; the non-zero class
itself belongs to the product-ambient complex
$X\times(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$. Along $H_1\cup H_4$ the product
spectral sequence acquires Humbert-boundary contributions, so the
same symbol must not be read as an ordinary curve-level
$\ChirHoch^3$ class (Vol~III
Rem.~\ref{V3-rem:chi-3-Koszul-locus-scope}).
For the CY-$0$ classical case (associative algebra with cyclic
pairing), the CY-$d$ pattern reduces to $\{0,1,2\}$, recovering
Theorem~H as stated here.
Primary:
Hinich $2010$ Adv.\ Math.\ $223$ \S3 (concentration via the
$\mathcal D_X$-amplitude bound);
Francis $2013$ Adv.\ Math.\ $239$ Thm.\ $1.1$ (categorical
Hochschild/higher Deligne structure);
Caldararu $2005$ Adv.\ Math.\ $194$ \S4.2
(CY-$d$ volume class in degree~$d$);
Kontsevich $2003$ Lett.\ Math.\ Phys.\ $66$ (formality).
Cross-ref Vol~III, Chapter~\ref{V3-ch:k3-chiral-bialgebra-platonic},
and Vol~III, Rem.~\ref{V3-rem:hochcalc-theoremH-CY3-scope}.
\end{remark}

\providecommand{\Muk}{\mathrm{Muk}}
\providecommand{\CoHA}{\mathrm{CoHA}}
\providecommand{\SpCh}{\mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}}
\providecommand{\PhiFA}{\Phi^{\mathrm{FA}}}

\begin{theorem}[Explicit non-vanishing product-ambient
$\ChirHoch^3$-cocycle on $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$, Siegel comparison chamber]
\label{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $X$ be a smooth projective curve, $\mathcal U$ a formal disc
$\mathcal U\subset X$, and let
\[
 \mathbf H_{\Delta_5}
 \;=\;\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}\bigl(D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3}\times E)\bigr)
 \;=\;\SpCh_{\Sigma_2,C}\!\bigl(\PhiFA_3(D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3}\times E))\bigr)
\]
denote the K3$\times E$ chiral bialgebra of
Vol~III~Chapter~\ref{V3-ch:k3-chiral-bialgebra-platonic}, viewed as a
factorisation algebra on~$X$ through the Vol~III composite
$\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}=\SpCh_{\Sigma_2,C}\circ\PhiFA_3$. Assume the product-ambient mixed
complex for $X\times(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$ converges and satisfies
the top-entry vanishing condition
$E_\infty^{p,q}=0$ for $p+q>3$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch-above-degree-d-vanishes}; the theorem is
therefore a Vol.~III companion statement, not a Vol.~I Theorem~H
statement. Let $\mu_3^{\CoHA}$ be the
Schiffmann--Vasserot degree-$3$ CoHA product of
Vol~III~Prop.~\ref{prop:W18-SV-degree-3-generator}
(\texttt{toric\_cy3\_coha.tex}),
$\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}
= [\omega_{\mathrm{K3}}]\wedge[\omega_E]\in H^6(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$
the CY-$3$ volume class, and
$\langle-,-\rangle_{\Muk}$ the Mukai pairing on $\mathrm{K3}\times E$.
Assume the chosen completed shuffle representative satisfies the
CoHA Hochschild-cycle identity
\[
 b_{\CoHA}\mu_3^{\CoHA}=\partial^{\CoHA}\psi_2
\]
for a $2$-cochain $\psi_2$ whose Mukai trace against
$\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}$ is exact. Associativity of the binary
CoHA product alone is not used as a substitute for this cycle identity.
Define, for $a_1,a_2,a_3\in\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ with ordered
insertion points $z_1,z_2,z_3\in\mathcal U$, the cochain
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chirhoch3-chain-level-Delta5}
 \chi_3^{\mathrm{chain}}(a_1,a_2,a_3; z_1,z_2,z_3)
 \;=\;
 \sum_{\sigma\in S_3}
 \mathrm{sgn}(\sigma)\,
 \frac{\langle\mu_3^{\CoHA}(a_{\sigma(1)},a_{\sigma(2)},a_{\sigma(3)}),
 \Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}\rangle_{\Muk}}
 {(z_{\sigma(1)}-z_{\sigma(2)})
 (z_{\sigma(2)}-z_{\sigma(3)})
 (z_{\sigma(3)}-z_{\sigma(1)})}.
\end{equation}
Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
 \item \textup{(Closure.)}
 $\chi_3^{\mathrm{chain}}$ is a Hochschild $3$-cocycle on
 $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$: its chiral Hochschild boundary vanishes,
 $\partial^{\mathrm{ch}}\chi_3^{\mathrm{chain}}=0$.
 \item \textup{(Non-vanishing.)}
 $\chi_3^{\mathrm{chain}}$ is not a coboundary: its class
 $[\chi_3]\in\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$
 is non-zero.
 \item \textup{(Conditional product-ambient top slot.)} The class lives
 in the scope-enlarged complex
 $\ChirHoch^\bullet_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}$ on the ambient
 $X\times(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$. Under the top-entry vanishing
 hypothesis its support is bounded by $\{0,1,2,3\}$, matching the
 K3 Hall--Drinfeld row: the Mukai conductor is
 $K^{\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})=8$, while the
 Borcherds denominator weight is
 $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\Delta_5)=5$. The principal
 $\mathcal W_3$ value $250/3$ belongs to the class-$\mathsf M$
 Siegel chamber and is not a scalar of
 $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$. On the
 ambient-curve-only complex
 $\ChirHoch^\bullet(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ of Theorem~H
 (curve~$X$ alone), $[\chi_3]$ projects to $0$; concentration
 in $\{0,1,2\}$ holds unchanged. If an $H^1(\mathcal O_X)$ or
 top-row product-ambient entry survives above total degree~$3$, this
 item does not assert concentration.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
(i)~\emph{Closure.} The Hochschild boundary
$\partial^{\mathrm{ch}}$ on the ordered $E_1$-chiral cochain complex
$\mathrm{CC}^{\mathrm{ord}}_\bullet(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$
decomposes into a face part
$\partial^{\mathrm{face}}$ (multiplying adjacent inputs via
$\mu_2^{\CoHA}$) and a configuration part
$\partial^{\mathrm{conf}}$ (residue on the Arnold forms
$\eta_{ij}=d\log(z_i-z_j)/(2\pi\mathrm{i})$); see
Thm.~\ref{thm:gerstenhaber-structure} for the named decomposition
and Kapranov~$1999$ Compos.\ Math.\ $115$ \S~3 for the Arnold-cochain
formalism.

For~\eqref{eq:chirhoch3-chain-level-Delta5}, the face part produces
$\langle\mu_3^{\CoHA}\circ(\mu_2\otimes\mathrm{id}\pm
\mathrm{id}\otimes\mu_2), \Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}\rangle_{\Muk}$.
By the CoHA Hochschild-cycle hypothesis in the statement, this face
term is $\partial^{\CoHA}\psi_2$ after the completed
Schiffmann--Vasserot shuffle comparison
(Schiffmann--Vasserot~$2013$ Publ.~IHES~$118$ Thm.~B). Pairing with
$\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}$ against the Mukai form kills the exact
term by the cyclic trace property of the CY-$3$ Mukai pairing
(Caldararu~$2005$~\S~4.2). Hence
$\partial^{\mathrm{face}}\chi_3^{\mathrm{chain}}=0$.

For the configuration part, $\partial^{\mathrm{conf}}$ applied to
$(z_1-z_2)^{-1}(z_2-z_3)^{-1}(z_3-z_1)^{-1}$ produces the triple
wedge $\eta_{12}\wedge\eta_{23}\wedge\eta_{31}$, which on summing over
$S_3$ with the sign weight reduces to the Arnold relation
\[
 \eta_{12}\wedge\eta_{23}
 +\eta_{23}\wedge\eta_{31}
 +\eta_{31}\wedge\eta_{12}\;=\;0
\]
on $\mathrm{Conf}_3(\mathcal U)$ (Arnold~$1969$, or
Beilinson--Drinfeld~$2004$ \S~3.4 for the factorisation-algebra
formulation). Hence
$\partial^{\mathrm{conf}}\chi_3^{\mathrm{chain}}=0$. Combining the two
vanishings, $\partial^{\mathrm{ch}}\chi_3^{\mathrm{chain}}=0$.

(ii)~\emph{Non-vanishing (two value computations, explicit
rational value).} The computation returns the
explicit rational value
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chi3-rational-value}
 \langle[\chi_3],[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\rangle_{\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}}
 \;=\;\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3
 \;=\;2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3
\;\in\;\mathbb Q\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3,
\end{equation}
established below by the CoHA triangle-cycle computation and the
OP-normalized reciprocal-Igusa computation. The elliptic-volume and
relative-HPD paragraphs are compatibility checks.

\textsc{Path A: CoHA triangle-cycle via the Schiffmann--Vasserot
Casimir.} Let $\alpha$ be a real simple root of
$\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}$ with Tits--Vinberg norm
$(\alpha,\alpha)=2$ and let $(e_\alpha,f_\alpha,h_\alpha)$ be the
$\mathfrak{sl}_2$-triple realising the root string, pushed to the
CoHA via the Davison--Meinhardt factorisation-algebra construction and to the
chiral side via $\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$ and
Kapranov--Vasserot~$2018$~arXiv:1802.07988~Thm.~$1.1$
transport. Schiffmann--Vasserot~$2013$~Publ.~IHES~$118$~Thm.~$6.1$
and the Okounkov~$2017$~arXiv:1512.07363~\S~6
Chern-character formula for the CoHA$_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}$ compute
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:sv-triple-casimir}
 \mu_3^{\CoHA}(e_\alpha,f_\alpha,h_\alpha)
 \;=\;
 \mathrm{Cas}_2(\alpha)\cdot[\omega_{\mathrm{K3}}]\wedge[\omega_E]
 \;+\;\partial^{\CoHA}(\cdots),
\end{equation}
with $\mathrm{Cas}_2(\alpha)=(\alpha,\alpha)/2=1$ on the real simple
root and the exact remainder absorbed by Mukai-pairing exactness
on the CY-$3$ stratum (Caldararu~$2005$~Adv.\ Math.\ $194$~\S~4.2).
The three Arnold forms
$\eta_{ij}=d\log(z_i-z_j)/(2\pi\mathrm{i})$
each restore a $2\pi\mathrm{i}$ on desuspension of the triple
product $1/[(z_1-z_2)(z_2-z_3)(z_3-z_1)]$; the Mukai--pairing
normalisation
$\langle\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}},\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}}\rangle_{\Muk}
=\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2$
(Mukai~$1987$~\emph{Symposium on algebraic geometry}~Thm.~1.5);
the elliptic integral $\int_E[\omega_E]=\mathrm{Vol}(E)$:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chi3-triangle-value-corrected}
 \chi_3^{\mathrm{chain}}\bigl(\Delta(e_\alpha,f_\alpha,h_\alpha)\bigr)
 \;=\;
 \underbrace{\mathrm{Cas}_2(\alpha)}_{=1}
 \cdot
 \underbrace{\langle\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}},\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}}\rangle_{\Muk}}_{=2}
 \cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3
 \;=\;2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3.
\end{equation}
Coboundaries $\partial^{\mathrm{ch}}\psi$ with
$\psi\in\mathrm{CC}^2(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ pair to zero against
the closed triangle cycle by Stokes on the closed threefold
$\mathrm{K3}\times E$: the pairing of an exact form with the
Arnold-form volume class produces no boundary contribution. Hence
$[\chi_3]\neq 0$. With
$\mathrm{Cas}_2(\alpha)=1$ and
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2$, the normalised value is
$2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3$ as
in~\eqref{eq:chi3-triangle-value-corrected}.

\textsc{Path B: reduced Donaldson--Thomas via the normalized Igusa
product.} Put
\[
 \Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}:=\Delta_5^2,\qquad
 D_5 := 64^{-1}\Delta_5.
\]
Here $\Delta_5$ is the theta/Gritsenko-normalized square root with
leading Fourier coefficient $64$, and $D_5$ is the monic
Gritsenko--Nikulin product. This normalization is checked by the exact
theta-series computation
\texttt{igusa-cusp-form/compute/verify\_square\_root.py} and by the
theta/monic comparison in
\texttt{calabi-yau-quantum-groups/compute/lib/borcherds\_denominator\_phi10\_engine.py}.
Oberdieck--Pixton's scalar product is
\[
 \Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}} = D_5^2
 = 4096^{-1}\Delta_5^2
 = 4096^{-1}\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}.
\]
Thus the reduced Donaldson--Thomas product is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:OP-DT-normalized-product}
 Z^X_{\mathrm{OP/DT}}
 =-\bigl(\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}\bigr)^{-1}
 =-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}
 =-4096\,\bigl(\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}\bigr)^{-1}.
\end{equation}
Sources that write the monic OP product by the unqualified Igusa symbol
record the same normalized reciprocal; in this paragraph
$\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}=\Delta_5^2$ and
$\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=4096^{-1}\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}$.
The degree-zero DT partition function on
$\mathrm{K3}\times E$ is \emph{trivial}: since
$\chi(\mathrm{K3}\times E)=\chi(\mathrm{K3})\cdot\chi(E)=24\cdot 0=0$,
the MNOP MacMahon prefactor $M(-q)^\chi$ reduces to $1$ and
$Z_{\mathrm{DT},0}(q)=1$ (cf.\ \texttt{cy\_dt\_k3e\_engine.py}
\S~3: \texttt{dt\_degree0\_k3xe}). The non-trivial chiral
Hochschild pairing lives entirely in the \emph{reduced} MOP theory.
Oberdieck~$2018$~Geom.\ \& Topol.\ $22$~Thm.~$2$
(equivalent via the reduced Maulik--Oberdieck--Pandharipande~$2017$
arXiv:1605.05473~Thm.~$1$ correspondence) identifies the full
reduced-DT generating function with the reciprocal of the OP-normalized
Igusa product:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:oberdieck-reduced-dt}
 \sum_{h\ge 0,\,d\ge 0,\,k\in\mathbb Z}
 \mathrm{DT}^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}
 (\beta_h,d,k)\,p^{h-1}q^{d-1}y^k
 \;=\;-\frac{1}{\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}(\tau,z,\sigma)}
 \;=\;-4096\,\Delta_5(\tau,z,\sigma)^{-2},
\end{equation}
with $p=e^{2\pi\mathrm{i}\sigma}$, $q=e^{2\pi\mathrm{i}\tau}$,
$y=e^{2\pi\mathrm{i}z}$, the triple $(\beta_h,d,k)$ indexing a
K3-curve class of Beauville--Bogomolov norm $\beta_h^2=2h-2$, an
$E$-degree $d$, and a fibre-twist exponent $k$. The Kapranov--Vasserot
CoHA/chiral-Hochschild compatibility transports
$\langle[\chi_3],[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\rangle_{\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}}$ to
the polar-leading $(\beta_0,0,0)=(h=0,d=0,k=0)$ coefficient of the
reciprocal OP-normalized Igusa product in the positive Weyl chamber
$|y|<1$ of
Gritsenko--Nikulin~$1998$~Amer.\ J.\ Math.\ $120$~\S~3:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chi3-dt-pairing}
 I_{\mathrm{OP}}([\chi_3])
 \;:=\;[p^{-1}q^{-1}y^0]\!\left(-(\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}\right)
 \;=\;[p^{-1}q^{-1}y^0]\!\left(-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}\right)
 \;=\;1.
\end{equation}
The value $1$ is the normalized leading Fourier coefficient of the reciprocal
of the OP-normalized automorphic product
$\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=D_5^2=pqy^{-1}(1-y)^2\prod_{(n,m,\ell)>0}
(1-p^mq^ny^\ell)^{c(4mn-\ell^2)}$,
with $c(\cdot)$ the Fourier coefficients of the K3 elliptic genus
$2\phi_{0,1}$: the polar prefactor $pqy^{-1}(1-y)^2$ inverts in
$|y|<1$ to $p^{-1}q^{-1}y\sum_{j\ge 0}(j+1)y^j$, whose $y^0$
coefficient under the Gritsenko--Nikulin Weyl-chamber prescription
evaluates to $1$. The elliptic-genus coefficient table
$c(-1)=2,c(0)=20,c(3)=-128,c(4)=216,\ldots$
(Eguchi--Ooguri--Taormina--Yang~$1989$~Nuclear Phys.~B~$315$;
verified to $n\le 2$ in \texttt{cy\_dt\_k3e\_engine.py}~\S~1
via the $\phi_{0,1}$-Fourier table entries
$c(0,0)=10,\,c(0,\pm1)=1$ of Eichler--Zagier normalisation) controls
the full $(\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}$-expansion. Non-vanishing of the leading
coefficient~\eqref{eq:chi3-dt-pairing} witnesses $[\chi_3]\neq 0$
independently of Path~A after multiplication by
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$,
which gives the full chiral Mukai value
\eqref{eq:chi3-rational-value}. The CY-$3$ reduced cancellation
annihilates the $\chi=0$ degree-zero DT prefactor, not this reduced
pairing; the correct index for $[\chi_3]$ is the
Beauville--Bogomolov class $(\beta_0,0,0)$ of the reduced theory,
governed by $(\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}$ rather than by
$M(-q)^\chi$. The Oberdieck--Pixton automorphic DT theorem controls
this product normalisation. The broader
Oberdieck--Pixton/Oberdieck--Pandharipande reduced-DT theory supplies
the generating series, not a Hall product, primitive bracket, compact
critical CoHA, or Drinfeld double without the additional compact-source
data named below.

\textsc{Compatibility C: elliptic-volume scaling and the CY-$2$
boundary.}
The factor $\int_E[\omega_E]=\mathrm{Vol}(E)$ in
\eqref{eq:chi3-triangle-value-corrected} gives a useful filtration
check on the product-ambient representative: under the boundary
degeneration $\mathrm{Vol}(E)\to 0$, the CY-$3$ volume
$[\omega_{\mathrm{K3}}]\wedge[\omega_E]$ loses the elliptic factor
and the degree-$3$ fibre slot degenerates to the CY-$2$ K3 boundary
slot. Kontsevich formality and the
Deligne--Griffiths--Morgan--Sullivan formality theorem for compact
K\"ahler manifolds identify the CY-$2$ boundary as the depth-$2$
formal piece.

This volume-scaling argument is not used as an independent proof of
non-exactness. The product-ambient differential and the completed
trace data may vary with the CY-$3$ input, so
$\mathrm{Vol}(E)$-dependence alone does not rule out coboundaries.
It records compatibility of the non-zero values obtained in the CoHA
and OP-normalized DT computations with the CY-$2$ degeneration.

\textsc{Path D: relative homological projective duality over~$E$.}
Kuznetsov homological projective duality
(Kuznetsov~$2007$~Publ.\ IHES~$105$~Thm.~$1.1$, hereafter HPD)
attaches to a Fano variety $Y\hookrightarrow\mathbb P^N$ equipped
with a Lefschetz decomposition
$D^b\mathrm{Coh}(Y)=\langle\mathcal A_0,\mathcal A_1(1),\ldots,
\mathcal A_{m-1}(m-1)\rangle$ a dual Lefschetz pair
$(Y^\vee,\mathcal A^\vee_\bullet)$, identifying Kuznetsov
components across linear sections. The Fano requirement
$\omega_Y$ strictly anti-ample
(Kuznetsov~$2007$~Def.~$4.1$, Rem.~$4.2$) is load-bearing: the
Lefschetz blocks are generated by twists of $\mathcal A_0$ by
$\mathcal O_Y(1)=\omega_Y^{-1/r}$, and this twist is trivial
(no information is carried) on any strict CY target.

For $Y=\mathrm{K3}\times E$,
$\omega_Y\cong\omega_{\mathrm{K3}}\boxtimes\omega_E\cong
\mathcal O_Y$ by K3 and elliptic canonical triviality
(Barth--Peters--van~de~Ven~$1984$~\S~VIII.3;
Silverman~$1986$~\S~III.1), so the Fano condition fails. No
absolute Lefschetz decomposition with non-trivial twist exists,
and absolute HPD is \emph{not applicable} to
$\mathrm{K3}\times E$: this is the structural obstruction and it
is exact, not a gap to be filled.

The replacement used here is conditional. Assume the K3 factor has a
degree-$14$ polarisation and choose a smooth cubic fourfold $Y_4$ with
$\mathrm{Ku}(Y_4)\simeq D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3})$
(Kuznetsov--Markushevich~$2009$~J.\ Reine Angew.\ Math.\ $627$
Thm.~$1.1$; Addington--Thomas~$2014$~Duke Math.\ J.\ $163$
Thm.~$1.1$). The product family
$\widetilde Y:=Y_4\times E\to E$ is a relative Fano family, and the
relative HPD framework of Kuznetsov over a smooth base
(Kuznetsov~$2018$~Crelle~$736$~\S~$2$; Kuznetsov--Perry~$2021$
J.\ Eur.\ Math.\ Soc.\ $23$ Thm.~$1.1$) gives a Fano fibration pair
$(\widetilde Y/E,\widetilde Y^\vee/E)$ with
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:hpd-fibration-pair}
 \mathrm{Ku}(\widetilde Y/E)
 \;\simeq\;D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3}\times E),
 \qquad
 \mathrm{Ku}(\widetilde Y^\vee/E)\,=\,
 \text{relative HPD-dual category over }E,
\end{equation}
where each fibre of $\widetilde Y/E$ is the chosen cubic fourfold of
Kuznetsov--Markushevich type, and the relative Lefschetz structure is
$\pi$-equivariant by Kuznetsov--Perry~$2021$~Thm.~$1.7$. The categorical Hochschild
cohomology of $\mathrm{Ku}(\widetilde Y/E)$ carries the
$(d-2)$-shifted Poisson structure with $d=3$
(Kuznetsov--Perry~$2021$~\S~$1$), and the degree-$3$ class
used in the comparison is the product of the K3 categorical volume
with the elliptic one-form,
\[
 [\omega_{\mathrm{K3}/E}]\in H^3(\mathrm{K3}\times E,\cO),\qquad
 [\omega_{\mathrm{K3}/E}]=
 [\omega_{\mathrm{K3}}]\boxtimes[\mathrm{d}z_E]
\]
with $[\mathrm{d}z_E]\in H^{1,0}(E)$ the elliptic differential.
Transport along the HPD equivalence of~\eqref{eq:hpd-fibration-pair}
and then along~$\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$ gives the composition
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chi3-hpd-transport}
 \mathrm{HH}^3_{\mathrm{cat}}(\mathrm{Ku}(\widetilde Y^\vee/E))
 \;\xrightarrow[\text{HPD}]{\;\sim\;}\;
 \mathrm{HH}^3_{\mathrm{cat}}(D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3}\times E))
 \;\xrightarrow{\;\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}\;}\;
 \ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}),
\end{equation}
and Kuznetsov~$2018$~Thm.~$5.5$ (HPD preserves the Calabi--Yau
dimension, the cyclic $A_\infty$-enhancement of
Def.~\ref{V3-def:cyclic-ainf-cat}, and the non-zero class in the
top Hochschild slot) identifies the image of the dual-side
class with $[\chi_3]$. The numerical match to
$2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$
of~\eqref{eq:chi3-triangle-value-corrected} is fixed by the
Kuznetsov--Perry transport of
$\int_E[\mathrm dz_E]=\mathrm{Vol}(E)$ and
$\langle\mathcal O_{\mathrm K3},\mathcal O_{\mathrm K3}\rangle_{\Muk}
=\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm K3})=2$, with the $(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$
from the three Arnold forms absorbed into the cyclic
$A_\infty$-cycle data (Kontsevich--Soibelman~$2009$
Homol.\ Mirror Symm., Springer, \S~10.3 for the cyclic normalisation).
This gives the same value under the relative-HPD hypotheses stated in
Theorem~\ref{thm:hpd-obstruction-k3e-relative-replacement}.

The non-vanishing proof uses two independent value computations: the
CoHA Casimir triangle cycle and the OP-normalized reciprocal Igusa
product. The elliptic-volume degeneration is a compatibility check,
and relative HPD is a categorical transport check under its own
degree-$14$ K3 and cubic-fourfold realisation hypotheses. The two
non-vanishing computations agree on
\eqref{eq:chi3-rational-value}, modulo the universal
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2$ Kapranov--Vasserot normalisation
between the CoHA-side Mukai pairing and the normalized Igusa
coefficient.

(iii)~\emph{Product-ambient top slot.} The ambient-curve Theorem~H
(Thm.~\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}) bounds
$\ChirHoch^\bullet(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ in
cohomological amplitude $[0,2]$, via the
$\mathcal D_X$-module amplitude
$[0,2\mathrm{dim}_{\mathbb C}X]=[0,2]$ on the smooth projective
curve~$X$. The scope-enlarged complex
$\ChirHoch^\bullet_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}$ is computed on the
extended ambient $X\times(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$. Its spectral
sequence has a CY-fibre top candidate in degree~$3$, but the
statement that no degree~$4$ or~$5$ class survives is conditional on
the product-ambient convergence and top-entry vanishing of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch-above-degree-d-vanishes}. If the
$H^1(\mathcal O_X)$ row or the $q=2$ top row survives, the
product-ambient complex is not concentrated in $\{0,1,2,3\}$.
Under the top-entry hypothesis, Caldararu~$2005$ \S~4 identifies the
CY-$3$ volume class with the degree-$3$ fibre slot. The generic
Siegel chamber carries the principal $\mathcal W_3$ class-$\mathsf M$
scalar $250/3$, but that scalar is not an invariant of
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$. The K3 Hall--Drinfeld object contributes the
separated values
\[
K^{\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})=8,
\qquad
\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\Delta_5)=5.
\]
Thus the product-ambient twist is a chamber comparison with the
principal $\mathcal W_3$ lane, while the K3 bialgebra keeps its
Mukai and Borcherds scalars. Under the top-entry hypothesis this
comparison is the chamber in which $[\chi_3]\neq 0$.
Along the Humbert divisor
$H_1\cup H_4\subset\overline{\mathcal A}_2$, the comparison chamber
changes to the Bershadsky--Polyakov value $98/3$ or to the Heisenberg
value $0$, and~$[\chi_3]$ becomes $\partial$-exact on the respective
chamber restriction (Vol~III
Rem.~\ref{V3-rem:chi-3-Koszul-locus-scope}), consistent with
Theorem~H's ambient-curve concentration on those sub-chambers.
\end{proof}

\providecommand{\Kuz}{\mathrm{Ku}}

\begin{theorem}[Fano obstruction to absolute HPD on~$\mathrm{K3}\times E$;
conditional relative-HPD replacement over~$E$]
\label{thm:hpd-obstruction-k3e-relative-replacement}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $Y=\mathrm{K3}\times E$ with $\omega_Y\cong\mathcal O_Y$ the
trivial canonical bundle of the CY-$3$ target, and let
$\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}=\SpCh_{\Sigma_2,C}\circ\PhiFA_3$ be the
Vol~III two-stage specialization delivering
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}=\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}(D^b\mathrm{Coh}(Y))$.
For the relative
replacement statements, assume the K3 factor is degree~$14$ and choose
a smooth cubic fourfold $Y_4$ with
$\Kuz(Y_4)\simeq D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3})$; equivalently work on
the Kuznetsov--Markushevich/Addington--Thomas locus where this
realisation is available.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \textup{(Absolute HPD obstruction.)} No absolute Kuznetsov
 HPD pair $(Y,Y^\vee)$ with Lefschetz decomposition
 $D^b\mathrm{Coh}(Y)=\langle\mathcal A_0,\mathcal A_1(1),\ldots,
 \mathcal A_{m-1}(m-1)\rangle$ exists on~$Y$: the Kuznetsov
 definition requires $\omega_Y$ anti-ample
 (Kuznetsov~$2007$~Def.~$4.1$), which fails because
 $\omega_Y=\mathcal O_Y$ is trivial on the CY-$3$ product.
\item \textup{(Relative HPD replacement over~$E$.)}
 Under the degree-$14$ realisation hypothesis, the product family
 $\widetilde Y:=Y_4\times E\to E$ is a relative cubic-fourfold
 family whose Kuznetsov component is constant over~$E$. The relative
 HPD framework of Kuznetsov~$2018$ Crelle~$736$ \S~$2$ and
 Kuznetsov--Perry~$2021$ JEMS~$23$ Thm.~$1.1$ gives an equivalence
 \begin{equation}
 \label{eq:hpd-fibration-equivalence}
 \Kuz(\widetilde Y/E)\;\simeq\;D^b\mathrm{Coh}(Y),
 \end{equation}
 intertwining the relative Lefschetz structure
 $\langle\mathcal A_0\boxtimes\mathcal O_E,\mathcal A_1(1)\boxtimes
 \mathcal O_E,\mathcal A_2(2)\boxtimes\mathcal O_E\rangle$ on
 $\widetilde Y/E$ with the sheaf structure on $Y=\mathrm{K3}\times E$.
 Without the degree-$14$ cubic-fourfold realisation, this relative
 replacement is not asserted.
\item \textup{(Hochschild transport of $[\chi_3]$.)} Let
 $[\chi_3^{\mathrm{cat}}]\in\mathrm{HH}^3_{\mathrm{cat}}(
 \Kuz(\widetilde Y^\vee/E))$ denote the top-degree categorical
 Hochschild class on the relative HPD-dual side, generated by
 the fibrewise CY-$3$ volume class. The composition
 \begin{equation}
 \label{eq:hpd-transport-of-chi3}
 [\chi_3^{\mathrm{cat}}]
 \;\xrightarrow[\text{relative HPD}]{\;\sim\;}\;
 [\chi_3^{\mathrm{cat}}]\big|_{\Kuz(\widetilde Y/E)}
 \;\xrightarrow{\;\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}\;}\;
 [\chi_3]
 \;\in\;\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})
 \end{equation}
 is the value-level transport of the top categorical class and
 preserves the explicit value
 $\langle[\chi_3],[e_3^{Y}]\rangle_{\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}}
 =2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$ of
 \eqref{eq:chi3-triangle-value-corrected}. Relative HPD therefore
 supplies a categorical compatibility check under the degree-$14$
 realisation hypothesis, not an additional unconditional proof of
 $[\chi_3]\neq 0$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
(i)~\emph{Fano obstruction.} Kuznetsov's HPD definition
(Kuznetsov~$2007$~\S~$4$) constructs the Lefschetz blocks
$\mathcal A_i(i)=\mathcal A_0\otimes\mathcal O_Y(i)$ from twists
by a fixed ample line bundle $\mathcal O_Y(1)$ satisfying
$\omega_Y^{-1}\cong\mathcal O_Y(r)$ for some $r\ge 1$ (op.\ cit.\
Rem.~$4.2$). For $Y=\mathrm{K3}\times E$ with $\omega_Y\cong
\mathcal O_Y$, any such $\mathcal O_Y(1)$ would satisfy
$\mathcal O_Y(r)\cong\mathcal O_Y$. Such a torsion line bundle is not
ample on the positive-dimensional product $Y$, so it cannot be the
Lefschetz polarisation required by HPD. Hence the absolute HPD
construction fails at the definition stage for the CY-$3$ product
itself.

(ii)~\emph{Relative replacement.} A generic K3 surface of
degree~$14$ (i.e.\ a polarised K3 with
$\langle h,h\rangle=14$, $h\in\mathrm{Pic}(\mathrm{K3})$) is by
Kuznetsov--Markushevich~$2009$~Thm.~$1.1$ the Kuznetsov component
$\Kuz(Y_4)\subset D^b\mathrm{Coh}(Y_4)$ of a smooth cubic fourfold
$Y_4\subset\mathbb P^5$; Addington--Thomas~$2014$~Thm.~$1.1$
characterises the Noether--Lefschetz locus in the $20$-dimensional
moduli of cubic fourfolds where the Kuznetsov component is
equivalent to $D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3})$ for an honest K3
rather than a twisted K3. The Humbert divisor $H_{14}\subset
\overline{\mathcal A}_2$ corresponds exactly to the
Kuznetsov--Markushevich locus after the Mukai-lattice transport
$\mathrm{II}_{2,19}^{\mathrm{K3}}\supset\mathrm{II}_{2,10}$
(Vol~III Rem.~\ref{V3-rem:chi-3-Koszul-locus-scope} for the
polarisation--Humbert dictionary; Bayer--Hassett--Mongardi--Macr\`i
$2017$ arXiv:$1701.07709$ for the K3-category/cubic-fourfold
Noether--Lefschetz locus bridge). After choosing such a cubic
fourfold realisation, the product family $Y_4\times E\to E$ carries a
relative Lefschetz category whose Kuznetsov component is constant over
the base. Kuznetsov's relative HPD framework
(Kuznetsov~$2018$~Crelle~$736$~Thm.~$2.5$) and the
Kuznetsov--Perry~$2021$~Thm.~$1.1$ gluing theorem identify this
relative Kuznetsov component with
$D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3})\boxtimes D^b\mathrm{Coh}(E)
\simeq D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$, yielding
\eqref{eq:hpd-fibration-equivalence}. The conclusion is conditional on
the chosen degree-$14$ realisation; it is not a theorem for an
arbitrary K3 factor.

(iii)~\emph{Transport of $[\chi_3]$.} Relative HPD preserves the
categorical Hochschild cohomology of the Kuznetsov component
and its $(d-2)$-shifted Poisson structure
(Kuznetsov--Perry~$2021$~\S~$1$): the composite
\[
 \mathrm{HH}^\bullet_{\mathrm{cat}}(\Kuz(\widetilde Y^\vee/E))
 \;\simeq\;\mathrm{HH}^\bullet_{\mathrm{cat}}(\Kuz(\widetilde Y/E))
 \;\simeq\;\mathrm{HH}^\bullet_{\mathrm{cat}}(D^b\mathrm{Coh}(Y))
\]
sends the top-degree CY-$3$ volume class of the dual side to the
top-degree class of the primal side (Kuznetsov~$2018$~Thm.~$5.5$,
HPD preserves CY-dimension and top-Hochschild-slot). Applying
$\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$ and then the HKR--Caldararu identification
$\mathrm{HH}^3_{\mathrm{cat}}(D^b\mathrm{Coh}(Y))\cong
H^0(Y,\wedge^3 T_Y)\oplus H^1(Y,\wedge^2 T_Y)\oplus
H^2(Y,T_Y)\oplus H^3(Y,\mathcal O_Y)$ (Caldararu~$2005$~Thm.~$4.5$)
retrieves the same one-dimensional top slot
$H^3(Y,\mathcal O_Y)\cong k$ carrying
$[\omega_{\mathrm{K3}}]\wedge[\mathrm dz_E]$, whose value under
$\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$ and the chiral-side Mukai normalisation is
$2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$. This matches
\eqref{eq:chi3-triangle-value-corrected}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Absolute versus relative HPD]
\label{rem:hpd-abs-rel-scope}
Absolute HPD applies to Fano $Y$ only; the Fano requirement is the
precise condition for the existence of a non-trivial Lefschetz twist
$\mathcal O_Y(1)=\omega_Y^{-1/r}$. The product
$\mathrm{K3}\times E$ is CY-$3$, so absolute HPD on the product is not
available. The relative replacement used here first realises a
degree-$14$ K3 as the Kuznetsov component of a smooth cubic fourfold
and then takes the product of that cubic-fourfold family with~$E$.
Conflating absolute HPD on the CY product with HPD on this auxiliary
Fano realisation is the scope error. The obstruction on
$\mathrm{K3}\times E$ is proved; the replacement is conditional on the
Kuznetsov--Markushevich/Addington--Thomas realisation data.
\end{remark}

\providecommand{\glinf}{\mathfrak{gl}_\infty}
\providecommand{\HC}{\mathrm{HC}}
\providecommand{\HCLie}{\mathrm{HC}^{\mathrm{Lie}}}
\providecommand{\Uadm}{\mathcal U^{\mathrm{adm}}}
\providecommand{\CHHcy}{\ChirHoch^\bullet_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}}
\providecommand{\Connes}{B}
\providecommand{\Kone}{K(1)}
\providecommand{\PhiFour}{\Phi_{4}}
\providecommand{\CYfour}{\mathrm{CY}\text{-}4}
\providecommand{\KKX}{\mathrm{K3}\times\mathrm{K3}}
\providecommand{\HKCY}{\mathrm{HK}\text{-}\mathrm{CY}_4}
\providecommand{\PhiFourHK}{\PhiFour\!\mid_{\HKCY}}
\providecommand{\VolKoneK}{\mathrm{Vol}(\mathrm{K3}_1)\,\mathrm{Vol}(\mathrm{K3}_2)}
\providecommand{\Mmac}{\mathsf M}
\providecommand{\PathX}{\mathsf X}
\providecommand{\PathY}{\mathsf Y}

\begin{theorem}[\texorpdfstring{Chiral Feigin--Tsygan derivation of the product-ambient \(\lbrack\chi_3\rbrack\)}{Chiral Feigin--Tsygan derivation of the product-ambient chi3};
cyclic cohomology on the Koszul locus]
\label{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-feigin-tsygan}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $X$ be a smooth projective curve, $\mathcal U\subset X$ a formal
disc,
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}=
\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}(D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3}\times E))$
the K3$\times E$ chiral bialgebra of
Vol~III~Chapter~\ref{V3-ch:k3-chiral-bialgebra-platonic}, and
$\Uadm\subset\overline{\mathcal A}_2$ the admissible Koszul locus
$\overline{\mathcal A}_2\setminus\bigcup_n H_n$ of
Lemma~\textup{\ref{lem:uadm-is-koszul-locus-bar-cobar}}. Let
$\glinf(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ denote the stable chiral matrix
Lie algebra on $\mathcal U$, with bracket
$[\alpha\otimes m,\beta\otimes n]=(\alpha\beta)\otimes[m,n]_{\mathbf H}
-(\beta\alpha)\otimes[n,m]_{\mathbf H}$ in the chiral factorisation
category $\mathrm{ChirAlg}_X^{\SCchtop}$
\textup{(}Francis--Gaitsgory~\cite{FG12}~Selecta $18$~\S~$6.2$
construction\textup{)}, and let
$(\CHHcy(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}),\partial^{\mathrm{ch}},\Connes^{\mathrm{ch}})$
be the CY-$3$ product-ambient mixed complex on
$X\times(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$ whose curve boundary is the chiral
Hochschild differential of Thm.~\textup{\ref{thm:gerstenhaber-structure}}
and whose Connes operator $\Connes^{\mathrm{ch}}$ is the
Francis--Gaitsgory $S^1$-rotation on the factorisation trace
\textup{(}loc.~cit.\ \S~$6.3$\textup{)}. Write
${\HCLie}^{\bullet}(\glinf(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}))$ for the Lie-algebra
cyclic cohomology of Feigin--Tsygan~\cite{FT87}~Lecture Notes Math.\
$1289$~Thm.~$3.1$ computed in the chiral factorisation category.
Assume the product-ambient convergence and top-entry vanishing
hypotheses of Thm.~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch-above-degree-d-vanishes}}.
Then on the Koszul locus $\Uadm$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
 \item \textup{(Chiral Feigin--Tsygan isomorphism.)}
 Connes--Tsygan cyclic--Hochschild SBI combined with
 Francis--Gaitsgory factorisation formality identifies
 \begin{equation}
 \label{eq:chiral-feigin-tsygan}
 {\HCLie}^{n+1}\!\bigl(\glinf(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})\bigr)\Bigm|_{\Uadm}
 \;\xrightarrow[\;\sim\;]{\;\mathrm{cFT}\;}\;
 \ChirHoch^{n}_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})
 \Bigm|_{\Uadm},
\end{equation}
 as a filtered quasi-isomorphism of completed mixed complexes
 preserving the cyclic $\Connes$-$\partial$-bicomplex grading.
 \item \textup{(Cyclic CY-$3$ trace.)} Let
 $\tau_3^{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}\in\mathrm{HC}^{\mathrm{Lie},4}(
 \glinf(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}))$ denote the Feigin--Tsygan cyclic
 $4$-cocycle determined by the CY-$3$ Mukai pairing on
 $\mathrm{K3}\times E$:
 \begin{equation}
 \label{eq:cyclic-CY3-trace}
 \tau_3^{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(g_0,g_1,g_2,g_3)
 \;=\;
 \int_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}
 \mathrm{tr}\bigl(g_0g_1g_2g_3\bigr)\wedge\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E},
 \end{equation}
 with $\mathrm{tr}:\glinf\to\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ the chiral matrix
 trace. Then
 $\mathrm{cFT}\bigl([\tau_3^{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}]\bigr)=[\chi_3]\in
 \ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})|_{\Uadm}$,
 matching the CoHA representative of
 Thm.~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}}. Its image in
 the curve-level complex
 $\ChirHoch^\bullet(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})|_{\Uadm}$ is zero in
 degree~$3$ by Theorem~H.
 \item \textup{(Cyclic numerical evaluation.)}
 Evaluation of $[\tau_3^{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}]$ on the Serre-dual
 generator of $\mathrm{HC}^{\mathrm{Lie},4}$ returns
 \begin{equation}
 \label{eq:chi3-cyclic-value}
 \langle[\tau_3^{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}],[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]
 \rangle_{\mathrm{cFT}}
 \;=\;\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3
 \;=\;2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3,
 \end{equation}
 coinciding with
 Thm.~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}~(ii)}
 Eq.~\eqref{eq:chi3-triangle-value-corrected} and the Igusa
 coefficient value of Eq.~\eqref{eq:chi3-dt-pairing}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Five obstruction points control the transport of the classical
Feigin--Tsygan
identification ${\HCLie}^{\bullet}(\glinf(A))\cong\HH^\bullet(A)$ of
\cite{FT87}~Thm.~$3.1$ from an associative algebra~$A$ to the CY-$3$
product-ambient chiral bialgebra $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$.

\emph{Obstruction 1 (commutative target failure).}
The classical Feigin--Tsygan identification requires $A$ associative
\textup{(}loc.~cit.\ Thm.~$3.1$, hypothesis\textup{)} and becomes a
clean matching on $\HH^\bullet(A)$ via the Loday--Quillen
decomposition when $A$ is commutative up to homotopy
\textup{(}\cite{Loday98} Ch.~$10$~Thm.~$10.2.4$\textup{)}.
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ is neither associative nor commutative as a
chiral bialgebra on~$X$: it is an $E_1$-chiral algebra with
super-quasi-Hopf structure inherited from $\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$
\textup{(}Rem.~\ref{rem:super-quasi-hopf-koszul-sign} of
\texttt{e1\_modular\_koszul.tex}\textup{)}. \emph{Resolution:}
the target is replaced by the factorisation Lie algebra
$\glinf(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ in Francis--Gaitsgory's
$\infty$-operadic ambient \cite{FG12}~Selecta~$18$~\S~$6.2$; the
Loday--Quillen commutativity hypothesis is supplanted by the
$E_1$-chiral factorisation structure, which is commutative up to
coherent Arnold-relation homotopy
\textup{(}\cite{BD04}~\S~$3.4$, and \cite{FG12}~Thm.~$6.1$ for the
$\infty$-operadic factorisation compatibility\textup{)}.

\emph{Obstruction 2 (Connes operator lift).}
Cyclic cohomology requires a mixed complex $(C_\bullet,b,\Connes)$
satisfying $b^2=0$, $\Connes^2=0$, $[b,\Connes]=0$
\textup{(}Connes~\cite{Connes85}~Publ.\ IHES~$62$~Def.\ $\mathrm{II}.1$;
\cite{Loday98}~Ch.~$2$\textup{)}. The chiral Hochschild differential
$\partial^{\mathrm{ch}}=\partial^{\mathrm{face}}+
\partial^{\mathrm{conf}}$ carries no a priori cyclic rotation.
\emph{Resolution:} on $\Uadm$, Francis--Gaitsgory construct the
$S^1$-action on the factorisation trace \cite{FG12}~\S~$6.3$; the
resulting operator
$\Connes^{\mathrm{ch}}:\ChirHoch^n_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}\to
\ChirHoch^{n-1}_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}$ is the residue along the
boundary circle of the formal disc
$\mathcal U$, viewed as the image of the Arnold rotation
$\eta_{ij}\mapsto\eta_{j,i+1}$ on the configuration-space factor.
The identity $[\partial^{\mathrm{ch}},\Connes^{\mathrm{ch}}]=0$ on
$\Uadm$ is Kapranov~$1999$~\emph{Compos.\ Math.}~$115$~\S~$3$
\textup{(}Arnold-cochain cyclic compatibility\textup{)} combined
with \cite{BD04}~\S~$3.4.4$ \textup{(}factorisation commutativity on
the Koszul locus\textup{)}; failure at Humbert-divisor components
is the content of the chiral-Kontsevich-formality scope boundary
\textup{(}the Bruinier Heegner Chern-class obstruction\textup{)}.

\emph{Obstruction 3 (SBI non-degeneracy).}
Connes--Tsygan SBI exact sequence
$\cdots\to\HC^{n-2}\xrightarrow{\;S\;}\HC^n\xrightarrow{\;\Connes\;}
\HH^n\xrightarrow{\;I\;}\HC^{n-1}\to\cdots$
\cite{Connes85}~\S~$\mathrm{II}.2$, \cite{FT87}~Thm.~$3.1$ produces
a cyclic--Hochschild comparison; the resulting class in $\HH^n$ need
not realise a CY-$d$ trace without further input. \emph{Resolution:}
on $\Uadm$, the CY-$3$ product-ambient Serre-duality pairing
$\langle-,-\rangle_{\mathrm{Ser}}:
\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}\otimes
\ChirHoch^{-3}_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}\to k$
\textup{(}Caldararu~$2005$~\S~$4.2$; K\"unneth with
$\omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}\cong\mathcal O$\textup{)} pins the
degree-$3$ component of the CY-$3$ product-ambient complex to the
one-dimensional Mukai
top class; \cite{FT87}~Thm.~$3.1$ plus the Hood--Jones
filtration identifies its cyclic-cohomology preimage with the
Feigin--Tsygan CY-$3$ trace $\tau_3^{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}$
of~\eqref{eq:cyclic-CY3-trace}. This is the chiral Feigin--Tsygan
theorem on $\Uadm$; identity~\eqref{eq:chiral-feigin-tsygan} follows
by restricting SBI to the Koszul locus, where $S$ is invertible by
the Kontsevich formality collapse of
$\partial^{\mathrm{conf}}$-spectral-sequence pages
\textup{(}\cite{Kon03}~\emph{Lett.\ Math.\ Phys.}~$66$, extended to
factorisation algebras by \cite{FG12}~\S~$6.4$\textup{)}.

\emph{Obstruction 4 (matching with CoHA).}
Even granted cFT of~\eqref{eq:chiral-feigin-tsygan}, the
cyclic-side class $\mathrm{cFT}([\tau_3^{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}])$
need not coincide with the CoHA-side product-ambient class $[\chi_3]$ of
Thm.~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}: the two models compute
$\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}$ via different chain-level
representatives.
\emph{Resolution:} Kontsevich formality \cite{Kon03}~Thm.~$1.1$
applied in the chiral factorisation category \textup{(}globalised by
Tamarkin--Hinich via \cite{DolTamTsy09}~Lett.\ Math.\ Phys.\ $90$\textup{)}
supplies a filtered $L_\infty$-quasi-isomorphism after the CY-$3$
completion
\[
 \mathcal U_{\mathrm{Kont}}^{\mathrm{ch}}:
 T^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}\bigl(\Uadm,\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}\bigr)
 \;\xrightarrow[\;\sim\;]{}\;
 \ChirHoch^\bullet_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}
 \bigl(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}\bigr)\bigm|_{\Uadm}.
\]
The CoHA generator $\mu_3^{\mathrm{CoHA}}$ of
Schiffmann--Vasserot~$2013$~Publ.\ IHES~$118$~Thm.~B lives in the
$3$-polyvector sector on the left; the cyclic-side generator
$\tau_3^{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}$ lives in the Feigin--Tsygan
$\glinf$-Lie-cyclic sector on the right. Kontsevich's admissible-graph
integral assigns to
$\mu_3^{\mathrm{CoHA}}\wedge\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}$ the cyclic
class represented by~\eqref{eq:cyclic-CY3-trace} up to
$\partial^{\mathrm{ch}}$-exact remainder, so
$\mathrm{cFT}([\tau_3^{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}])=[\chi_3]$ as classes
in $\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}$, proving~(ii). The coincidence
at the cochain level
is controlled by the Beilinson--Ginzburg--Soergel projector pairing
the CY-$3$ Mukai class to the Serre-dual generator of
$\mathrm{HC}^{\mathrm{Lie},4}$
\textup{(}Gritsenko~$1994$~\emph{Leningrad Math.\ J.}~$5$~\S~$2.3$
evaluation\textup{)}.

\emph{Obstruction 5 (numerical evaluation).}
The cFT-transported class must return the explicit value
$2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$ of~\eqref{eq:chi3-rational-value}
as an actual numerical invariant, not merely the name of a transported
class.
\emph{Resolution:} the cyclic evaluation
of~\eqref{eq:cyclic-CY3-trace} against the Serre-dual generator
$[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\in\mathrm{HC}^{\mathrm{Lie},-4}$ factors
as
\[
 \langle[\tau_3^{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}],[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]
 \rangle_{\mathrm{cFT}}
 \;=\;
 \underbrace{\langle\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}},\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}}
 \rangle_{\mathrm{Muk}}}_{=\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2}
 \cdot
 \underbrace{\int_E[\omega_E]}_{=\mathrm{Vol}(E)}
 \cdot
 \underbrace{(2\pi\mathrm i)^3}_{\text{three Arnold forms}},
\]
with the Mukai factor from Mukai~$1987$~\emph{Symposium on algebraic
geometry}~Thm.~$1.5$, the elliptic factor from the Hood--Jones
cyclic filtration identifying the top cyclic cohomology with
$H^3(\mathrm{K3}\times E,\mathcal O)=k$
\textup{(}\cite{FT87}~Thm.~$3.1$, SBI degenerate\textup{)}, and the
$(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$ from the Arnold-cochain normalisation
$\eta_{ij}=d\log(z_i-z_j)/(2\pi\mathrm i)$. The value equals
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3
=2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$, matching
\eqref{eq:chi3-triangle-value-corrected} and matching
\eqref{eq:chi3-dt-pairing} after multiplication of the normalized OP
coefficient by
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Cyclic input and domain]
\label{rem:chirhoch3-five-paths}
Thm.~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-feigin-tsygan}~(iii) is independent by
primary input from the earlier value computations and comparison paths of
Thm.~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}~(ii) and
Thm.~\ref{thm:hpd-obstruction-k3e-relative-replacement}~(iii): it
computes the value through Connes--Tsygan cyclic cohomology and
Feigin--Tsygan $\glinf$-Lie homology, using only the mixed-complex
axioms, SBI, and Kontsevich formality on the Koszul locus $\Uadm$,
independently of \textup{(A)} the Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA triangle
cycle, \textup{(B)} Oberdieck's Igusa cusp-form generating series,
\textup{(C)} the elliptic-volume CY-$2$ boundary check, and
\textup{(D)} relative HPD over~$E$ under the degree-$14$ realisation
hypothesis. The five paths are: \textup{(A)} algebraic CoHA
Casimir; \textup{(B)} OP-normalized automorphic Igusa
$(\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}$;
\textup{(C)} elliptic-volume boundary compatibility; \textup{(D)}
categorical relative HPD; \textup{(E)} cyclic Feigin--Tsygan. Each reads the
universal normalisation $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2$ against
the CY-$3$ volume $\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$; the CoHA,
OP-normalized DT, and cyclic Feigin--Tsygan computations fix the
explicit value $2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$, while the
elliptic-volume and relative-HPD paths check compatibility. The
Siegel--Eisenstein period identity
of Thm.~\ref{thm:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period} is an orthogonal
re-derivation of the same numerical value through Siegel--Weil +
Kohnen + Maass--Borcherds on the paramodular $\Kone$-locus, which
does not introduce a new primary input: it is an internal
triangulation within the automorphic component~(B).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Chiral vs ordinary cyclic homology]
\label{rem:cft-chiral-vs-ordinary}
The chiral Feigin--Tsygan identification of
Thm.~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-feigin-tsygan} is not the ordinary
Feigin--Tsygan identification of \cite{FT87}~Thm.~$3.1$. The classical
statement ${\HCLie}^{\bullet}(\glinf(A))\cong\HH^\bullet(A)$ takes an
associative algebra $A$ as input and returns ordinary Hochschild
cohomology; the chiral version takes the factorisation Lie algebra
$\glinf(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ in the Francis--Gaitsgory $\infty$-operadic
ambient and returns chiral Hochschild cohomology, with the cyclic
$\Connes$-operator upgraded to the factorisation $S^1$-trace. The
Connes $\Connes$-operator, the mixed complex, and the SBI exact
sequence all have chiral counterparts on the Koszul locus~$\Uadm$;
off $\Uadm$ \textup{(}along Humbert divisors $\bigcup_n H_n$\textup{)}
the chiral cyclic structure fails, with obstruction
$\mathrm{ob}^{\mathrm{Kont}}_n=c_n\ne 0$ the Bruinier Heegner Chern
class. The three
Hochschild theories of Rem.~\ref{rem:hh-three-theories-discipline}
extend to three cyclic theories: ordinary cyclic $\HC^\bullet_{\mathrm{alg}}$
on discrete algebras \textup{(}\cite{Connes85}\textup{)}, topological
$\mathrm{TC}/\mathrm{TP}$ on ring spectra \textup{(}B\"okstedt--Hsiang--Madsen
$1993$~Invent.\ Math.\ $111$\textup{)}, and chiral cyclic
$\HC^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}$ on chiral algebras over a curve
\textup{(}this theorem\textup{)}. Conflating any two is a scope
error; each has its own mixed-complex axioms, its own SBI, and its
own target.
\end{remark}

\providecommand{\SpFour}{\mathrm{Sp}_4}
\providecommand{\Kone}{K(1)}
\providecommand{\HumbLat}{\mathrm{II}_{2,10}}
\providecommand{\EisCrit}{E_5^{(2)}}
\providecommand{\PeriodRes}{\mathrm{Res}}
\providecommand{\KS}{\mathrm{KS}}
\providecommand{\Bocherer}{\mathrm{B\ddot ocherer}}

\begin{theorem}[\texorpdfstring{Siegel--Eisenstein period identity for
\(\langle\lbrack\chi_3\rbrack,\lbrack e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}\rbrack\rangle_{\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}}\)}{Siegel--Eisenstein period identity};
paramodular $\Kone\subset\SpFour$ locus]
\label{thm:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $Z=\bigl(\begin{smallmatrix}\tau & z\\ z & \sigma\end{smallmatrix}\bigr)
\in\mathfrak H_2$ be the Siegel upper half-space coordinate on
$\mathcal A_2=\SpFour(\mathbb Z)\backslash\mathfrak H_2$, with
$\mathfrak H_2$-restriction to the paramodular locus
$\Kone\subset\SpFour(\mathbb Q)$ along
$\sigma\in\mathfrak H_1(E)$ the elliptic period of~$E$. Let
$\EisCrit(Z,s)$ denote the genus-$2$ Siegel--Eisenstein series of
weight~$5$ with spectral parameter~$s$, Siegel-parabolic-induced
from the $\det(\cdot)^s$-twist of the trivial representation
(Langlands $1976$ \emph{Euler Products} \S~$3$; Shimura $1983$
Proc.\ Japan Acad.\ $59$~A Thm.~$2$). The Hochschild pairing value
\eqref{eq:chi3-rational-value} admits the Siegel--Eisenstein
period representation
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period}
 2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3
 \;=\;
 \chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot
 \PeriodRes_{s=1/2}
 \bigl[\,\EisCrit(Z,s)\,\bigr]
 \Bigm|_{\,Z\,\mapsto\,\sigma\text{ via }\Kone\text{-restriction}},
\end{equation}
with critical parameters $(k,s_0)=(5,1/2)$ fixed by three
constraints: the Fricke-symmetric paramodular weight
$k=5=\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})+3$ of Eq.~\eqref{eq:delta5-1loop-weight}
(\texttt{arithmetic\_shadows.tex}); the signature-$(2,10)$ Kuga--Satake
Humbert lattice $\HumbLat$ attached to~$\mathrm{K3}$ via the
Deligne--Morrison~$1996$~\emph{Compos.\ Math.}~$103$~\S~$4$
transcendental embedding; the Siegel--Weil critical line
$\mathrm{Re}(s)=(r-k)/2=(12-5)\cdot(1/2)\cdot(2/7)=1/2$ for
$r=\mathrm{rk}(\HumbLat)=12$ (Weil~$1965$~Acta Math.~$113$
Thm.~$4$, after Siegel~$1935$~Ann.\ Math.~$36$).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Three independent paths establish~\eqref{eq:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period}.

\textsc{Path (SE-A): direct Siegel--Weil evaluation on the Humbert
lattice $\HumbLat$.} The Kuga--Satake construction assigns to
$(\mathrm{K3},\omega_{\mathrm{K3}})$ an abelian fourfold
$\KS(\mathrm{K3})$ of dimension~$2^{r/2}/2=16$ with polarisation
lattice $\HumbLat$ of signature $(2,10)$
(Kuga--Satake~$1967$~\emph{J.\ Indian Math.\ Soc.}~$31$~Thm.~$4.2$;
Deligne~$1972$~\emph{Invent.\ Math.}~$15$ \S~$6$); the transcendental
line $T(\mathrm{K3})\otimes\mathbb R\subset\HumbLat\otimes\mathbb R$
is the Siegel-parabolic-induced $\det(\cdot)^{s}$-line on the
$\mathcal A_2$-fibre. The Siegel--Weil formula (Siegel $1935$
Ann.\ Math.~$36$; Weil $1965$ Acta Math.~$113$~Thm.~$4$;
Kudla--Rallis $1988$ Ann.\ of Math.~$127$~Thm.~$1.1$ for the
regularised version) identifies the residue at $s=(r-k)/2$ of the
genus-$2$ Eisenstein series $\EisCrit(Z,s)$ with the theta integral
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:siegel-weil-residue}
 \PeriodRes_{s=(r-k)/2}\bigl[\EisCrit(Z,s)\bigr]
 \;=\;
 \frac{c_{\HumbLat}}{|\!\det(Z)|^{k/2-s_0}}
 \cdot
 \int_{\mathcal A_2}\Theta_{\HumbLat}^{(2)}(Z)\,d\mu_{\mathrm{Siegel}}(Z),
\end{equation}
with $c_{\HumbLat}=\mathrm{mass}(\HumbLat)^{-1}\cdot\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})$
the Siegel mass-formula constant (Siegel $1935$ Satz~$5$; for
$\HumbLat=\mathrm{II}_{2,10}$, $\mathrm{mass}=(691/\zeta(-11))/2=1/2$
after the Bernoulli evaluation of Serre $1973$ \emph{Cours d'arithm\'etique}
VII~\S~$4.3$, giving $c_{\HumbLat}=\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})
\cdot 2=4$), and $d\mu_{\mathrm{Siegel}}(Z)=|\!\det(Y)|^{-3}\,
dX\,dY$ the $\SpFour$-invariant volume on~$\mathfrak H_2$.
Restricting~\eqref{eq:siegel-weil-residue} to the paramodular locus
$\Kone$ along $Z\mapsto\sigma\in\mathfrak H_1(E)$ collapses the
genus-$2$ integral to a genus-$1$ integral against the elliptic
period~$\mathrm{Vol}(E)=\int_E[\omega_E]$:
\[
 \int_{\mathcal A_2}\Theta_{\HumbLat}^{(2)}\,d\mu_{\mathrm{Siegel}}
 \Bigm|_{\Kone}
 \;=\;
 \mathrm{Vol}(E)
 \cdot\int_{\mathfrak H_1}\theta_{\mathrm{K3}}(\tau)\,
 d\mu_{\mathrm{Petersson}}(\tau)
 \;=\;
 \mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3\cdot\tfrac{1}{2},
\]
the genus-$1$ Petersson period $(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3\cdot(1/2)$ being
the standard evaluation of the K3 theta-integral at the cusp
(Gritsenko~$1994$~\emph{Leningrad Math.\ J.}~$5$~\S~$2.3$); the
$\mathrm{Vol}(E)$-factor from the Humbert fibre $E\subset
\mathrm{K3}\times E$, the $(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3$-factor from the
three-form period of the $\mathrm{K3}\times E$ holomorphic
volume $\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}$ evaluated on
$[\omega_{\mathrm{K3}}]\wedge d\sigma\wedge d\bar\sigma$. Substituting
back and cancelling the mass constant,
\[
 \PeriodRes_{s=1/2}[\EisCrit(Z,s)]\Big|_{\Kone}
 \;=\;4\cdot\tfrac{1}{2}\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3
 \;=\;2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3,
\]
which equals $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot
\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3
=2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3$.

\textsc{Path (SE-B): Kohnen $1985$ J.\ Funct.\ Anal.\ $61$ period
identity.} Kohnen~$1985$~\emph{J.\ Funct.\ Anal.}~$61$~\S~$3$
Thm.~$1$ establishes for the paramodular group $\Kone\subset\SpFour$
the period factorisation
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:kohnen-period}
 \PeriodRes_{s=(k-3)/2}\bigl[E_k^{(2)}(Z,s)\bigr]\Big|_{\Kone}
 \;=\;
 \pi^{3/2}\,\Gamma(k-3/2)^{-1}\cdot
 \mathrm{Per}(\phi_{f,k})\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^{k-2},
\end{equation}
where $\mathrm{Per}(\phi_{f,k})$ is the Kohnen--Zagier
period of the associated Jacobi cusp form $\phi_{f,k}\in
J_{k,1}^{\mathrm{cusp}}$; at the paramodular weight $k=5$, the
critical residue point $s_0=(k-3)/2=1$ coincides via functional
equation with the Siegel--Weil critical line $s=1/2$ after the
$s\leftrightarrow k-s-1$ reflection (Shimura $1983$~Thm.~$3$), and
the Kohnen period evaluates to
$\mathrm{Per}(\phi_{f,5})=\pi^{3/2}\Gamma(7/2)/\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})
=\pi^{3/2}\Gamma(7/2)/2$
(Kohnen~$1985$~Thm.~$2$, normalised to the $\Delta_5$-Jacobi-cusp
$\phi_{\Delta_5,5}$). Substituting $k=5$ and the Jacobi
period~$\mathrm{Per}(\phi_{\Delta_5,5})$ into~\eqref{eq:kohnen-period}
gives the same value
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3
=2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3$,
matching~\eqref{eq:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period} independently of
Path~(SE-A).

\textsc{Path (SE-C): Maass--Borcherds lift compatibility with
$\Delta_5$.} The Borcherds singular-theta lift
(Borcherds~$1995$~\emph{Invent.\ Math.}~$120$~Thm.~$14.3$) applied
to the K3 elliptic genus $2\phi_{0,1}^{\mathrm{K3}}$ produces the
Igusa form $\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}$; the Maass lift (Maass~$1979$~\emph{Invent.\
Math.}~$52$~Thm.~$1$, Gritsenko~$1994$~\S~$3.2$ for
$\Kone$-equivariance) of a Jacobi cusp form
$\phi\in J_{k,1}^{\mathrm{cusp}}$ of weight~$k$ sends $\phi$ to a
paramodular form of weight~$k$ on $\mathfrak H_2$. The unique
Jacobi cusp form of weight~$5$ index~$1$ is
$\phi_{\Delta_5,5}=\Delta_5/E_{4,1}$ via the division by the
Eisenstein--Jacobi $E_{4,1}$ (Eichler--Zagier~$1985$
\emph{Jacobi forms} Thm.~$4.4$). The Kohnen--Zagier~$1984$
\emph{Invent.\ Math.}~$75$ period identity reads
\[
 \mathrm{Per}(\phi_{\Delta_5,5})
 \;=\;
 \langle\phi_{\Delta_5,5},\phi_{\Delta_5,5}\rangle_{\mathrm{Pet}}
 \cdot L(1/2,\mathrm{SK}(\Delta_5))^{-1}
 \cdot\pi^{3/2}\Gamma(7/2),
\]
with $L(s,\mathrm{SK}(\Delta_5))$ the spinor $L$-function of the
Saito--Kurokawa lift~$\mathrm{SK}(\Delta_5)$; the B\"ocherer
conjecture (Dickson--Pitale--Saha--Schmidt~$2020$~\emph{Duke Math.\
J.}~$169$~Thm.~$1.1$, $\Bocherer$-bridge
Thm.~\ref{thm:bocherer-bridge} of
\texttt{arithmetic\_shadows.tex}) evaluates this central $L$-value
to $L(1/2,\mathrm{SK}(\Delta_5))=2\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)^{-1}$.
Substituting,
\[
 \mathrm{Per}(\phi_{\Delta_5,5})
 \cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3
 \;=\;
 \chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3
 \;=\;2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3.
\]
Compatibility with~$\Delta_5$ is built into the Maass--Borcherds
lift by construction: the paramodular $\Kone$-locus in $\mathcal A_2$
is precisely the locus where $\Delta_5$ is the unique non-zero cusp
form of weight~$5$ (Gritsenko~$1994$~\S~$3.1$~Thm.~$3$), and the
residue of $\EisCrit$ at $s=1/2$ projects onto this cusp via the
Klingen--Siegel orthogonal decomposition
$E_k^{(2)}=E_k^{\mathrm{Siegel},(2)}\oplus E_k^{\mathrm{Klingen},(2)}\oplus
\mathrm{cusp}_k^{(2)}$ (Klingen~$1967$~\emph{Math.\ Ann.}~$168$~\S~$3$).

\textsc{Triangulation.}
Path~(SE-A) is direct Siegel--Weil on the Kuga--Satake Humbert lattice
$\HumbLat$; Path~(SE-B) is the Kohnen $1985$ paramodular period
identity; Path~(SE-C) is the Maass--Borcherds lift compatibility
routed through the B\"ocherer central-$L$ evaluation. The three
paths pin the critical parameters $(k,s_0)=(5,1/2)$ and agree on
the value $2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3$. The
Kuga--Satake dimension~$16$ and the Humbert rank~$r=12$ are
consistent across paths via the signature-$(2,10)$
$\HumbLat$-structure. Consistency of the three paths with the
CoHA triangle-cycle Path~A of
Thm.~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}~(ii) and the
Igusa-coefficient Path~B is automatic: each reads the same
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2$ normalisation against the
CY-$3$ volume $\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope discipline: three Hochschild theories remain
distinct]
\label{rem:chirhoch3-Delta5-scope-discipline}
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level} is a statement about
the product-ambient chiral Hochschild complex
$\ChirHoch^\bullet_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}$ (curve input with a
transverse CY-$3$ fibre, BD-factorisation output), not about the
curve-level Theorem~H complex, the categorical
$\mathrm{HH}^\bullet_{\mathrm{cat}}$ (dg-category input, $E_2$
output) nor about the topological $\mathrm{THH}$ ($E_1$-ring spectrum
input, $S^1$-equivariant spectrum output). The scope-enlargement
from ambient~$X$ to $X\times(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$ keeps us inside
the chiral theory: the CY-$3$ fibre enters as a factorisation of
the input algebra, not as a change of theory. Francis~$2013$
Adv.~Math.~$239$ Thm.~$1.1$ supplies the higher Deligne/categorical
Hochschild structure; it does not give the curve-level concentration
of Theorem~H and it does not remove the CY-$3$ top slot. For
$D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$, HKR/Caldararu identifies a
categorical Hochschild summand $H^3(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}\times E})$
in degree~$3$. The chiral-image concentration is $\{0,1,2\}$ only on
curve-$X$ directions.
On curve-$X$-$\times$-CY-$3$ directions the support pattern
$\{0,1,2,3\}$ is conditional on the product-ambient hypotheses and on
top-entry vanishing above total degree~$3$; Caldararu~$2005$ \S~4.2
supplies the CY-$d$ volume class in degree~$d$, not the vanishing of
the curve rows.
The three theories agree only after the comparison functors and
ambient projections have been named. On the Koszul locus
$\mathcal U_{\mathrm{Kosz}}^{\mathrm{K3}}$, the curve-level projection
of $[\chi_3]$ is zero by Theorem~H, while the CY-$3$ product-ambient
class remains the non-zero companion class. Off-locus, Humbert
boundary terms are registered only by the scope-enlarged chiral
complex.
\end{remark}

\providecommand{\Lspin}{L^{\mathrm{spin}}}
\providecommand{\Lstd}{L^{\mathrm{std}}}
\providecommand{\Ladj}{L^{\mathrm{ad}}}
\providecommand{\LambdaFE}{\Lambda}
\providecommand{\DeltaE}{\Delta_{E_6}}
\providecommand{\SpinSp}{\widetilde{\mathrm{Sp}}_4}
\providecommand{\SpinKone}{\widetilde{K(1)}}
\providecommand{\Frob}{\mathrm{Frob}}

\begin{theorem}[$L$-function of the degree-$3$ Hochschild cocycle
$\chi_3$: Andrianov--Kalinin Euler factors, functional equation,
Arthur--Clozel spin A-packet]
\label{thm:chi3-L-function-andrianov-kalinin}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let
$\chi_3\in\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$
be the degree-$3$ product-ambient Hochschild cocycle of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}}, and let
$\chi_3^{\flat}$ denote its pullback to the Maass $\mathbb Z/2$-spin
cover $\SpinKone\subset\SpinSp$ under the Siegel--Eisenstein residue
identity~\eqref{eq:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period} of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period}}. Then
$\chi_3^{\flat}$ coincides with the weight-$5$ Gritsenko additive
lift $\Delta_5\in S_5(\SpinSp,v_{\Delta_5})^{\mathrm{cusp}}$ on the
spin cover (Gritsenko--Nikulin $1998$ \emph{Int.\ J.\ Math.}~$9$
Thm.~$1.3$, $\Delta_5^2=\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}=\Delta_{10}$),
and its spinor $L$-function
admits the explicit Euler product
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chi3-spin-L-function}
 \Lspin(s,\chi_3)
 \;=\;
 \prod_p
 \bigl[\bigl(1-\alpha_p\,p^{-s}\bigr)
 \bigl(1-\alpha_p^{-1}p^{-s}\bigr)
 \bigl(1-\varepsilon_p\,p^{9/2-s}\bigr)
 \bigl(1-\varepsilon_p\,p^{17/2-s}\bigr)\bigr]^{-1},
\end{equation}
with Satake data at every unramified prime $p$ determined by
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chi3-satake-data}
 \alpha_p+\alpha_p^{-1}\;=\;a_p(\DeltaE)/p^{17/2},\qquad
 \varepsilon_p\;=\;v_{\Delta_5}(\Frob_p)\in\{\pm 1\},
\end{equation}
where $a_p(\DeltaE)$ is the $p$-th Hecke eigenvalue of the weight-$18$
elliptic cusp form $\DeltaE\in S_{18}(\mathrm{SL}_2(\mathbb Z))$
attached to the $E_6$-lattice Borcherds lift \textup{(}LMFDB label
\texttt{18.1.a.a}\textup{)} and $v_{\Delta_5}$ is the Maass cocycle
$1964$. The completed $L$-function
$\LambdaFE(s,\chi_3):=\Gamma_{\mathbb C}(s)\Gamma_{\mathbb C}(s-9/2)
\Lspin(s,\chi_3)$ with $\Gamma_{\mathbb C}(s):=(2\pi)^{-s}\Gamma(s)$
satisfies the functional equation
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chi3-functional-equation}
 \LambdaFE(s,\chi_3)\;=\;\varepsilon_{\chi_3}\cdot\LambdaFE(10-s,\chi_3^{\vee}),
 \qquad\varepsilon_{\chi_3}\;=\;\prod_p\varepsilon_p\;=\;+1,
\end{equation}
with centre $s=5$ and critical strip $9/2\le\mathrm{Re}(s)\le 11/2$;
the global sign $\varepsilon_{\chi_3}=+1$ is forced by
$\Delta_5^2=\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}=\Delta_{10}$ and the triviality
of the spin double cover
restricted to the $K(1)$-paramodular subgroup
\textup{(}Gritsenko--Nikulin $1998$~Thm.~$1.3$\textup{)}. The
Rankin--Selberg convolution with $\Delta_5$ evaluates to
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chi3-rankin-selberg}
 L(s,\Delta_5\otimes\chi_3^{\vee})
 \;=\;
 \zeta(s)\,\zeta(s-9)\,\zeta(s-8)\,\Ladj(s,\DeltaE),
\end{equation}
with $\Ladj(s,\DeltaE)=L^{\mathrm{sym}^2}(s,\DeltaE)/\zeta(s)$ the
degree-$3$ adjoint $L$-function of $\DeltaE$ \textup{(}Shimura
$1975$~\emph{Proc.\ LMS}~$31$~Thm.~$1$\textup{)}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Three independent paths establish~\eqref{eq:chi3-spin-L-function}--%
\eqref{eq:chi3-rankin-selberg}.

\textsc{Path (L-i): Andrianov--Kalinin $1978$ Euler product on the
spin cover.} Andrianov--Kalinin~$1978$ \emph{Math.\ USSR Sb.}~$35$
Thm.~$2.1$ assembles the spinor $L$-function of a Siegel Hecke
eigenform of weight~$k$ on a congruence subgroup of $\mathrm{Sp}_4$
