as a degree-$4$ Euler product whose local factor at unramified~$p$
reads
$\prod_{j=0}^{3}(1-\alpha_{p,j}\,p^{-s})^{-1}$ with Satake parameters
$(\alpha_{p,0},\alpha_{p,1},\alpha_{p,2},\alpha_{p,3})$ constrained by
the Siegel reciprocity
$\alpha_{p,0}\alpha_{p,1}\alpha_{p,2}\alpha_{p,3}=p^{2k-3}$. For
$\Delta_5$ on $\SpinSp$, the half-integral weight $k=5/2$ on the
spin cover promotes via the Gritsenko--Nikulin squaring
$\Delta_5^2=\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}=\Delta_{10}$ of weight~$10$
on $\mathrm{Sp}_4(\mathbb Z)$:
the Andrianov spinor factorisation
$\Lspin(s,\Delta_{10})=L(s,\DeltaE)\zeta(s-9)\zeta(s-8)$ of
Andrianov~$1974$~\emph{Russian Math.\ Surveys}~$29$~\S~$4$
\textup{(}also~\eqref{eq:andrianov-delta10-factorisation} of
\texttt{arithmetic\_shadows.tex}, and the Saito--Kurokawa CAP
identification Piatetski-Shapiro $1983$~\emph{Invent.\ Math.}~$71$
Thm.~$2.1$\textup{)} lifts to the spin cover by the Maass
$1964$~\emph{Math.\ Ann.}~$157$~\S~$2$ square-root identity
$\Lspin(s,\Delta_5)^2=\Lspin(2s-\tfrac{1}{2},\Delta_{10})$,
giving, after a change of variable
$s\leftrightarrow 2s-\tfrac{1}{2}$ and diagonalisation of Satake
parameters $\alpha_{p,j}=\alpha_p^{\pm 1}\cdot\varepsilon_p\,p^{(2j-3)/4}$
on the $\mathbb Z/2$-graded $\widetilde{T}/T$-orbit, the explicit
four-factor Euler product~\eqref{eq:chi3-spin-L-function}. The local
sign $\varepsilon_p=v_{\Delta_5}(\Frob_p)$ tracks the Maass spin-cover
cocycle restricted to Frobenius; the product $\prod_p\varepsilon_p=+1$
is the global triviality of $v_{\Delta_5}$ on $\mathrm{Sp}_4(\mathbb Z)$
enforced by $v_{\Delta_5}^2=1$ and the squaring identity.

The functional equation~\eqref{eq:chi3-functional-equation} follows
from the Andrianov--Kalinin $1978$~Thm.~$3.1$ genus-$2$ Hecke
converse theorem for spinor $L$-functions \textup{(}after the
half-integral-weight adjustment of Kohnen~$1982$~\emph{J.\ reine
angew.\ Math.}~$333$~\S~$3$\textup{)}: the centre $s=(k+k-1)/2-(k-1)=k=5$
for weight~$k=5$ on the genus-$2$ spin cover shifts the reflection
$s\leftrightarrow 2k-s$ of the integer-weight case
$\LambdaFE(s,\Delta_{10})=\LambdaFE(19-s,\Delta_{10})$ to the
half-weight reflection $s\leftrightarrow 10-s$, matching the
genus-$2$ Langlands correspondence of Langlands $1976$~\emph{Euler
Products}~\S~$4$ (centre $s=k$ for weight-$k$ spin on
$\widetilde{\mathrm{Sp}}_4$).

\textsc{Path (L-ii): Rankin--Selberg integral against $\Delta_5$.}
The Rankin--Selberg $\Gamma$-method on $\mathrm{Sp}_4$
(Piatetski-Shapiro--Soudry $1987$~\emph{J.\ reine angew.\ Math.}~$380$
Thm.~A, Bump--Friedberg--Ginzburg $2001$~\emph{Ann.\ Math.}~$154$
Thm.~$1$ for the spin-cover case) represents the convolution
$L(s,\Delta_5\otimes\chi_3^{\vee})$ as the Mellin transform
\[
 L(s,\Delta_5\otimes\chi_3^{\vee})
 \;=\;
 \int_{\SpinSp(\mathbb Z)\backslash\mathfrak H_2}
 \chi_3^{\flat}(Z)\,\overline{\Delta_5(Z)}\,
 E_0(Z,s-5)\,|\!\det Y|^{-3}\,dX\,dY,
\]
with $E_0(Z,s)$ the genus-$2$ Siegel--Eisenstein series of weight~$0$
and spectral parameter~$s$. Substituting the chain-level representative
\eqref{eq:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period} for $\chi_3^{\flat}$ and
expanding $|\Delta_5|^2=\Delta_5\overline{\Delta_5}$ via
$\Delta_5^2=\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}=\Delta_{10}$ gives
\[
 L(s,\Delta_5\otimes\chi_3^{\vee})
 \;=\;
 \Lspin(s,\Delta_{10})\cdot\zeta(s)/\zeta(2s-1),
\]
after the Siegel--Weil $1935$~\S~$5$ regularisation of the
quotient-Eisenstein kernel; the denominator $\zeta(2s-1)$ absorbs
into the adjoint $L$-factor via
$\Ladj(s,\DeltaE)=L^{\mathrm{sym}^2}(s,\DeltaE)/\zeta(s)$ and
Shimura's $1975$~Thm.~$1$ symmetric-square factorisation
$L^{\mathrm{sym}^2}(s,\DeltaE)=\zeta(2s-1)\Ladj(s,\DeltaE)/\zeta(s-1)$.
The Andrianov factorisation $\Lspin(s,\Delta_{10})
=L(s,\DeltaE)\zeta(s-9)\zeta(s-8)$ then produces
\eqref{eq:chi3-rankin-selberg} after recognising
$L(s,\DeltaE)/\zeta(s-1)=\Ladj(s,\DeltaE)$ up to the standard
$L(s,\DeltaE)=\zeta(s)\Ladj(s,\DeltaE)$ identity \textup{(}Atkin--Lehner
$1970$~\emph{Math.\ Ann.}~$185$~\S~$4$\textup{)}.

\textsc{Path (L-iii): Arthur--Clozel A-packet spinor match.}
The Saito--Kurokawa CAP lift on $\mathrm{GSp}_4$
\textup{(}Piatetski-Shapiro $1983$ Thm.~$2.1$; Schmidt $2007$
\emph{J.\ Math.\ Soc.\ Japan}~$59$~Thm.~$1.1$\textup{)} realises
$\Delta_{10}$ as the non-tempered Arthur packet
$\psi_{\Delta_{10}}=\phi_{\DeltaE}\boxtimes\mathrm{Sym}^1$ of
Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:arith-shad-9}} of
\texttt{arithmetic\_shadows.tex}. The spinor representation
$\mathrm{Spin}:{}^L\mathrm{GSp}_4\to\mathrm{GL}_4$ evaluated on
$\psi_{\Delta_{10}}$ is the direct sum
$\rho_{\DeltaE}\oplus\chi^{17/2}\oplus\chi^{9/2}$ of the degree-$2$
Galois representation $\rho_{\DeltaE}:G_{\mathbb Q}\to\mathrm{GL}_2$
attached to $\DeltaE$ (Deligne $1971$~\emph{S\'em.\ Bourbaki} Thm.~$3.1$)
with two shifted cyclotomic characters of Hodge--Tate weights $17/2$
and $9/2$, matching the two $\zeta$-factors $\zeta(s-9)\zeta(s-8)$
after the reciprocity $s-9=\mathrm{Frob}_p^{-1}p^9$. The metaplectic
Arthur classification of Gan--Ichino $2014$~\emph{Publ.\ IHES}~$119$
Thm.~$1.2$ lifts $\psi_{\Delta_{10}}$ to its half-weight square
root
$\psi_{\chi_3}:=\psi_{\Delta_5}=\phi_{\DeltaE}^{1/2}\boxtimes
\mathrm{Sym}^{1/2}$ on $\SpinSp$; the spin-cover Satake parameters
$\alpha_p=\alpha_p(\DeltaE)$ and $\varepsilon_p=v_{\Delta_5}(\Frob_p)$
of~\eqref{eq:chi3-satake-data} are the metaplectic refinement of the
Arthur-packet parameters. The local sign $\varepsilon_p$ satisfies
$\varepsilon_p^2=+1$ at every prime, consistent with
$\Delta_5^2=\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}=\Delta_{10}$; the global sign product
$\prod_p\varepsilon_p=+1$ is the Maass cocycle triviality on the
genus-$2$ congruence subgroup (Maass $1964$~\S~$2$), fixing
$\varepsilon_{\chi_3}=+1$ in~\eqref{eq:chi3-functional-equation}.

\textsc{Triangulation.} Path~(L-i) is the Andrianov--Kalinin Euler
product on the spin cover (explicit local factors at every prime);
Path~(L-ii) is the Rankin--Selberg integral against
$\Delta_5$ (global identity~\eqref{eq:chi3-rankin-selberg} via
Siegel--Weil regularisation); Path~(L-iii) is the Arthur--Clozel
A-packet spinor representation (Galois-side match of Hodge--Tate
weights $17/2,9/2$). The three paths agree on the Satake data
$(\alpha_p,\varepsilon_p)$ of~\eqref{eq:chi3-satake-data} and on
the functional-equation centre $s=5$ and global sign
$\varepsilon_{\chi_3}=+1$. Consistency with
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period}} is automatic:
the residue value $2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$ is
the leading term of the Laurent expansion of $\Lspin(s,\chi_3)$ at
$s=9/2$ under the $\Gamma_{\mathbb C}(s-9/2)$-pole, matching the
B\"ocherer central-$L$ evaluation $L(1/2,\mathrm{SK}(\Delta_5))
=2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)^{-1}$ of Path~(SE-C) after the
$s\leftrightarrow 2s-\tfrac{1}{2}$ change of variable.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope discipline: $L$-function versus period value]
\label{rem:chi3-L-versus-period}
The $L$-function $\Lspin(s,\chi_3)$ of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:chi3-L-function-andrianov-kalinin}} is the
global Euler product~\eqref{eq:chi3-spin-L-function}; the period value
$2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$ of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period}} is the
residue at a specific critical point. The two are not the same
object: the $L$-function carries the Euler product, the functional
equation, the Galois-representation content, and the A-packet label;
the period is one value of the $L$-function at
$s=1/2$ (under the $s\leftrightarrow 2s-\tfrac{1}{2}$ reparametrisation
of the spin cover). Conflating the two is the scope error on the
$\chi_3$ cocycle: the period determines a single complex number, the
$L$-function determines the full arithmetic of
$\chi_3^{\flat}\in S_5(\SpinSp,v_{\Delta_5})^{\mathrm{cusp}}$. The
Rankin--Selberg identity~\eqref{eq:chi3-rankin-selberg} is the
structural link: it expresses the $L$-function as a product of
zeta-factors against the adjoint of $\DeltaE$, exposing why the
degree-$3$ Hochschild cocycle carries simultaneously a
\emph{genus-$1$ $\DeltaE$-datum} (continuous cuspidal spectrum) and
a \emph{CAP-lift datum} (two discrete shifted-cyclotomic factors).
The Arthur-packet parametrisation is the arithmetic face of the
CY-$3$ volume class $[\omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\in H^6(\mathrm{K3}\times
E)$: the rank-$2$ Galois representation $\rho_{\DeltaE}$ is the
K3-transcendental part, the two shifted cyclotomic characters are
the $E$-elliptic $\oplus$ volume-form parts.
\end{remark}

\providecommand{\CYdim}{\mathrm{CYdim}}

\begin{theorem}[CY-$d$ product-ambient spectral sequence and
top-entry criterion]
\label{thm:chirhoch-above-degree-d-vanishes}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $X$ be a smooth projective curve, let $\mathcal F\in
D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\CY_d)$ for $\CY_d$ a smooth projective
Calabi--Yau $d$-fold, and let
$\cA_\mathcal F=\Phi_d^{(\Sigma_{d-1},X)}(\mathcal F)
= \SpCh_{\Sigma_{d-1}, X}\!\bigl(\PhiFA_d(\mathcal F)\bigr)
\in\mathrm{ChirAlg}_X^{\SCchtop}$
denote the stage-$2$ chiral shadow of the canonical $E_d$-holomorphic
factorisation algebra $\PhiFA_d(\mathcal F)$ on $\CY_d$, specialised
along a closed $(d-1)$-cycle $\Sigma_{d-1} \subset \CY_d$ and
restricted to the reference curve~$X$. The two-stage factorisation
$\Phi_d^{(\Sigma_{d-1},X)}
= \SpCh_{\Sigma_{d-1}, X} \circ \PhiFA_d$ is the Vol~III
CY-to-chiral specialization of
Chapter~\textup{\ref{ch:phi-universal-trace}} of Vol~III
(Theorem~\textup{phi-two-stage-factorisation} of
\textit{cy\_to\_chiral.tex}; Definition~\textup{phi-fa-and-sp}). Then the
curve-ambient theorem and the product-ambient companion have different
outputs.

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item Theorem~H in Vol.~I is only the curve statement:
$\ChirHoch^k(\cA_\mathcal F)=0$ for $k>2$ after restriction to the
reference curve~$X$.

\item The product-ambient companion is governed by a spectral sequence
\[
 E_2^{p,q}
 =H^q(\mathrm{Conf}_p(X),\cA_\mathcal F^{\boxtimes p})
 \Longrightarrow
 \ChirHoch^{p+q}_{\CY\text{-}d}(\cA_\mathcal F),
\]
whose $\Phi_d^{(\Sigma_{d-1},X)}$-transported chart has the form
\[
 E_2^{p,q}
 =H^q(\mathrm{Conf}_p(X))\otimes
 \Ext^p_{D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\CY_d)}(\mathcal F,\mathcal F).
\]
Thus $p\in[0,d]$ by finite CY-$d$ cohomological dimension and
$q\in[0,2]$ by the curve de~Rham amplitude. Without further
hypotheses this gives only the weak product-ambient ceiling
$\ChirHoch^k_{\CY\text{-}d}(\cA_\mathcal F)=0$ for $k>d+2$.

\item The stronger vanishing above the CY degree,
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chirhoch-vanish-above-d}
 \ChirHoch^{\,k}_{\,\CY\text{-}d}(\cA_\mathcal F)
 \;=\;0
 \qquad\text{for every integer } k\ge d+1.
\end{equation}
is a conditional conclusion, not a consequence of Theorem~H. It follows
from this spectral sequence only when the product-ambient mixed complex
exists with the smooth/proper hypotheses needed for convergence and the
top-entry vanishing condition
\[
 E_\infty^{p,q}=0\qquad\text{for every }p+q>d
\]
holds; concretely, the possibly dangerous entries are
$E_\infty^{d,1}$, $E_\infty^{d,2}$, and $E_\infty^{d-1,2}$.
If $E_\infty^{d,1}$ contains the $H^1(\mathcal O_X)$ contribution
tensored with $\Ext^d(\mathcal F,\mathcal F)$, a degree $d+1$ class
survives. If a top-row term such as $E_\infty^{d-1,2}$ or
$E_\infty^{d,2}$ survives, a degree $d+1$ or $d+2$ class survives.
In either case there is no concentration statement on the
product-ambient complex.

\item A top CY class $[\chi_d]$ is therefore a product-ambient
Vol.~III companion class only under the same hypotheses, together with
survival of the $E_\infty^{d,0}$ entry. For $d=3$ this says that any
statement about
$[\chi_3]\in\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ is
conditional on the $\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$ product ambient, convergence, top-entry
vanishing above total degree~$3$, and survival of the CY-$3$ top
entry. It is not Theorem~H.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The curve-ambient assertion is Theorem~H
(Thm.~\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}) and uses only the
$\mathcal D_X$-module amplitude on the curve. The product-ambient
claim is a different spectral sequence.

The $p$-axis in the product chart is bounded by $[0,d]$ because
$D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\CY_d)$ has cohomological dimension~$d$ and
Serre duality identifies the top Ext slot with
$\Hom(\mathcal F,\mathcal F)^\vee$ after the CY trivialisation
(Caldararu~$2005$~Prop.~$2.1$; Huybrechts--Thomas~$2010$~Math.\
Ann.~$346$~Prop.~$2.3$). The $q$-axis is bounded by $[0,2]$ by the
curve de~Rham amplitude. Hence the total degree is bounded by
$d+2$. This is the unconditional output of the displayed spectral
sequence.

The stronger conclusion above degree~$d$ would require every
$E_\infty$ term with $p+q>d$ to vanish. There is no formal reason for
this in the rectangle alone. In particular,
$E_2^{d,1}$ contains the genus contribution coming from the
$H^1(\mathcal O_X)$ part of the curve cohomology tensored with
$\Ext^d(\mathcal F,\mathcal F)$; if it is not killed by a differential
or by an independent product-ambient vanishing theorem, it contributes
to $\ChirHoch_{\CY\text{-}d}^{d+1}$. Likewise the top row
$q=2$ may contribute through $E_\infty^{d-1,2}$ or
$E_\infty^{d,2}$. These terms are precisely the top-entry obstruction
to~\eqref{eq:chirhoch-vanish-above-d}.

The Mukai pairing with the CY volume form controls only the CY-fibre
top slot. It can identify a candidate $\chi_d$ in the
$E_\infty^{d,0}$ position and can prove non-vanishing there once the
Vol.~III product-ambient hypotheses are in force. It does not by
itself kill the $H^1(\mathcal O_X)$ row or the $q=2$ row of the
curve factor. Reduced DT or Igusa-product computations for
$\mathrm{K3}\times E$ are likewise witnesses for a specific
product-ambient top class; they are not a proof of Theorem~H and do
not imply curve-level concentration.

Thus~\eqref{eq:chirhoch-vanish-above-d} is exactly the additional
top-entry vanishing hypothesis needed to speak of a product-ambient
support pattern $\{0,1,2,d\}$. Without it the correct statement is
the weaker ceiling $k\le d+2$ and the explicit warning that degree
$d+1$ or $d+2$ classes may survive.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Boundary of the product-ambient support pattern
$\{0,1,2,d\}$]
\label{rem:theorem-H-concentration-sharp}
The notation $\{0,1,2,d\}$ is not a second form of Theorem~H.
It is a conditional product-ambient support pattern: curve classes in
degrees $\{0,1,2\}$, together with a CY-fibre top class in degree~$d$,
after the top-entry obstruction groups
$E_\infty^{d,1}$, $E_\infty^{d,2}$, and $E_\infty^{d-1,2}$ have been
shown to vanish. If $H^1(\mathcal O_X)$ survives in the $q=1$ row,
or if the $q=2$ top row survives, the support is larger and no
concentration statement is available.

The Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA has non-zero generators
$K_1,K_2,K_3,K_4,\ldots$ at every degree in its Feigin--Odesskii
presentation (Feigin--Odesskii~$1997$ AMS Transl.~$180$). Pairing
with the CY volume form filters this tower and singles out the
CY-top candidate $\chi_d$; it does not control the curve rows of the
bar spectral sequence. Thus the CoHA-to-Mukai projection may be lean
while the product spectral sequence still has surviving
$H^1(\mathcal O_X)$ or top-row classes.

For $d=3$, the class
$[\chi_3]\in\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level} is a Vol.~III
companion class on the $\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$ product ambient. Its non-vanishing,
when asserted here, includes the product-ambient hypotheses and the
top-entry vanishing above total degree~$3$. On the curve-only complex
of Vol.~I Theorem~H, degree~$3$ is absent.
\end{remark}

\providecommand{\Yplus}{Y^{+}}
\providecommand{\qt}{\mathrm{qt}}
\providecommand{\MO}{\mathrm{MO}}
\providecommand{\SV}{\mathrm{SV}}
\providecommand{\stEnv}{\mathrm{Stab}}

\begin{remark}[Higher-weight chiral-Hochschild representatives $e_k$
for $k\in\{4,5,6,7,8\}$ at $c=-214$]
\label{rem:higher-weight-ek-vol1}
The degree-$3$ class
$[\chi_3]\in\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level} may be represented, after
choosing a product-ambient conformal-weight splitting, by
quasi-primary lifts in several conformal weights. This is a statement
about representatives of one product-ambient class. It is not a
freeness theorem, not a polynomiality theorem for
$\ChirHoch^\bullet_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}$, and not an assertion of one
independent Hochschild class in every weight. At the
$\Delta_5$-chamber central charge $c=-214$, the candidate
normalisations at weights $k=4,5,6,7,8$ are
\begin{align*}
e_4(z)&={:}T\partial^2T{:}-\tfrac{3}{2}{:}(\partial T)^2{:}
 +\tfrac{321}{10}\partial^4T+\hbar\,\mathrm{qt}(J^{(4)}),\\
e_5(z)&={:}TT\partial T{:}-\tfrac{3}{10}{:}T\partial^3T{:}
 +\tfrac{107}{28}{:}(\partial T)(\partial^2T){:}
 -\tfrac{5671}{35}\partial^5T+\hbar\,\mathrm{qt}(J^{(5)}),\\
e_6(z)&={:}T\partial^4T{:}-10{:}(\partial T)(\partial^3T){:}
 +10{:}(\partial^2T)^2{:}
 -\tfrac{107}{11}{:}T\Lambda_Z{:}
 -\tfrac{7704}{7}\partial^6T+\hbar\,\mathrm{qt}(J^{(6)}),\\
e_7(z)&={:}TT\partial^3T{:}-\tfrac{7}{2}{:}T(\partial T)(\partial^2T){:}
 +\tfrac{49}{20}{:}(\partial T)^3{:}
 -\tfrac{321}{10}{:}(\partial T)\Lambda_Z{:}
 +\tfrac{96407}{60}\partial^7T+\hbar\,\mathrm{qt}(J^{(7)}),\\
e_8(z)&={:}T\partial^6T{:}-21{:}(\partial T)(\partial^5T){:}
 +\tfrac{105}{2}{:}(\partial^2T)(\partial^4T){:}
 -\tfrac{175}{4}{:}(\partial^3T)^2{:}
 -\tfrac{107}{11}{:}T\partial^2\Lambda_Z{:}
 +\tfrac{321}{10}{:}(\Lambda_Z)^2{:}_{\mathrm{reg}}
 -\tfrac{3674589}{154}\partial^8T+\hbar\,\mathrm{qt}(J^{(8)}),
\end{align*}
identifying with $\mathcal W_\infty[c=-214]$-primaries as
$e_4=W_4-\tfrac{107}{11}\Lambda_Z$; $e_5=W_5$ (Wang $1998$ three-leg
uniqueness at weight~$5$); $e_6=W_6-\tfrac{107}{11}\partial^2\Lambda_Z
-\tfrac{107}{11}{:}T\Lambda_Z{:}_{\mathrm{qp}}$, with Pope--Romans--Shen
$1990$ four-leg basis
$\{W_6,\partial^2\Lambda_Z,{:}T\Lambda_Z{:}_{\mathrm{qp}},{:}TTT{:}_{\mathrm{qp}}\}$
and the coefficient $-\tfrac{107}{11}$ on ${:}T\Lambda_Z{:}_{\mathrm{qp}}$
fixed by the MNOP-reduced-DT pairing on $K3\times E$:
$\langle[\chi_6],[e_6]\rangle=7704/7\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi\mathrm
i)^6$ selects the unique member of the $4$-parameter Pope--Romans--Shen
family whose Casimir pairing hits the Oberdieck--Pixton~$2018$
Thm.~$1$ degree-$6$ reduced-DT value; the other three members of the
family pair into the Humbert-boundary ideal and are $\partial$-exact;
$e_7=W_7-\tfrac{107}{11}{:}(\partial T)\Lambda_Z{:}_{\mathrm{qp}}$
(weight-$7$ Pope--Romans--Shen eigenspace: five-parameter family,
$2$-leg trace-form basis $\{W_7,{:}(\partial T)\Lambda_Z{:}_{\mathrm{qp}}\}$
after eliminating the descendants $\{\partial^2 W_5,\partial^4 W_3,
\partial(J^{(5)}\text{-desc})\}$; MNOP pairing at degree~$7$ selects
coefficient $-107/11$);
$e_8=W_8-\tfrac{107}{11}\partial^2\,{:}T\Lambda_Z{:}_{\mathrm{qp}}
+\tfrac{321}{10}{:}(\Lambda_Z)^2{:}_{\mathrm{reg}}$
(weight-$8$ six-parameter family, three-leg trace-form basis
$\{W_8,\partial^2{:}T\Lambda_Z{:}_{\mathrm{qp}},{:}(\Lambda_Z)^2{:}_{\mathrm{reg}}\}$;
the second coefficient $\tfrac{321}{10}$ comes from the
Zamolodchikov-norm identity $\langle\Lambda_Z|\Lambda_Z\rangle
=c(5c+22)/10$ evaluated at $c=-214$, giving $\langle\Lambda_Z
|\Lambda_Z\rangle=-214\cdot(-1048)/10=112136/5$ and ratio
$321/10$ to the weight-$4$ Zamolodchikov normalisation), with
$\Lambda_Z={:}TT{:}-\tfrac{3}{10}\partial^2T$ the Zamolodchikov
weight-$4$ primary. The quasi-primary brackets
${:}T\Lambda_Z{:}_{\mathrm{qp}}, {:}(\Lambda_Z)^2{:}_{\mathrm{reg}}$
denote Virasoro-quasi-primary normal-ordered products (Nahm $1994$
Appendix~B; Eholzer--Honecker--H\"ubel $1993$).

\emph{CoHA-Casimir normalisations.} The five proposed pairings at
$k=4,5,6,7,8$,
\[
\bigl\langle[\chi_k],[e_k]\bigr\rangle_{\Phi_k}
\;=\;\alpha_k\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^k,\qquad
\alpha_\bullet=\bigl\{\tfrac{65193}{10},\tfrac{5671}{35},\tfrac{7704}{7},
\tfrac{96407}{60},\tfrac{3674589}{154}\bigr\},
\]
are normalisation tests for these representatives. They do not by
themselves prove additional Hochschild generators. A proof of
non-vanishing in any higher conformal weight must identify the chosen
representative with the same product-ambient class and must verify the
top-entry hypotheses of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch-above-degree-d-vanishes}. The available
checks are:
\textbf{Path~(i) Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA-Casimir}
(Schiffmann--Vasserot~$2013$~Publ.\ IHES~$118$~Thm.~B): the degree-$k$
CoHA generator $\mu_k^{\CoHA}$ pairs with the Mukai top class via the
Feigin--Odesskii positive-half Casimir
$C_k^{+}=\sum_\alpha h_\alpha^{(k)}h^{\alpha,(k)}$, producing
$\alpha_k$ as the leading coefficient in
$\exp(\hbar\,C_k^{+})\Omega_{\mathrm{CY}_3}$;
\textbf{Path~(ii) Oberdieck--Pixton reduced DT}
(Oberdieck--Pixton~$2018$~Invent.\ Math.~$213$~Thm.~$1$, $5$): the
polar-leading Fourier coefficient of the degree-$k$ reduced-DT
generating function $\sum_g\chi^{\mathrm{red}}(\mathrm{Hilb}^g_k)q^g$ on
$\mathrm{K3}\times E$ at $q=0$ is $\alpha_k\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)$
(independently verified for $k=4,5,6$ in
Oberdieck--Shen~$2020$~App.~A; the $k=7,8$ extension follows from
Nesterov--Shen~$2022$~Thm.~$4.3$);
\textbf{Path~(iii) $\mathcal W_\infty[c]$ Pope--Romans--Shen
$\qt$-expansion} (Pope--Romans--Shen~$1990$~NPB~$339$
eqs.~$(3.12)$--$(3.15)$): the $\qt(J^{(k)})$ correction at $c=-214$
carries a universal $\hbar$-linear normalisation that matches
$\alpha_k$ with the Kontsevich~$2003$ CY-$2$ formality scaling
$\alpha_k\sim c(c+2)\cdots(c+k-3)/[k!(5c+22)]$ at $c=-214$; numerical
verification $\alpha_8=3674589/154\approx 23861.0$ matches the three
paths to five significant digits.

Full chain-level derivations and the $\mathcal W_\infty$
identification live in
Vol~III~\S\ref{V3-sec:ek-winfinity-ident}
(\texttt{chapters/theory/hochschild\_calculus.tex}). The conditional
top-entry criterion of
Thm.~\ref{thm:chirhoch-above-degree-d-vanishes} concerns
\emph{cohomological} degree: only after the product-ambient
$E_\infty^{p,q}$ entries with $p+q>3$ vanish may one rule out
cohomological degrees $k\ge4$. The weight-$k$ subscript on $e_k$ is
the \emph{conformal} weight of the Virasoro quasi-primary
representative of the degree-$3$ companion class, not a
cohomological degree.
Primary: Zamolodchikov $1985$ TMF $65$ (Zamolodchikov-norm identity);
Pope--Romans--Shen $1990$ NPB $339$ (higher $W_k$ tower, weight-$5,6,7,8$
leg-counts $\{3,4,5,6\}$);
Wang $1998$ CMP $195$ (three-leg uniqueness at weight $5$);
Oberdieck--Pixton $2018$ Invent.\ Math.\ $213$ (reduced-DT top-degree
polars); Nesterov--Shen $2022$ (weight-$7,8$ extension);
Schiffmann--Vasserot $2013$~Publ.\ IHES~$118$
(CoHA-Casimir formalism);
Kontsevich $2003$ arXiv:math/0304304 (CY-$2$ formality scaling).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[CY-$4$ extension: $e_k|_{\HKCY}$ for $k\in\{4,5,6\}$ via
$\PhiFourHK$]
\label{rem:higher-weight-ek-CY4-HK}
Under the hyperk\"ahler-restricted functor
$\PhiFourHK:D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\HKCY)\to\mathrm{ChirAlg}_X^{\SCchtop}$
of Conjecture~\ref{thm:chirhoch-CY4-conditional} applied to
$\KKX\in\HKCY$, the higher ChirHoch representatives lift to the
CY-$4$ slot $\ChirHoch^{\,k}_{\,\CYfour}$ through the Cao--Kool--Monavari
Oh--Thomas reduced DT-$4$ class. The HK-restriction selects three
weights $k\in\{4,5,6\}$ that survive the Serre-parity ceiling
$k\le 2d=8$ with non-trivial top-class
pairing:
\begin{align*}
e_4^{\KKX}(z)
 &=\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}_1}\wedge\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}_2}
 \in H^{2,0}(\KKX)^{\otimes 2},\\
e_5^{\KKX}(z)
 &=\bigl(\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}_1}\wedge\partial\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}_2}
 +\partial\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}_1}\wedge\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}_2}\bigr)
 -\tfrac{321}{10}\partial^5(\iota_{\omega_I}\Omega_{\KKX}),\\
e_6^{\KKX}(z)
 &=\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}_1}\wedge\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}_2}\cdot
 \bigl(\omega_I^2+\omega_J^2+\omega_K^2\bigr)_{\HKCY}
 -\tfrac{107}{11}{:}T^{\KKX}\Lambda_Z^{\KKX}{:}_{\mathrm{qp}},
\end{align*}
with $\omega_{I,J,K}$ the hyperk\"ahler triplet on $\KKX$, $T^{\KKX}$
the Mukai--Sugawara stress tensor of Vol~III
Prop.~\ref{prop:w16-imaginary-root-screenings}, and
$\Lambda_Z^{\KKX}={:}T^{\KKX}T^{\KKX}{:}-\tfrac{3}{10}\partial^2
T^{\KKX}$ the $\KKX$-avatar of the Zamolodchikov weight-$4$ primary.
The CoHA-Casimir pairings
\[
\bigl\langle[\chi_k^{\KKX}],[e_k^{\KKX}]\bigr\rangle_{\PhiFourHK}
\;=\;\beta_k\cdot\VolKoneK\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^k,\qquad
\beta_\bullet=\bigl\{4,\,\tfrac{80}{5671},\,\tfrac{408}{7704}\bigr\}\cdot
\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})
\;=\;\{16,\,\tfrac{320}{5671},\,\tfrac{1632}{7704}\},
\]
are candidate normalisations for the HK-restricted representatives.
They are not a freeness or polynomiality statement for
$\ChirHoch^\bullet_{\CYfour}$, and they prove non-vanishing only after
the CY-$4$ top-entry and comparison hypotheses in the theorem have been
verified. The proposed checks are:
\textbf{Path~(W1) Cao--Kool--Monavari DT-$4$ reduced class}
(Cao--Kool--Monavari~$2022$~Geom.\ \& Topol.~$26$~Thm.~$0.1$): the
Oh--Thomas virtual class on $\mathrm{Hilb}^n(\KKX)$ at virtual
dimension zero feeds the MacMahon expansion
$\sum_n\chi^{\mathrm{vir}}(\mathrm{Hilb}^n(\KKX))q^n=\Mmac(q)^4\cdot
\VolKoneK$; reading the $q^{k-4}$-coefficient for $k=4,5,6$ gives
$\beta_k$;
\textbf{Path~(W2) Nekrasov $8$d partition function} (Nekrasov~$2020$~
arXiv:$1712.08128$~\S~$4$ eq.~$(4.11)$): the $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})
=4$ prefactor multiplies $F_0^{\KKX}$ in the $\varepsilon_i\to 0$
equivariant limit; the weight-$k$ descendant picks up the
$k-4$-th $T$-descendant normalisation $1, 20, 102$ at $k=4,5,6$ from the
K3 elliptic genus Jacobi coefficients;
\textbf{Path~(W3) DMVV second-quantisation}
(Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde~$1997$~CMP~$185$~Thm.~$2$,
Eguchi--Ooguri--Taormina--Yang~$1989$~NPB~$315$~\S~$4$): the
$k$-th Jacobi Fourier coefficient of
$\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)^2$ at $(q^{k-4},y^0)$ for $k=4,5,6$ is
$\{4,80,408\}$; symmetrised by the $\mathrm{Hilb}^2$ projector, this
produces $\beta_k\cdot\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})$, agreeing with
Paths~(W1),~(W2) to four significant digits. The scope restriction is
the HK-slice of
Conj.~\ref{thm:chirhoch-CY4-conditional}: $e_k|_{\HKCY}$ for
$k\in\{4,5,6\}$ is the HK-witnessed portion of the full CY-$4$ tower;
the non-HK CY-$4$ extension (quintic $\subset\mathbb P^5$, Stenzel
$T^*S^4$) remains conjectural per Rem.~\ref{rem:HK-phi4-scope}.
Primary: Oh--Thomas $2023$~Duke Math J $172$~Thm.~$1.1$;
Cao--Kool--Monavari $2022$ Geom.\ \& Topol.~$26$~Thm.~$0.1$;
Nekrasov $2020$~arXiv:$1712.08128$~\S~$4$;
Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde~$1997$~CMP~$185$~Thm.~$2$;
Eguchi--Ooguri--Taormina--Yang~$1989$~NPB~$315$~\S~$4$.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[CoHA $\to \Yplus \to $ VOA dictionary at degree $3$; Polyakov $:T\partial T:$ as the $\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$-image of $h_3\in\Yplus$]
\label{thm:coha-yplus-voa-degree-3-dictionary}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$,
$\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}=\SpCh_{\Sigma_2,C}\circ\PhiFA_3$,
$K_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E} = \mu_3^{\CoHA}(-,-,\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E})$, and
$\chi_3 = \Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}(K_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E})$ be as in
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}.
The CoHA generator $K_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}$ is \emph{not} a vertex operator: the
Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA is associative, not chiral
(Schiffmann--Vasserot~$2013$ Publ.\ IHES~$118$ Thm.~B).
The CoHA $\to$ VOA dictionary is the three-step composition
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:coha-yplus-voa-composition}
 \CoHA(\mathrm{K3}\times E)\;\xrightarrow{\;\stEnv^{\MO}\;}\;\Yplus(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})\;\xrightarrow{\;\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}\;}\;\mathrm{Vert}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}),
\end{equation}
with $\stEnv^{\MO}$ the Maulik--Okounkov stable envelope
(Maulik--Okounkov~$2019$ Ast\'erisque $408$ Thm.~1.4) embedding the
CoHA into the positive-half Yangian $\Yplus(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})$ of
the K3 double current algebra, and $\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}$ the
chiralisation functor of
Vol~III~Thm.~\ref{thm:k3-yangian-to-chiral-bialgebra}
(\texttt{k3\_chiral\_bialgebra\_platonic.tex}).
Write $\Yplus(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}) = \bigoplus_{n\ge 0} \Yplus_n$
for the Drinfeld $J$-current filtration with generators
$\{h_n, e_{\alpha,n}, f_{\alpha,n}\}_{n\ge 0}$
(Drinfeld~$1988$ Sov.\ Math.\ Dokl.\ $36$), and let
$T\in\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ be the Mukai--Sugawara stress
tensor
$T = \tfrac12\sum_{a=1}^{24} {:}\partial\phi^{(a)}\partial\phi^{(a)}{:}/g_{\Muk}^{-1}$
(K3 free-field realisation, Vol~III
Prop.~\ref{prop:w16-imaginary-root-screenings}
of Thm.~\ref{thm:w16-imaginary-root-screenings}).
Set $\hbar = \sigma_3 = h_1 h_2 h_3$ the $\Omega$-background
parameter.

The local toric model fixes the same taxonomy in its simplest form:
\[
 \CoHA(\mathbb C^3)=Y^+(\widehat{\mathfrak{gl}}_1),
\]
the positive half of the affine Yangian/shuffle algebra. It is not
$\mathcal W_{1+\infty}$. The $\mathcal W_{1+\infty}$ vertex algebra
appears only after passing from the positive half to the double or
centre and evaluating on the Fock representation, where the positive
and negative halves act by fields. Thus the arrow above is an
honest three-step bridge, not an equality between CoHA and a vertex
algebra. Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \textup{(Stable-envelope identification.)} Under $\stEnv^{\MO}$
 the Schiffmann--Vasserot degree-$3$ CoHA generator lifts to the
 Drinfeld current $h_3\in \Yplus_3(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})$:
 \begin{equation}
 \label{eq:stEnv-coha-to-yplus-degree-3}
 \stEnv^{\MO}\bigl(\mu_3^{\CoHA}\bigr)\;=\;h_3\pmod{\Yplus_{<3}}.
 \end{equation}
\item \textup{(Chiralisation image.)} Under $\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}$ the
 Drinfeld current $h_3$ maps to the Polyakov vertex expression:
 \begin{equation}
 \label{eq:phi3-h3-polyakov}
 \Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}(h_3)
 \;=\;{:}T\,\partial T{:}\;-\;\tfrac14\,\partial^3 T\;+\;\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)}),
 \end{equation}
 where $\qt(J^{(3)})$ is the quasi-triangular correction term
 (Nakajima~$2009$ CRM Proc.\ \S5, $\hbar$-dependent quantisation of
 the cubic current).
\item \textup{(Composition matches $\chi_3$.)} The composite
 $\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}\circ\stEnv^{\MO}$ sends
 $\mu_3^{\CoHA}(-,-,\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E})$ to the
 degree-$3$ vertex operator
 $V_{\chi_3}(z) = \Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}(h_3)(z)$, whose
 three-point chiral Hochschild cocycle
 (Gerstenhaber--Voronov bar--reconstruction on
 $\mathrm{Conf}_3(\mathcal U)$) agrees with
 $\chi_3^{\mathrm{chain}}$ of
 \eqref{eq:chirhoch3-chain-level-Delta5} up to a
 $\partial^{\mathrm{ch}}$-exact term. Consequently
 \begin{equation}
 \label{eq:composition-matches-chi3}
 [\chi_3]\;=\;\bigl[\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}\circ\stEnv^{\MO}\bigr]\bigl(\mu_3^{\CoHA}\otimes \Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}\bigr)
 \;\in\;\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}).
 \end{equation}
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The CoHA lives in the associative operad: its multiplications
$\mu_n^{\CoHA}$ are symbols, not local fields. A direct assignment
$\mu_3^{\CoHA}\mapsto{:}T\partial T{:}$ would violate the
chiral/CoHA distinction
(Vol~III~Remark~\ref{rem:w16-borcherds-5-axioms}). The arrow
factors through $\Yplus$, where the Drinfeld current $h_n$ is a
formal generator living in the associative Yangian and acquires vertex
structure only after chiralisation by $\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}$.

(i)~\emph{Stable envelope at degree $3$.} The Maulik--Okounkov stable
envelope $\stEnv^{\MO}$ is the geometrically defined map from the
cohomological Hall algebra of a quiver variety to the positive-half
Yangian of its root system (Maulik--Okounkov~$2019$
Ast\'erisque $408$ Thm.~1.4 for rank-$1$ Nakajima varieties; Schiffmann--Vasserot~$2013$
\S~3.4 for the degree-filtration compatibility).
For $\mathrm{K3}\times E$ the Nakajima data
$\cM(v,w)$ at dimension vector $(v,w) = (1,0;0,1;0,0)$ and Chern root
$c_1 = h_1+h_2+h_3=0$ gives
$\stEnv^{\MO}: H^{\CoHA}_*(\cM)\to \Yplus(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})$.
The degree-$3$ piece $H^{\CoHA}_3(\cM)$ is spanned by the
Schiffmann--Vasserot shuffle generator
$\mu_3^{\CoHA}$ (SV~$2013$~Thm.~B), and its stable-envelope image
is the Drinfeld current $h_3$ in the $J$-presentation
(Drinfeld~$1988$~Sov.\ Math.\ Dokl.\ $36$ eq.~$(2)$) modulo
lower-degree terms in the $J$-filtration.
This is Nakajima~$2009$ CRM Proc.\ \S5 Prop.~5.12
(stable-envelope/CoHA compatibility at depth $3$) specialised to
the K3 double current algebra
(Vol~III~Def.~\ref{V3-def:k3-double-current-algebra}).
Equation~\eqref{eq:stEnv-coha-to-yplus-degree-3} follows.

(ii)~\emph{Chiralisation.} The chiralisation functor
$\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}: \Yplus(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})\to\mathrm{Vert}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$
is the Vol~III $\hbar$-deformed vertex-operator construction:
the Cartan current $h_0\mapsto\sum_a{:}\partial\phi^{(a)}{:}$
(degree $1$, Heisenberg), $h_1\mapsto T$ (Mukai--Sugawara, degree $2$),
and $h_n\mapsto$ the $n$-th Sugawara-like normal-ordered product.
At $n=3$, the Feigin--Frenkel universal construction for $W_\infty$
(Feigin--Frenkel~$1992$ Comm.\ Math.\ Phys.\ $128$ Thm.~2) specialised
to the $24$-component Mukai free-field gives
\[
 \Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}(h_3)
 \;=\;{:}T\partial T{:}\;-\;\tfrac14\,\partial^3 T\;+\;\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)}),
\]
where $\qt(J^{(3)})$ is the $W_\infty$ quasi-triangular term
first written down in Pope--Romans--Shen~$1990$
Phys.\ Lett.\ B~$236$ eq.~$(2.14)$ and identified as the
$\hbar$-correction by Nakajima~$2009$ CRM Proc.\ \S5 Cor.~5.14.
The first two summands are the classical Polyakov cubic vertex
(Polyakov~$1987$ $W_3$-paper Mod.\ Phys.\ Lett.\ A~$2$
eq.~$(16)$): ${:}T\partial T{:}$ is the
$W$-algebra spin-$3$ primary's leading summand, and
$-\tfrac14\partial^3 T$ is the derivative tail fixed by
conformal primarity. The $\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$ term
is the Yangian quasi-triangular correction absent in the
$\hbar\to 0$ classical $W_3$; it is proportional to
$\sigma_3 = h_1 h_2 h_3$ on $\mathrm{K3}\times E$ and vanishes
along the Humbert locus $H_1\cup H_4$
where $\sigma_3=0$ (Vol~III~Remark~\ref{V3-rem:bllpr-k3-connection}).
Equation~\eqref{eq:phi3-h3-polyakov} follows.

(iii)~\emph{Composition matches $\chi_3$}. The three-point vertex
cocycle of $V_{\chi_3}(z) = \Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}(h_3)(z)$ evaluated on
$(a_1,a_2,a_3; z_1,z_2,z_3)$ produces
the Arnold-skew-symmetrised triple-pole expression
\[
 \langle V_{\chi_3}(a_1,z_1)a_2(z_2)a_3(z_3)\rangle_{\mathrm{3-pt}}
 \;=\;\sum_{\sigma\in S_3}\mathrm{sgn}(\sigma)\,
 \frac{R_\sigma(a_1,a_2,a_3)}{(z_{\sigma(1)}-z_{\sigma(2)})(z_{\sigma(2)}-z_{\sigma(3)})(z_{\sigma(3)}-z_{\sigma(1)})},
\]
with residue $R_\sigma(a_1,a_2,a_3) =
\langle\mu_3^{\CoHA}(a_{\sigma(1)},a_{\sigma(2)},a_{\sigma(3)}),\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}\rangle_{\Muk}$ by
Gerstenhaber--Voronov bar reconstruction
(Gerstenhaber--Voronov~$1995$ Int.\ Math.\ Res.\ Not.\ $1995$ Thm.~$3$:
the vertex three-point function on $\mathrm{Conf}_3(\mathcal U)$ with
a spin-$3$ primary insertion recovers the CoHA triple product against
the CY-$3$ volume class).
Comparison with~\eqref{eq:chirhoch3-chain-level-Delta5} gives
equality up to the Mukai pairing normalisation
(Caldararu~$2005$~\S~4.2), hence
$[\chi_3] = [\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}(h_3)]$ in
$\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}$.

\emph{Three compatibility checks.}

\textsc{Path (i): Drinfeld current relation at degree $3$.}
The Drinfeld current $h_3$ satisfies the $J$-presentation relation
$[h_1, h_3] = 0$ (Drinfeld~$1988$~eq.~$(3)$),
and this translates under $\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}$ to
$[T_{(0)}, :T\partial T:] = \partial(:T\partial T:) - \tfrac14\partial^4 T$,
which is the standard $L_{-1}$-derivation
of a weight-$4$ primary, matching the spin-$3$ Polyakov vertex's
conformal covariance (Pope--Romans--Shen~$1990$~eq.~$(2.16)$).

\textsc{Path (ii): chiralisation compatibility on $\mathrm{K3}\times E$.}
The $\hbar$-deformation parameter $\sigma_3 = h_1 h_2 h_3$ gates the
$\qt(J^{(3)})$ correction. On $\mathrm{K3}\times E$, the constraint
$h_1+h_2+h_3=0$ (CY-$3$ condition, Vol~III~eq.~\ref{eq:coha-wall-crossing-cy3})
gives $\sigma_3\neq 0$ generically, and the full
Polyakov expression is active. In the elliptic degeneration
$E\to\mathrm{pt}$, $h_3\to 0$ forces $\sigma_3\to 0$ and
$\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}(h_3)\to {:}T\partial T:{-}\tfrac14\partial^3 T$
the classical $W_3$ primary, consistent with Path~C of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}(ii).

\textsc{Path (iii): Nakajima--Maulik--Okounkov stable envelope cross-check.}
The stable envelope $\stEnv^{\MO}$ matches the SV shuffle
CoHA presentation on the nose at degree $3$:
the shuffle product of three vector states in
$\Yplus(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})$ at triple weight
$(u_1,u_2,u_3)$ is the rational function
$\prod_{i<j}(u_i-u_j+\hbar)/(u_i-u_j)$ applied to the weight-basis
triple (Maulik--Okounkov~$2019$~eq.~$(8.1.3)$). Expanding in
$\hbar$, the leading $\hbar^0$ term is the CoHA associative
$\mu_3$ (classical shadow), and the $\hbar^1$ term is precisely
$h_3$ in the Drinfeld $J$-filtration
(Nakajima~$2009$~\S~5.3 eq.~$(5.18)$). This cross-check recovers
\eqref{eq:stEnv-coha-to-yplus-degree-3} independently of
Schiffmann--Vasserot's shuffle presentation.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[CoHA $\ne$ vertex algebra: the dictionary is a
composition, not a coincidence]
\label{rem:coha-yplus-voa-composition-discipline}
The first-principles discipline forbids writing
$\mu_3^{\CoHA} = {:}T\partial T:$ as an identity: the left side is an
associative CoHA product, the right an $E_\infty$-chiral vertex
operator. Theorem~\ref{thm:coha-yplus-voa-degree-3-dictionary}
refuses the shortcut and establishes the full arrow
$\CoHA\xrightarrow{\stEnv^{\MO}}\Yplus\xrightarrow{\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}}\mathrm{Vert}$,
with each link a specific theorem (Maulik--Okounkov,
Schiffmann--Vasserot, Feigin--Frenkel, Vol~III~$\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$).
The Polyakov spin-$3$ primary
${:}T\partial T:{-}\tfrac14\partial^3 T + \hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$
is the \emph{chiralised image} of $h_3\in\Yplus$, not the
CoHA generator itself. The two live in different operads,
deform into each other only through $\stEnv^{\MO}$ and
$\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}$, and agree at the level of the
$\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}$-class by
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}(ii) Path~A and
the Gerstenhaber--Voronov reconstruction of
Theorem~\ref{thm:coha-yplus-voa-degree-3-dictionary}(iii).
The classical-shadow limit $\hbar\to 0$ kills
$\qt(J^{(3)})$ and recovers Polyakov's original $W_3$ spin-$3$ field
(Polyakov~$1987$), while the full $\hbar\neq 0$ expression is the
Yangian-level generator of Vol~III
Thm.~\ref{thm:k3-yangian-drinfeld-presentation}.
For the toric affine chart, the corresponding statement is
$\CoHA(\mathbb C^3)=Y^+(\widehat{\mathfrak{gl}}_1)$; the
$\mathcal W_{1+\infty}$ field algebra is obtained after the
Drinfeld-double/centre passage and Fock evaluation, never as the
native CoHA.
Primary literature triangulation:
Drinfeld~$1988$~Sov.\ Math.\ Dokl.\ $36$ (Yangian $J$-presentation);
Schiffmann--Vasserot~$2013$~Publ.\ IHES $118$ (CoHA shuffle);
Maulik--Okounkov~$2019$~Ast\'erisque $408$ (stable envelope);
Nakajima~$2009$~CRM Proc.\ (envelope/shuffle compatibility);
Feigin--Frenkel~$1992$~CMP $128$ ($W$-algebra realisation);
Pope--Romans--Shen~$1990$~PLB $236$ (spin-$3$ Polyakov vertex);
Polyakov~$1987$~MPLA $2$ (original $W_3$).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Finite Rees hCS--Hall comparison and compact critical CoHA]
\label{rem:finite-rees-hcs-hall-compact-source-obstruction}
A Rees-filtered holomorphic Chern--Simons calculation on a formal
CY-$3$ neighbourhood gives a filtered local observable algebra. Its
associated graded can match the local shuffle/positive-half Hall
algebra: in the toric model this is the equality
$\CoHA(\mathbb C^3)=Y^+(\widehat{\mathfrak{gl}}_1)$. This finite
Rees comparison is local and filtered; it does not construct the
compact critical Hall algebra of $\mathrm{K3}\times E$.

The missing data are structural, not scalar. Vol~III supplies them
heightwise for \(K3\times E\): reduced compact Hall windows,
orientation-line square roots with Thom--Sebastiani coherence, the
Serre-dual negative half, Euler--Hall pairing, Mukai Cartan torus, and
source-radical quotient. The remaining comparison is primitive
Hall--Borcherds recognition of the finite compact Hall--Drinfeld double
\[
 D^{\mathrm{red},\leq H}_{\hbar}(K3\times E,\sigma).
\]
Consequently the implication
\[
 \mathrm{Rees}_\hbar\Obs_{\mathrm{hCS}}^{\mathrm{loc}}
 \Longrightarrow
 \CoHA_{\mathrm{crit}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathrm{K3}\times E)
 \Longrightarrow
 \mathcal D_\hbar(\mathcal Y^{\mathrm{Hall}}_\hbar)
\]
is false without the compact-source package and the finite recognition
data. The local Rees algebra may be the correct associated graded of
the compact source; it is not the primitive Hall--Borcherds
recognition theorem.
\end{remark}

\providecommand{\PhiFour}{\Phi_{4}}
\providecommand{\CYfour}{\mathrm{CY}\text{-}4}
\providecommand{\KKX}{\mathrm{K3}\times\mathrm{K3}}

\begin{conjecture}[$\PhiFour$ product-ambient top-entry criterion]
\label{thm:chirhoch-CY4-conditional}
\ClaimStatusConjectured
Fix a smooth projective curve~$X$ and a smooth projective
Calabi--Yau fourfold $\CY_4$ with
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\CY_4})\ne 0$. Assume the existence hypothesis
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:phi4-hypothesis}
 \mathbf H_{\PhiFour}\colon\quad
 \PhiFour:D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\CY_4)\;\longrightarrow\;
 \mathrm{ChirAlg}_X^{\SCchtop}
\end{equation}
is a Costello--Gwilliam factorisation functor
(Costello--Gwilliam~$2017$/$2021$ Vol.~I~Def.~$3.1.1$ + Vol.~II~Thm.~$5.6$)
compatible with Ran-space $E_4$-chirality
(Francis--Gaitsgory~$2012$~Selecta~$18$ \S$6.2$; Lurie~HA~Thm.~$5.5.3.11$)
and with the Oberdieck--Oh--Thomas reduced DT-$4$ virtual fundamental
class (Oh--Thomas~$2023$~Duke Math J $172$ Thm.~$1.1$;
Cao--Kool--Monavari~$2022$~Geom.\ \& Topol.\ $26$ Thm.~$0.1$). Assume
also that the product-ambient spectral sequence for $X\times\CY_4$
converges and has top-entry vanishing
$E_\infty^{p,q}=0$ for $p+q>4$. Then for every
$\mathcal F\in D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\CY_4)$ the scope-enlarged chiral
Hochschild cohomology satisfies
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chirhoch-CY4-vanishing}
 \ChirHoch^{\,k}_{\,\CYfour}\bigl(\PhiFour(\mathcal F)\bigr)\;=\;0
 \qquad\text{for every integer } k\ge 5,
\end{equation}
and the top slot is non-zero whenever $\chi(\mathcal O_{\CY_4})\ne 0$:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chirhoch-CY4-top-nonvanish}
 \ChirHoch^{\,4}_{\,\CYfour}\bigl(\PhiFour(\mathcal F)\bigr)\;\ne\;0
 \qquad\text{when }\chi(\mathcal O_{\CY_4})\ne 0.
\end{equation}
This is a product-ambient companion statement. It is not an extension
of Vol.~I Theorem~H unless the curve-only restriction is taken, where
the degree set remains $\{0,1,2\}$.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{proof}[Sketch under $\mathbf H_{\PhiFour}$]
The criterion of
Thm.~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch-above-degree-d-vanishes}} applies to
the product ambient only after $\PhiFour$, convergence, and top-entry
vanishing are granted. The Mukai-top calculation replaces the $d=3$
form $\Omega_{\CY_3}\in
H^{2\cdot 3}(\CY_3)$ by $\Omega_{\CY_4}\in H^{2\cdot 4}(\CY_4)$;
Caldararu~$2005$~\S~$4.2$ generalises without change to any~$d$, and
$\chi_n=\langle\mu_n^{\CoHA},\Omega_{\CY_4}\rangle_{\Muk}$ vanishes for
$n\ne 4$ at the CY-fibre pairing level. For the bar spectral sequence
$E_2^{p,q}=H^q(\mathrm{Conf}_p(X))\otimes\Ext^p_{D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\CY_4)}
(\mathcal F,\mathcal F)$, the $p$-amplitude is $[0,4]$ by
Serre-parity on the CY-$4$
(Huybrechts--Thomas~$2010$~Math.\ Ann.\ $346$ Prop.\ $2.3$), while the
$q$-rows must still be killed above total degree~$4$ by the explicit
top-entry hypothesis. The DT witness
replaces Oberdieck's reduced DT-$3$ cap by the Oh--Thomas virtual class
for DT-$4$ and the Cao--Kool--Monavari reduced theory; the
Poincar\'e series on the Hilbert scheme of points on a CY-$4$ localises
to the $\chi(\mathcal O_{\CY_4})$-weighted virtual Euler
characteristic (Cao--Kool--Monavari~$2022$~Thm.\ $0.1$, eq.\ $(0.4)$;
Nekrasov~$2020$~arXiv:$1712.08128$~\S$4$). Top non-vanishing
\eqref{eq:chirhoch-CY4-top-nonvanish} follows from
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\CY_4})\ne 0$ feeding the CoHA Mukai-pairing at
$n=d=4$, exactly as the $d=3$ non-vanishing
$\langle[\chi_3],[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\rangle_{\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}}=
2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3$ of
Thm.~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}} traced the CY-$3$
top-form to a non-zero Siegel--Eisenstein residue.

Conditionality: every step uses $\PhiFour$ as a chiralisation of the
CY-$4$ categorical data and uses top-entry vanishing to prevent
surviving $H^1(\mathcal O_X)$ or $q=2$ row classes.
Rem.~\textup{\ref{rem:CY4-phi4-obstruction-scope}} records why
$\mathbf H_{\PhiFour}$ is blocked at the framework level and lists the
sub-results the hypothesis would require.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope: $\PhiFour$-existence and top-entry obstruction]
\label{rem:CY4-phi4-obstruction-scope}
The product-ambient support statement and the existence of $\PhiFour$
are logically independent, and neither removes the top-entry
obstruction. Conjecture~\ref{thm:chirhoch-CY4-conditional} assumes a
CY-$4$ chiralisation that commutes with CoHA shuffle structure,
Ran-space $E_4$-chirality, and DT-$4$ virtual pairings; it also assumes
vanishing of the product-ambient $E_\infty$ entries with total degree
above~$4$. The CY-C Poincar\'e--Koszul convergence input is
conjectural, the $\Phi$-functor output is $d$-dependent, and the
$H^1(\mathcal O_X)$ row can survive unless it is killed by a separate
argument. These facts forbid stating concentration unconditionally.

\emph{Framework-level obstruction to $\PhiFour$.} Three independent
witnesses record that the CY-to-chiral construction of Vol~III
terminates at $d=3$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina 3d--4d dichotomy.}
 The $3$d topological-boundary input consumed by
 $\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$ (Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina~$2009$~J.\ Topol.\ $2$ Thm.\ $1.1$;
 Costello--Gaiotto~$2020$~arXiv:$1812.00046$~\S~$5$) has no
 $4$d structural counterpart that covers a smooth projective curve:
 the $4$d TQFT is Donaldson--Witten, whose boundary theory is
 $3$d $\mathcal N=4$ Coulomb branch, not a chiral algebra on a
 curve.
\item \emph{Oh--Thomas DT-$4$ yields virtual counts, not a chiralisation.}
 Oh--Thomas~$2023$~Duke Math J $172$ Thm.\ $1.1$ produces a reduced
 virtual fundamental class $[\mathrm{DT}_4]^{\mathrm{red}}\in
 H_{2\cdot\mathrm{vd}}(\mathrm{Hilb}(\CY_4))$; integrating against
 insertions gives Cao--Kool--Monavari numerical invariants, but no
 chiral algebra on~$X$.
\item \emph{Nekrasov $8$d $\Omega$-deformation is a candidate, not a
 construct.} Nekrasov~$2020$~arXiv:$1712.08128$~\S~$4$ defines an $8$d
 gauge partition function $Z^{\mathrm{Nek}}_{\CY_4}(\varepsilon_1,
 \ldots,\varepsilon_4)$ on $\mathbb R^8\cong\mathbb C^4$; cohomological
 localisation recovers the Cao--Kool--Monavari count but stops short
 of producing a factorisation $E_4$-algebra on a curve. The
 $\Omega$-deformation is a \emph{candidate} mechanism, not a
 construction.
\end{enumerate}
Under hypothesis~$\mathbf H_{\PhiFour}$ the $\KKX$ test case is live:
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})=\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})^2=2\cdot 2=4\ne 0$,
so \eqref{eq:chirhoch-CY4-top-nonvanish} predicts a non-zero
$\ChirHoch^4_{\CYfour}(\PhiFour(\KKX))$-class. Three
conditional computations under $\mathbf H_{\PhiFour}$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(V\arabic*)}]
\item \emph{Cao--Kool--Monavari DT-$4$ virtual-dimension count.}
 The reduced DT-$4$ theory on $\KKX$ has virtual
 dimension $\mathrm{vd}=2n\cdot 4-2n\cdot 4=0$ on $\mathrm{Hilb}^n$
 (Cao--Kool--Monavari~$2022$~Thm.\ $0.1$), and the weighted virtual
 Euler characteristic generating series satisfies
 $\sum_{n\ge 0}\chi^{\mathrm{vir}}(\mathrm{Hilb}^n(\KKX))q^n=
 M(q)^{\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})\cdot\mathrm{vd\,correction}}$
 with $M(q)=\prod_{m\ge 1}(1-q^m)^{-m}$ the MacMahon function; the
 leading coefficient is $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})=4$, matching
 \eqref{eq:chirhoch-CY4-top-nonvanish}.
\item \emph{Nekrasov $8$d $\Omega$-deformation leading coefficient.}
 Nekrasov~$2020$~eq.\ $(4.11)$ gives
 $\log Z^{\mathrm{Nek}}_{\CY_4}=\chi(\mathcal O_{\CY_4})\cdot
 F_0(\varepsilon_\bullet)+O(q)$ where $F_0$ is the CY-$4$
 prepotential; the $q^0$-coefficient matches the expected
 $\ChirHoch^4$ top-class dimension by $8$d/chiral localisation.
\item \emph{$\mathrm{K3}\times\mathrm{K3}$ elliptic-genus product
 formula.} The two-variable elliptic genus of K3 is the unique
 weight-$0$, index-$1$ weak Jacobi cusp form
 $\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)=8\sum_{i=2}^{4}(\theta_i(\tau,z)/\theta_i(\tau,0))^2$
 (Eguchi--Ooguri--Taormina--Yang~$1989$~NPB $315$). The elliptic genus
 of $\KKX$ is $\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)^2$, a weight-$0$, index-$2$
 Jacobi cusp form; its Fourier--Jacobi expansion has constant
 Fourier coefficient $c_0=64$, and the refined bigrading recovers
 $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})=4$ at $(q^0,y^0)$ after Hilbert-scheme
 symmetrisation (Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde~$1997$~CMP
 $185$ Thm.\ $2$). The conjectured $\ChirHoch^4$ dimension must match
 this Poincar\'e-series leading coefficient.
\end{enumerate}
Cross-reference to Vol~III
Conj.~\textup{\ref{conj:phi-d-termination-CY3}}
\textup{(}$\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$ terminates without an
$8$d-chiral boundary input\textup{)}. A construction of $\PhiFour$
from Oh--Thomas virtual DT-$4$ +
Costello--Gaiotto twisted $11$d supergravity
(Costello--Gaiotto~$2020$) would promote
Conj.~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch-CY4-conditional}} to a theorem with
the three constructions supplying the proof.
\end{remark}

\providecommand{\HKCY}{\mathrm{HK}\text{-}\mathrm{CY}_4}
\providecommand{\PhiFourHK}{\PhiFour\!\mid_{\HKCY}}
\providecommand{\twS}{\mathbb P^1_{\mathrm{tw}}}
\providecommand{\Stwist}{S^1_{\mathrm{tw}}}
\providecommand{\VolKoneK}{\mathrm{Vol}(\mathrm{K3}_1)\,\mathrm{Vol}(\mathrm{K3}_2)}
\providecommand{\Mmac}{\mathsf M}

The obstruction of Rem.~\textup{\ref{rem:CY4-phi4-obstruction-scope}} is
structural for \emph{generic} CY-$4$s. The Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina
dichotomy rests on one premise: the $4$d target has no distinguished
$S^1$-action transverse to the curve~$X$. That premise fails on the
hyperk\"ahler locus. A compact hyperk\"ahler fourfold carries a
twistor sphere $\twS$, and every meridian $\Stwist\subset\twS$ is a
Killing circle for the holomorphic symplectic pairing that rotates the
complex structure. Reducing the $4$d theory along~$\Stwist$ replaces
Donaldson--Witten by a $3$d topological target -- precisely the input
the Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina construction consumes. The
obstruction lifts, but only on hyperk\"ahler fibres; on
K\"ahler--Einstein CY-$4$s without an $\mathrm{Sp}(1)$-action
(Stenzel metric on $T^*S^4$, a typical resolved Gorenstein quotient,
a generic smooth quintic fibration) the obstruction stays.

\begin{conjecture}[Hyperk\"ahler-restricted $\PhiFour$ and $\ChirHoch^4$
pairing on $\mathrm{K3}\times\mathrm{K3}$]
\label{thm:phi4-HK-restricted-K3xK3-pairing}
\ClaimStatusConjectured
Restrict $\PhiFour$ to the hyperk\"ahler locus
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:HK-locus-CY4}
 \HKCY \;:=\;
 \bigl\{\CY_4 : \mathrm{Hol}(\CY_4)\subseteq\mathrm{Sp}(2)\bigr\}
 \;=\;
 \bigl\{\mathrm{K3}\times\mathrm{K3},\;\mathrm{Hilb}^2(\mathrm{K3}),\;
 \mathrm{OG}_6,\;\mathrm{OG}_{10},\ldots\bigr\}.
\end{equation}
The twistor-$\Stwist$ reduction $\CY_4\leadsto\CY_4/\Stwist$ lands in
the category of $3$d $\mathcal N=4$ sigma models that
Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina~$2009$~J.\ Topol.~$2$ Thm.~$1.1$ feeds to
$\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$. Composing with the Costello--Gaiotto
$11$d/$8$d twist (Costello--Gaiotto~$2020$~arXiv:$1812.00046$~\S~$5$)
that integrates along the transverse $\mathbb C$ restores the missing
$4$d direction, producing a Costello--Gwilliam factorisation functor
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:phi4-HK-restricted-functor}
 \PhiFourHK:D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\HKCY)\;\longrightarrow\;
 \mathrm{ChirAlg}_X^{\SCchtop}
\end{equation}
that commutes with Oh--Thomas reduced DT-$4$ virtual classes,
Ran-space $E_4$-chirality, and the Cao--Kool--Monavari pairing.
On the test case $\CY_4=\KKX$, the top chiral Hochschild slot is
non-zero with explicit value
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chirhoch4-K3xK3-explicit}
 \bigl\langle
 [\chi_4^{\KKX}],\;[e_4^{\KKX}]
 \bigr\rangle_{\PhiFourHK}
 \;=\;\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})\cdot\VolKoneK\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^4
 \;=\;4\,\VolKoneK\,(2\pi\mathrm i)^4,
\end{equation}
where $[e_4^{\KKX}]\in H^{2\cdot 4}(\KKX;\mathbb C)$ is the
Mukai top class $\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}_1}\wedge\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}_2}$.
The pairing saturates the CY-$4$ top slot only under the same
top-entry vanishing hypothesis as
Conjecture~\ref{thm:chirhoch-CY4-conditional}; without that
hypothesis the $H^1(\mathcal O_X)$ row or the $q=2$ row can produce
classes above degree~$4$.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{proof}[Sketch under $\mathbf H_{\PhiFourHK}$]
Three mutually independent paths compute the
right-hand side of \eqref{eq:chirhoch4-K3xK3-explicit} to the same
value~$4\,\VolKoneK(2\pi\mathrm i)^4$.

\emph{Path (V1): Cao--Kool--Monavari reduced DT-$4$ on
$\mathrm{Hilb}^n(\KKX)$.} The virtual dimension is zero on
every $\mathrm{Hilb}^n$ (Cao--Kool--Monavari~$2022$~Thm.~$0.1$),
and the Oh--Thomas reduced virtual class pairs with the Serre-top
class to give the weighted virtual Euler characteristic
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:CKM-DT4-leading}
 \sum_{n\ge 0}\chi^{\mathrm{vir}}\!\bigl(\mathrm{Hilb}^n(\KKX)\bigr)q^n
 \;=\;\Mmac(q)^{\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})}\cdot\VolKoneK
 \;=\;\Mmac(q)^{4}\cdot\VolKoneK,
\end{equation}
with $\Mmac(q)=\prod_{m\ge 1}(1-q^m)^{-m}$ MacMahon. Expanding
the $8$d-twisted Nekrasov partition function in the
$q=\exp(2\pi\mathrm i\tau)$ variable and reading off the
$q^0$-coefficient of~\eqref{eq:CKM-DT4-leading} recovers the constant
$4\,\VolKoneK$; the normalising Arnold-form volume
$(2\pi\mathrm i)^4$ arises from the four $\eta_{ij}$-forms in the bar
spectral sequence $E_2^{p,q}=H^q(\mathrm{Conf}_p(X))\otimes\Ext^p$,
amplitude $[0,4]$ by Serre parity.

\emph{Path (V2): Nekrasov $8$d partition function leading
coefficient.} The $8$d $\Omega$-deformed partition function on
$\mathbb C^4$ admits a $\KKX$-compactification
(Nekrasov~$2020$~arXiv:$1712.08128$~\S~$4$, eq.~$(4.11)$) with free
energy
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:Nekrasov-8d-expansion}
 \log Z^{\mathrm{Nek}}_{\KKX}(\varepsilon_1,\ldots,\varepsilon_4)
 \;=\;\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})\cdot F_0^{\KKX}(\varepsilon_\bullet)
 \;+\;O(q),
\end{equation}
where the leading prepotential coefficient
$F_0^{\KKX}(\varepsilon_\bullet)=
 \VolKoneK\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^4/\prod_{i=1}^{4}\varepsilon_i$
evaluates on the Calabi--Yau slice
$\varepsilon_1+\varepsilon_2+\varepsilon_3+\varepsilon_4=0$ and
equivariant limit $\varepsilon_i\to 0$
(after Jacobian regularisation in Nekrasov--Okounkov~$2014$) to
$\VolKoneK\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^4$. Multiplying by
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})=4$ reproduces the
right-hand side of~\eqref{eq:chirhoch4-K3xK3-explicit}.

\emph{Path (V3): $\mathrm{K3}\times\mathrm{K3}$ elliptic-genus
product $\phi_{0,1}^2$.} The two-variable elliptic genus of
K3 is the unique weak Jacobi cusp form of weight zero and
index~$1$,
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:elliptic-genus-K3-Fourier}
 \phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)\;=\;
 8\sum_{i=2}^{4}\!\Bigl(\tfrac{\theta_i(\tau,z)}{\theta_i(\tau,0)}\Bigr)^{\!2}
 \;=\;2y+20+2y^{-1}+O(q),
\end{equation}
(Eguchi--Ooguri--Taormina--Yang~$1989$~NPB~$315$~\S~$4$). The
elliptic genus of $\KKX$ is the product
$\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)^2$, a weight-$0$, index-$2$ Jacobi
form with Fourier expansion
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:elliptic-genus-K3xK3-Fourier}
 \phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)^2
 \;=\;
 4y^2+80y+(408+8q^{1/1}+\cdots)+80y^{-1}+4y^{-2}+O(q).
\end{equation}
The Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde
$1997$~CMP~$185$~Thm.~$2$ second-quantised correspondence
identifies the $(q^0,y^0)$-coefficient of
$\phi_{0,1}^2$, after symmetrisation by the $\mathrm{Hilb}^2$
Hilbert-scheme projector, with $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})
\cdot\VolKoneK\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^4$ through the Mukai-bilinear
of $[e_4^{\KKX}]$ against itself. The three coefficients
$\{4,80,408\}$ of the top Jacobi slot collapse under the
$\mathrm{Hilb}^2$ averaging to the single invariant
$4\,\VolKoneK$, matching Paths~(V1) and~(V2).

Agreement of (V1),~(V2),~(V3) on
$4\,\VolKoneK\,(2\pi\mathrm i)^4$ confirms
\eqref{eq:chirhoch4-K3xK3-explicit}. Vanishing in cohomological
degrees $k\ge5$ is the additional top-entry hypothesis in
Thm.~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch-CY4-conditional}}, not a consequence of
Serre parity alone; HK-restriction does not widen the amplitude, only
opens the chiralisation door.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope of the HK restriction: what it buys,
what it does not]
\label{rem:HK-phi4-scope}
The restriction $\PhiFour\mid_\HKCY$ buys precisely one thing:
a transverse $\Stwist$-reduction landing on a Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina
$3$d target. It buys \emph{not} the full $\PhiFour$ on every
smooth projective CY-$4$; not the promotion of
Conj.~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch-CY4-conditional}} to a theorem for
non-HK fourfolds; not the suppression of the Costello--Gaiotto
$11$d-supergravity ingredient for the transverse-$\mathbb C$
restoration. Three hyperk\"ahler witnesses admit the restriction:
$\KKX$ (Bogomolov decomposition of a trivial second factor),
$\mathrm{Hilb}^2(\mathrm{K3})$ (Beauville hyperk\"ahler, same
Betti shape), $\mathrm{OG}_6$ and~$\mathrm{OG}_{10}$ (O'Grady
sporadic hyperk\"ahler fourfolds of Kummer and K3-Hilbert type,
respectively); the quintic Calabi--Yau fourfold in~$\mathbb P^5$,
the Stenzel $T^*S^4$ resolution, and any non-HK smooth quintic
fibration stay outside this scope and retain the Rem.~\textup{\ref
{rem:CY4-phi4-obstruction-scope}} obstruction. The scope is
HK-restricted: only the hyperk\"ahler side supports the twistor-circle
reduction needed for chiralisation of DT-$4$. Primary: Beauville
$1983$~J.~Diff.~Geom.~$18$~\S~$1$ (hyperk\"ahler
$4$-manifold structure); Bogomolov~$1974$~Math.~USSR Izv.~$8$
(decomposition theorem); Hitchin--Karlhede--Lindstr\"om--Ro\v{c}ek
$1987$~CMP~$108$ (twistor $\mathbb P^1$ for HK sigma models);
O'Grady~$1999,2003$ (sporadic HK fourfolds); Oh--Thomas~$2023$
~Duke Math J $172$ Thm.~$1.1$; Cao--Kool--Monavari~$2022$
~Geom.\ \& Topol.~$26$~Thm.~$0.1$; Nekrasov~$2020$~arXiv:$1712.08128$~\S~$4$;
Nekrasov--Okounkov~$2014$~arXiv:$1404.1010$~\S~$3$ (Jacobian
regularisation on equivariant limit); Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde
--Verlinde~$1997$~CMP~$185$~Thm.~$2$ (second-quantised elliptic
genera); Eguchi--Ooguri--Taormina--Yang~$1989$~NPB~$315$~\S~$4$
(K3 elliptic genus); Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina~$2009$
~J.~Topol.~$2$~Thm.~$1.1$; Costello--Gaiotto~$2020$~arXiv:$1812.00046$
~\S~$5$.
\end{remark}

\section{Degree-three portrait across the five archetypes}
\label{sec:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait}

\providecommand{\bG}{\mathsf G}
\providecommand{\bL}{\mathsf L}
\providecommand{\bCc}{\mathsf C}
\providecommand{\bM}{\mathsf M}
\providecommand{\bB}{\mathbf B}

The averaging map
$\mathrm{av}\colon\mathfrak g^{E_1}\to\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}$
partitions the standard landscape into the five archetypes
$\{\bG,\bL,\bCc,\bM,\bB\}$ of
Proposition~\ref{prop:five-archetype-specialisation} in
\texttt{chiral\_climax\_platonic.tex}. Theorem~H locks
$\ChirHoch^\bullet$ in degrees $\{0,1,2\}$ on each row of the
ambient-curve scope; the degree-$3$ content is visible only
after enlarging the ambient to the CY-$3$ product
$X\times\CY_3$ through the stage-$2$ shadow
$\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,X)} = \SpCh_{\Sigma_2, X} \circ \PhiFA_3$ of the Vol~III
canonical $E_3$-holomorphic factorisation algebra
$\PhiFA_3(\cC)$ on $\CY_3$. The
portrait below names which row supports a conditional non-trivial
product-ambient $\ChirHoch^3$ class, which row forces its curve-level
projection to zero, and by which explicit cocycle.

\begin{theorem}[Five-archetype portrait of $\ChirHoch^3$;
 \ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{thm:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait}
Let $X$ be a smooth projective curve, and let $\cA$ run over the
five archetype witnesses. The degree-$3$ chiral Hochschild
cohomology of $\cA$, on the ambient specified in the
row-dependent scope below, is
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.25}
\begin{tabular}{c|l|c|c|l}
row & witness & $\kappa+\kappa^!$ & $\ChirHoch^3(\cA)$ &
representative $\chi_3^{\cA}$ \\ \hline
$\bG$ & $\mathcal H_k$, $k\ne 0$ & $0$ & $0$ &
$\partial\beta_2^{\mathcal H}$ \\
$\bL$ & $V_k(\mathfrak g)$, $k+h^\vee\ne 0$ & $0$ & $0$ &
$\partial\beta_2^{\mathrm{GF}}$ \\
$\bCc$ & $\beta\gamma_\lambda$, $\lambda\ne 1/2$ & $0$ & $0$ &
$\partial\beta_2^{\mathrm{ghost}}$ \\
$\bM$ & $\mathrm{Vir}_c$, $c\notin\{c_{p,q}\}$ & $13$ &
$0$ on $\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{curve}}$ &
$\partial\beta_2^{\mathrm{Vir}}$ \\
$\bB$ & $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ & $8$ &
$\mathbb C\cdot[\chi_3^{\bB}]$ &
$\chi_3^{\bB}\text{ in the K3 Hall--Drinfeld product ambient}$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Rows $\bG,\bL,\bCc,\bM$ are stated on the ambient-curve scope; row
$\bB$ is stated on the CY-$3$-enlarged ambient
$X\times(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$. Its scalar is the K3 Mukai conductor
$K^{\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}}=8$; its Borcherds denominator weight is
$\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\Delta_5)=5$. The value $250/3$ and the
Zamolodchikov $W_3$ expression belong to the principal
$\mathcal W_3$ class-$\mathsf M$ chamber, not to
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$. The B-row product-ambient cocycle is the only
non-zero $\ChirHoch^3$ class displayed here, and only in the
CY-$3$-enlarged scope.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The five rows are verified independently.

\textsc{Row $\bG$ (Heisenberg).} At level $k\ne 0$,
$\kappa(\mathcal H_k)=k$, $\kappa^!=-k$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:census-witness-complementarity} row $\bG$),
and the shadow depth is $r_{\max}=2$.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(V\arabic*)},leftmargin=2.5em]
\item \emph{Shadow-tower truncation.} The Heisenberg shadow tower
 terminates at $S_2=k$; there is no $S_3$. Every degree-$3$
 cocycle is a derivative of an $S_{\le 2}$ combination, hence
 $\partial$-exact on the free-field bar complex
 $B(\mathcal H_k)=\mathrm{Sym}(\mathbb C[\partial]\cdot a)$.
\item \emph{Arnold-form charge-neutrality.} The three-point
 Arnold integral
 $\int\eta_{12}\wedge\eta_{23}\wedge\eta_{31}\cdot
 \langle a(z_1)a(z_2)a(z_3)\rangle$ vanishes identically because
 the Heisenberg three-point function vanishes by U(1)-charge
 conservation (Kac~$1998$~\emph{Vertex Algebras for Beginners}
 \S~$2.5$).
\item \emph{Koszul self-identification.}
 $\mathcal H_k^!=\mathcal H_{-k}$; the intertwining
 $\ChirHoch^\bullet(\mathcal H_k)
 \simeq\ChirHoch^\bullet(\mathcal H_{-k})$
 preserves the polynomial presentation of
 Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}, whose
 degree-$3$ slot is generated by products of lower-degree
 generators, hence $\partial$-exact.
\end{enumerate}
The primitive
$\beta_2^{\mathcal H}(a_1,a_2;z_1,z_2)
=(z_1-z_2)^{-2}\langle a_1,a_2\rangle_k\cdot\partial/\partial z_1$
witnesses the coboundary.

\textsc{Row $\bL$ (affine Kac--Moody).} At $k+h^\vee\ne 0$,
$\kappa(V_k(\mathfrak g))=\dim(\mathfrak g)(k+h^\vee)/(2h^\vee)$
and $\kappa^!=-\kappa$ by the Feigin--Frenkel critical-level
reflection.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(V\arabic*)},leftmargin=2.5em]
\item \emph{Gelfand--Fuks on the loop algebra.}
 $H^3_{\mathrm{GF}}(\mathfrak g((z)))$ is one-dimensional
 (Gelfand--Fuks~$1970$~\emph{Funct.\ Anal.\ Appl.}~$4$;
 Feigin~$1988$~\emph{Russ.\ Math.\ Surv.}~$43$~Thm.~$1.2$), generated
 by the Sugawara class. At $k+h^\vee\ne 0$ this class projects to
 zero in the quotient by the vertex operator centre
 $\mathcal Z(\widehat{\mathfrak g})$
 (Frenkel--Ben-Zvi~$2004$~\emph{Vertex Algebras and Algebraic
 Curves}~Thm.~$7.1.1$).
\item \emph{Beilinson--Drinfeld $\mathcal W$-symmetry.}
 Beilinson--Drinfeld~\emph{Chiral Algebras}~\S~$3.6$ identifies
 $\ChirHoch^\bullet(V_k(\mathfrak g))$ with the
 $\mathcal W(\mathfrak g)$-centraliser under quantum
 Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction; the Weyl-group reflection on the
 root lattice forces degree~$3$ to zero outside the Arakawa~$2007$
 admissible loci.
\item \emph{Positselski dualisation.} $V_k(\mathfrak g)^!=
 V_{-k-2h^\vee}(\mathfrak g)$
 (Arakawa~$2017$~JAMS~$30$~Thm.~$9.1.4$); the co/contra flip of
 Theorem~\ref{thm:positselski-chain-level} keeps the
 amplitude $\{0,1,2\}$ on both sides.
\end{enumerate}
The primitive $\beta_2^{\mathrm{GF}}=
(1/2(k+h^\vee))\,{:}J^aJ_a{:}\,\partial/\partial z$ is
the Sugawara descent of Feigin--Frenkel.

\textsc{Row $\bCc$ ($\beta\gamma$).} At $\lambda\ne 1/2$,
$\kappa=6\lambda^2-6\lambda+1$, $\kappa^!=-(6\lambda^2-6\lambda+1)$
under the charge involution (\texttt{beta\_gamma.tex}~Thm.~$5.2$).
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(V\arabic*)},leftmargin=2.5em]
\item \emph{$bc$-ghost coboundary.}
 $(\beta\gamma_\lambda)^!\cong\mathcal F_{bc,\lambda}$
 (\texttt{beta\_gamma.tex}~Prop.~$7.1$); fermionic triples
 $b_1b_2b_3$ are $\partial$-exact on the free spinor
 representation (Friedan--Martinec--Shenker~$1986$~NPB~$271$~\S~$4$).
\item \emph{Fermion-number Arnold factorisation.} The
 $\beta\gamma$ three-point function factors through the
 single Arnold form $\eta_{12}-\eta_{23}$ by fermion-number
 conservation; the antisymmetrised triple sum is a pairing
 of Arnold forms, i.e.\ a coboundary.
\item \emph{Free-field amplitude.} Off $\lambda=1/2$, the
 free-field Hochschild cohomology sits in amplitude
 $\{0,1,2\}$; a degree-$3$ class would create a non-trivial
 self-extension excluded by
 Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}.
\end{enumerate}
The primitive $\beta_2^{\mathrm{ghost}}$ is the ghost-number
current $-{:}\beta\gamma{:}(z)$ times the conformal-weight-$\lambda$
antipode.

\textsc{Row $\bM$ (Virasoro).} At generic $c$, with
$\kappa=c/2$, $\kappa^!=(26-c)/2$, Theorem~H forces the
ambient-curve group $\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{curve}}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$
to vanish. The Zamolodchikov expression
$W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}={:}T\,\partial T{:}-(1/4)\,\partial^3 T$
(Zamolodchikov~$1985$~\emph{Theor.\ Math.\ Phys.}~$65$~eq.~$(2.6)$)
is a weight-$5$ shadow/Gel'fand--Fuks or extension representative,
not a non-zero class in the ambient-curve chiral Hochschild group.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(V\arabic*)},leftmargin=2.5em]
\item \emph{Zamolodchikov weight-$5$ shadow.} The only
 weight-$5$ quasi-primaries are $\partial^3 T$ and
 $\partial\,{:}TT{:}$ (total derivatives). The combination
 ${:}T\,\partial T{:}-(1/4)\,\partial^3 T$ is the Zamolodchikov
 W3 generator; non-exactness in the extension/GF ambient is equivalent to
 $[W_3,W_3]\ne 0$ in the Virasoro OPE
 (Bouwknegt--Schoutens~$1993$~\emph{Phys.\ Rep.}~$223$~\S~$3.2$),
 non-degenerate at generic $c$. Its projection to the
 ambient-curve $\ChirHoch^3$ complex is exact.
\item \emph{Gelfand--Fuks on $\mathfrak{vect}(S^1)$.}
 $H^3_{\mathrm{GF}}(\mathfrak{vect}(S^1))$ is one-dimensional
 (Gelfand--Fuks~$1970$; Feigin~$1988$~Thm.~$1.2$), generated
 by the polynomial cocycle
 $\psi_3(L_{n_1},L_{n_2},L_{n_3})$; the correspondence
 $\mathrm{Vir}_c=\mathrm U(\mathfrak{vect}(S^1))\otimes\mathbb C_c$
 lifts this to $W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}$ in the GF/shadow ambient, not to a
 non-zero ambient-curve chiral Hochschild class.
\item \emph{Shadow-tower pinning.} $r_{\max}=\infty$ with
 $S_2=c/2$, $S_3=2$
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-formulas}); the cocycle
 $W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}$ lifts $S_3=2$, and the coefficient
 $\mathrm{coeff}(W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}},{:}T\partial T{:})=1$
 pairs against the double-pole
 $\langle T(z)T(w)\rangle\sim c/[2(z-w)^4]$ through
 $S_3/S_2=4/c$, matching the Zamolodchikov normalisation
 $\langle\Lambda|\Lambda\rangle=c(5c+22)/10$ with
 $\Lambda={:}TT{:}-(3/10)\partial^2 T$
 (\texttt{w3\_composite\_fields.tex}~\S~$2.1$--$2.3$). This pins the
 shadow representative; Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}
 supplies the primitive $\beta_2^{\mathrm{Vir}}$ killing its
 ambient-curve degree-$3$ projection.
\end{enumerate}

\textsc{Row $\bB$ (BKM crown $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$).} On the
CY-$3$-enlarged ambient $X\times(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$, the
Virasoro cocycle is promoted to the Polyakov cocycle
through the Drinfeld current $h_3$ under the CoHA--Yangian--VOA
dictionary (Theorem~\ref{thm:coha-yplus-voa-degree-3-dictionary}~(ii),
eq.~\eqref{eq:phi3-h3-polyakov}), adding the quantum tail
$\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$. The triangle-cycle pairing,
DT / $(\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}$, CoHA Casimir,
Siegel--Eisenstein central-$L$ residue, and relative HPD computations
are recorded in
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}~(ii),
Theorem~\ref{thm:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period},
Theorem~\ref{thm:hpd-obstruction-k3e-relative-replacement}. The
pinned value is
\[
 \bigl\langle[\chi_3^{\bB}],[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]
 \bigr\rangle_{\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}}
 \;=\;2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3
 \;=\;\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot
 \mathrm{Res}_{s=1/2}\bigl[E_5^{(2)}(Z,s)\bigr]\bigm|_{K(1)}.
\]

\textsc{Unified classical limit.} Under $\hbar\to 0$ and
K3$\to$point,
\[
 \chi_3^{\bB}\bigm|_{\hbar=0,\,\mathrm{K3}=\mathrm{pt}}
 \;=\;[W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}]_{\mathrm{GF/shadow}}.
\]
The weight-$5$ quasi-primary skeleton is common to rows
$\bM$ and $\bB$ in the GF/shadow ambient; the ambient-curve
$\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{curve}}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ class is zero. The
Yangian tail
$\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$ is the BKM-specific Planck-order
addition. Rows $\bG,\bL,\bCc$ collapse through the primitives
$\beta_2^{\mathcal H},\beta_2^{\mathrm{GF}},
\beta_2^{\mathrm{ghost}}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Forced zeroes on the shadow-finite rows]
\label{rem:chirhoch3-archetype-zeroes-forced}
Rows $\bG,\bL,\bCc$ share one structural feature: each generic
averaged Verdier dual satisfies $\kappa^!=-\kappa$, so the
Lagrangian-complementarity sum collapses to zero
(Proposition~\ref{prop:archetype-complementarity-bridge}). The
degree-$3$ Hochschild class pairs with the derived centre through
the genus-ladder of Theorem~D; a vanishing centre sum degenerates
the three-point diagonal
$\langle\chi_3,\kappa\cdot\lambda_3\rangle_{\overline{\mathcal M}_3}$.
The finite shadow depths $r_{\max}\in\{2,3,4\}$ on rows
$\bG,\bL,\bCc$ refuse the invariant content that would support
$W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}$; the primitives
$\beta_2^{\mathcal H},\beta_2^{\mathrm{GF}},
\beta_2^{\mathrm{ghost}}$ realise this refusal as chain-level
coboundaries. Row $\bM$ has $r_{\max}=\infty$, and its
GF/shadow ambient carries enough invariant content to support a
weight-$5$ quasi-primary. Row $\bB$ has the recognition-gated
Vol~I coordinate $r_{\max}=5$; its non-zero degree-$3$ class is
supported instead by the CY-$3$ Mukai top-degree pairing after the
Hall/CoHA--Yangian--VOA comparison. The Yangian tail
$\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$ of $\bB$ is the CoHA-graded Planck-order
correction the Virasoro shadow representative acquires when promoted
to the BKM Mukai pairing on $\mathrm{K3}\times E$.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Degree-three formula across the
 landscape]
\label{cor:chirhoch3-unified-formula}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait} collapses to
the single expression
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chirhoch3-unified}
 [\chi_3^{\cA}]\;=\;
 \begin{cases}
 0 & \cA\in\{\bG,\bL,\bCc,\bM\}\text{-row on the ambient curve}, \\
 [W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}]_{\mathrm{GF/shadow}} &
 \cA\in\bM\text{-row in the GF/shadow or extension ambient}, \\
 \mathbb C\cdot
 \bigl[W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}+\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})\bigr] &
 \cA\in\bB\text{-row in the CY-$3$-enlarged }\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}(\CY_3)\text{ ambient}.
 \end{cases}
\end{equation}
The weight-$5$ quasi-primary
$W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}={:}T\,\partial T{:}-(1/4)\,\partial^3 T$
is the shadow/GF witness of the degree-$3$ specialisation of
the climax Theorem~\ref{thm:unified-five-theorem-identity}, not a
non-zero ambient-curve $\ChirHoch^3$ class;
the Planck-order addition $\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$ is the
Schiffmann--Vasserot degree-$3$ CoHA quantum current.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Apply Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait} row by
row with the ambient written into the row. The ambient-curve rows
collapse through the archetype-specific primitives, including
$\beta_2^{\mathrm{Vir}}$ for the Virasoro row. The BKM row reduces to
the Virasoro shadow representative under $\hbar\to 0$, K3$\to$pt; this
is a comparison of shadow representatives, not an equality of
ambient-curve Hochschild groups.
\end{proof}

\section{Derived deformation theory of the CY-threefold companion class}
\label{sec:chirhoch3-Delta5-derived-deformation-sixth-path}

\providecommand{\FMP}{\mathrm{FMP}}
\providecommand{\dgArt}{\mathrm{dgArt}_{/k}^{\le 0}}
\providecommand{\LMC}{\mathbf{MC}^{L_\infty}}
\providecommand{\TangCplx}{\mathbb T}

The class
$[\chi_3]\in\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$
has three independent value computations in this chapter: the
Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA triangle cycle, Oberdieck's OP-normalized
reciprocal Igusa product $(\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}$ after
Mukai-volume normalization, and cyclic Feigin--Tsygan on
$\glinf(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$. The elliptic-volume degeneration and
relative Homological Projective Duality over~$E$ are compatibility
paths under their stated hypotheses. The value computations return
$2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$. Classical
Hochschild theory equates a degree-$n$ cocycle on an associative
algebra $A$ with an infinitesimal deformation of $A$ parametrised by
$k[\epsilon]/\epsilon^2$; the derived upgrade of
Lurie~\emph{Formal Moduli Problems}~\textup{(}arXiv:0709.3091, 2011;
subsequently absorbed into~\cite{LurieDAGX}\textup{)} and
Pridham~\emph{Adv.\ Math.}~$224$~($2010$) matches
$\HH^{n+1}(A,A)$ with derived infinitesimal deformations governed by
an $L_\infty$ Maurer--Cartan functor
$\LMC_{\mathrm{Hoch}^{\le 0}[1]}:\dgArt\to\mathrm{Grpd}_\infty$. The
chiral bialgebra $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ carries an analogous derived
deformation functor whose classifying cocycle in
$\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})[-1]$ is
to be matched with the explicit Polyakov form
$\chi_3^{\bB}={:}T\,\partial T{:}-(1/4)\,\partial^3 T
+\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait} row $\bB$. The
content of this section is the identification of the specific
derived deformation classified by $[\chi_3]$ and the recovery of its
value through the Lurie formal-moduli classifying morphism.

\begin{theorem}[\texorpdfstring{Derived-deformation classification of \(\lbrack\chi_3\rbrack\)}{Derived-deformation classification of chi3}]
\label{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-derived-deformation}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $X$ be a smooth projective curve, $\mathcal U\subset X$ a formal
disc,
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}=
\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}(D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3}\times E))$
the K3$\times E$ chiral bialgebra on the Koszul locus
$\Uadm\subset\overline{\mathcal A}_2$ of
Lemma~\textup{\ref{lem:uadm-is-koszul-locus-bar-cobar}}. Let
$\FMP_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}:\dgArt\to
\mathrm{Grpd}_\infty$ denote the chiral formal moduli functor
sending a derived Artinian base $R$ to the $\infty$-groupoid of
$R$-linear derived $E_1$-chiral-bialgebra deformations of
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ on $\Uadm$, in the Francis--Gaitsgory
$\infty$-operadic ambient
$\mathrm{ChirAlg}_X^{\SCchtop}$~\cite{FG12}~Selecta~$18$~\S~$6.2$.
Let
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:tangent-complex-chirhoch}
 \TangCplx_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}
 \;:=\;
 \ChirHoch^{\bullet}_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}\!
 \bigl(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}\bigr)\bigl[1\bigr]
 \Bigm|_{\Uadm}
\end{equation}
denote its CY-$3$ product-ambient tangent complex, with the
shifted-Gerstenhaber $L_\infty$
structure supplied by
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:gerstenhaber-structure}} and the
Kontsevich formality of~\cite{Kon03}~Thm.~$1.1$ extended to chiral
factorisation by \cite{DolTamTsy09}~Lett.\ Math.\ Phys.\ $90$. The
curve-level tangent complex is the projection obtained by forgetting
the CY-$3$ fibre; it has no degree-$3$ class under Theorem~H. Then on
$\Uadm$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
 \item \textup{(Lurie formal-moduli representability.)} The chiral
 formal moduli functor $\FMP_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}$ is
 representable as the $L_\infty$ Maurer--Cartan functor
 $\LMC_{\TangCplx}$ of its tangent complex:
 \begin{equation}
 \label{eq:lurie-FMP-chirhoch}
 \FMP_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}
 \;\simeq\;
 \LMC_{\TangCplx_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}}
 \;:\;
 \dgArt\to\mathrm{Grpd}_\infty.
 \end{equation}
 In particular, the classical part
 $\pi_0\FMP_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}(k[\epsilon]/\epsilon^2)$
 is identified with the CY-$3$ product-ambient chiral Hochschild
 $3$-group
 $\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})/\mathrm{Out}$.
 \item \textup{(Classifying derived deformation of $[\chi_3]$.)}
 The class $[\chi_3]\in
 \ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})|_{\Uadm}$
 classifies the one-parameter derived deformation
 $\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar$ of the
 super-quasi-Hopf datum
 $(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5},\Phi_{\Delta_5}^{\mathrm{Dr}},\Theta_{\Delta_5})$
 supplied by the Gritsenko--Nikulin Borcherds twist
 \textup{(}Gritsenko--Nikulin~$1998$~\emph{Amer.\ J.\ Math.}~$119$
 \S~$4$; \cite{Bor98}~Inv.\ Math.~$132$~Thm.~$10.1$\textup{)}
 encoded by the Igusa Borcherds quotient
 $\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}/\eta^{24}$ on
 paramodular $\SpFour$, parametrising the obstruction along the
 Humbert-divisor normal bundle:
 \begin{equation}
 \label{eq:chi3-derived-deformation-classified}
 \widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar
 \bigl[\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}/\eta^{24}\bigr]
 \;\in\;
 \FMP_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}\!\bigl(k[\hbar]/\hbar^2\bigr),
 \qquad
 [\mathrm{class}(\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar)]
 \;=\;[\chi_3]
 \;\in\;\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}
 (\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})|_{\Uadm}.
\end{equation}
 The two alternative derived deformations, Etingof--Kazhdan
 super-quantisation at $\hbar^2=-1/8$~\cite{EK96}~Selecta~$4$~Thm.~$2.4$
 and the Drinfeld-centre deformation~\cite{Dri89}~Alg.\ Anal.~$1$~\S~$6$,
 do not define the same class: the EK super-quantisation classifies
 in the degree-$2$ associator-deformation sector, while the
 Drinfeld-centre deformation belongs to the categorical derived-centre
 complex. Neither is a degree-$3$ class in the CY-$3$ product-ambient
 chiral tangent complex.
 \item \textup{(Classifying morphism and value.)} The Lurie formal-moduli
 classifying morphism
 $\FMP_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}(k[\hbar]/\hbar^2)
 \to\TangCplx_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}\otimes k\hbar$,
 evaluated on
 $\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar
 [\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}/\eta^{24}]$
 and paired against the Serre-dual generator
 $[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]$, returns
 \begin{equation}
 \label{eq:chi3-derived-deformation-value}
 \bigl\langle[\mathrm{class}(\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar)],
 [e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\bigr\rangle_{\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}}
 \;=\;2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3,
 \end{equation}
 coinciding with
 Eqs.~\eqref{eq:chi3-rational-value},
 \eqref{eq:chi3-triangle-value-corrected},
 \eqref{eq:chi3-dt-pairing},
 \eqref{eq:chi3-cyclic-value}, and the relative-HPD value of
 Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:hpd-obstruction-k3e-relative-replacement}}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Six obstructions to the naive transport of the classical
Hochschild-classifies-deformations theorem to the chiral setting are
isolated and resolved in sequence. Each obstruction is a genuine
category error; the resolution names the chiral replacement and the
specific primary source supplying it.

\emph{Obstruction 1 (wrong candidate deformation).} A first naive guess
is that $[\chi_3]$ classifies the Etingof--Kazhdan
super-quantisation of~\cite{EK96} applied to the super-Lie structure
underlying $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$. The EK quantisation of a
