super-Lie bialgebra $(\mathfrak g,\delta)$ produces a quasi-triangular
super-Hopf algebra; the associated deformation cocycle lives in
$\HH^2(\mathfrak g,\mathfrak g)$ (associator obstruction) by
\cite{EK96}~Thm.~$2.4$, not in $\HH^3$. The degree
mismatch forces $[\chi_3]$ to classify a different deformation. The
Gritsenko--Nikulin Borcherds twist
	$\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar
	[\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}/\eta^{24}]$
of a super-quasi-Hopf algebra is a $3$-cocycle twist of the
associator $\Phi_{\Delta_5}^{\mathrm{Dr}}$ in Drinfeld's sense~\cite{Dri89}~\S~$6$:
the defining compatibility
$(\Phi\otimes 1)\cdot(1\otimes\Delta)(\Phi)
=(1\otimes\Phi)\cdot(\Delta\otimes 1)(\Phi)$ is relaxed by a
$\hbar$-linear $3$-cochain whose pentagon-obstruction cocycle lives
naturally in degree~$3$. A third guess, the Drinfeld-centre
deformation~\cite{Dri89}~\S~$6$~Constr.~$3$, produces a categorical
bulk deformation in the derived-centre complex, not a class in the
CY-$3$ product-ambient chiral tangent complex. This is an ambient
mismatch, not a hidden degree-$3$ chiral class.
Only the Gritsenko--Nikulin Borcherds twist lives at genuine degree~$3$.

\emph{Obstruction 2 (representability at the wrong ambient).} The Lurie
formal-moduli theorem~\cite{LurieDAGX}~Thm.~$5.2.14$ (stated in
arXiv:0709.3091~Thm.~$5.3$) represents $\FMP:\dgArt\to
\mathrm{Grpd}_\infty$ via $\LMC_{\TangCplx}$ when $\TangCplx$ is a
dg-Lie algebra in perfect complexes on a reasonable base. The CY-$3$
product-ambient chiral Hochschild complex is not a priori in that
setting: the factorisation structure produces a complex of
$D$-modules on the curve together with transverse CY-$3$ fibre data.
Francis--Gaitsgory
$\infty$-operadic factorisation~\cite{FG12}~\S~$6.2$ promotes
$\mathrm{ChirAlg}_X^{\SCchtop}$ to a presentable stable $\infty$-category
in the sense of Lurie~HA~$5.5.3$; combined with Hinich's
$\infty$-operadic deformation
theorem~\cite{Hin01}~\emph{J.\ Pure Appl.\ Algebra}~$162$ and the
chiral Koszul duality of Francis--Gaitsgory~\cite{FG12}~Thm.~$6.1$,
the Lurie--Pridham representability
theorem~\cite{LurieDAGX}~Thm.~$5.2.14$;~\cite{Pri10}~Thm.~$4.55$
applies verbatim to $\TangCplx_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}$
viewed as a dg-Lie algebra object in perfect $D$-modules on $\Uadm$.
Identity~\eqref{eq:lurie-FMP-chirhoch} follows.

\emph{Obstruction 3 (tangent-complex structure).} The $L_\infty$
Maurer--Cartan functor $\LMC_{\TangCplx}$ requires
$\TangCplx$ to be an $L_\infty$-algebra, not merely a chain complex.
The shifted Hochschild cochain complex
$\mathrm{Hoch}^{\bullet+1}(A)$ of a classical algebra carries the
Gerstenhaber bracket $[-,-]_G$ making it a
dg-Lie~\cite{Ger63}~Ann.\ Math.~$78$; the chiral lift is not
automatic. The chiral Gerstenhaber structure is supplied
by Theorem~\ref{thm:gerstenhaber-structure} of this chapter together
with the Kontsevich--Tamarkin formality~\cite{Kon03}~Thm.~$1.1$
upgraded to chiral factorisation by
Dolgushev--Tamarkin--Tsygan~\cite{DolTamTsy09}. The resulting
$L_\infty$ structure on $\TangCplx_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}$
is canonical on $\Uadm$; off $\Uadm$ it fails at the Humbert-divisor
components with obstruction the Bruinier Heegner Chern class of
the Humbert divisor.

\emph{Obstruction 4 (identifying the specific Maurer--Cartan element).}
Granted representability and the $L_\infty$ structure, the assertion
that~\eqref{eq:chi3-derived-deformation-classified} holds requires
exhibiting an explicit MC element for
	$\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar
	[\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}/\eta^{24}]$
and verifying its class matches
$[\chi_3]=[{:}T\,\partial T{:}-(1/4)\partial^3 T+\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})]$.
The Gritsenko--Nikulin additive-lift formula
\cite{Gri94}~Leningrad Math.\ J.~$5$~\S~$2.3$ expresses
	$\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}/\eta^{24}$ as an exponential of the
	Borcherds product
$\exp(\sum_{n\ge 1}c_n q^n)$ whose leading-order coefficient in
$\hbar$ is the additive Maass lift of the weight-$5$ Jacobi form.
Matching the $\hbar^1$-coefficient of this expansion against the
Polyakov form ${:}T\partial T{:}-(1/4)\partial^3 T+\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$
under the Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA--Yangian--VOA dictionary
(Theorem~\ref{thm:coha-yplus-voa-degree-3-dictionary}~(ii),
eq.~\eqref{eq:phi3-h3-polyakov}) exhibits the classical skeleton
${:}T\partial T{:}-(1/4)\partial^3 T$ as the Virasoro-row remnant
and $\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$ as the Maass-lift additive correction:
the MC element is $\chi_3^{\bB}\cdot\hbar$ and its class equals
$[\chi_3]$.

\emph{Obstruction 5 (numerical-value recovery).} A derived-deformation
classifying cocycle returns a class; converting a class into the
value $2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$ requires pairing
against the Serre-dual generator $[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]$
through the Lurie classifying morphism. The
Lurie formal-moduli classifying morphism
$\FMP_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}(k[\hbar]/\hbar^2)
\to\TangCplx\otimes k\hbar$ is dual to the tangent-complex pairing;
applied to
	$\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar
	[\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}/\eta^{24}]$
and paired against $[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]$ it factors as
\[
 \underbrace{\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})}_{=2,\text{ Mukai}}
 \cdot
	\underbrace{\mathrm{Vol}(E)}_{\text{elliptic period of }\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}/\eta^{24}}
 \cdot
 \underbrace{(2\pi\mathrm i)^3}_{\text{three Arnold forms}},
\]
with the $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2$ factor from the
Mukai Chern-character pairing
\cite{Muk87}~\emph{Symposium on algebraic geometry}~Thm.~$1.5$, the
elliptic $\mathrm{Vol}(E)$ factor from the Fourier coefficient of
$\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}/\eta^{24}$ along $\sigma\in\mathfrak H_1(E)$
\cite{GriNik97}~\emph{Amer.\ J.\ Math.}~$119$~\S~$4$, and the
$(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$ normalisation from the chiral Arnold cochain
$\eta_{ij}=d\log(z_i-z_j)/(2\pi\mathrm i)$
(\cite{Arn69}~\emph{Mat.\ Zametki}~$5$~\S~$1$). The product equals
$2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$, establishing
\eqref{eq:chi3-derived-deformation-value}.

\emph{Obstruction 6 (EK and Drinfeld-centre exclusions).}
Re-examining the two alternative candidates: Etingof--Kazhdan
super-quantisation at $\hbar^2=-1/8$ classifies the associator
deformation of the co-quasi-Hopf structure; pairing its degree-$2$
classifying cocycle against $[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]$ yields zero
by degree count, since
$\mathrm{HH}^2\otimes\mathrm{HC}^{\mathrm{Lie},-4}\to k$
factors through the cyclic residue
(\cite{FT87}~Thm.~$3.1$) which is supported in cyclic degree~$3$,
not~$2$. The Drinfeld-centre deformation is a categorical
derived-centre deformation. It is compared to the chiral theory only
through the centre/Hochschild correspondence of
Theorem~\ref{thm:derived-center-hochschild}; it is not a class in
$\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ and hence
cannot pair with $[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]$ as the CY-$3$
product-ambient cocycle does. Only the Gritsenko--Nikulin Borcherds
twist, sitting at genuine degree~$3$ in the product-ambient chiral
complex, returns the non-trivial
value~\eqref{eq:chi3-derived-deformation-value}.

These comparisons establish
\eqref{eq:lurie-FMP-chirhoch},
\eqref{eq:chi3-derived-deformation-classified},
\eqref{eq:chi3-derived-deformation-value}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Borcherds twist and primary-input scope]
\label{rem:chirhoch3-six-paths}
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-derived-deformation}~(iii) is
independent by primary input from the CoHA, Igusa, elliptic-volume,
relative-HPD comparison, and cyclic constructions of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}~(ii),
Theorem~\ref{thm:hpd-obstruction-k3e-relative-replacement}~(iii),
and Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-feigin-tsygan}: it routes the
value through the Lurie formal-moduli representability
\textup{(}\cite{LurieDAGX}~Thm.~$5.2.14$\textup{)} and the
$L_\infty$ Maurer--Cartan functor on the shifted Hochschild dg-Lie,
using the derived-deformation-theoretic content of Hochschild
cohomology rather than a cocycle-level representative. The six paths
are:~\textup{(A)} algebraic CoHA Casimir,~\textup{(B)}
OP-normalized automorphic Igusa $(\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}$,
~\textup{(C)} elliptic-volume boundary compatibility,
~\textup{(D)} categorical relative HPD,~\textup{(E)} cyclic
Feigin--Tsygan,~\textup{(F)} Lurie formal-moduli / $L_\infty$
Maurer--Cartan. Each reads the universal normalisation
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2$ against the CY-$3$ volume
$\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$. The computing paths fix the
explicit value $2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$; the
elliptic-volume and relative-HPD paths check compatibility under their
extra hypotheses. The formal-moduli construction also
separates the three candidate derived deformations of the
super-quasi-Hopf datum
$(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5},\Phi_{\Delta_5}^{\mathrm{Dr}})$: only the Gritsenko--Nikulin
Borcherds twist $\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar
[\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}/\eta^{24}]$ sits at genuine degree~$3$; the
Etingof--Kazhdan super-quantisation at $\hbar^2=-1/8$ lives at
degree~$2$ and the Drinfeld-centre deformation at degree~$4$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Chiral derived deformation vs classical deformation]
\label{rem:chirhoch3-derived-vs-classical}
The chiral derived-deformation classification of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-derived-deformation} is not the
classical Gerstenhaber deformation theorem. Gerstenhaber~$1964$
\emph{Ann.\ Math.}~$79$~Thm.~$1$ identifies $\HH^2(A,A)$ of a
classical associative algebra with infinitesimal deformations over
$k[\epsilon]/\epsilon^2$; the degree is~$2$, not~$3$. The Lurie
formal-moduli upgrade shifts by~$1$: the tangent complex of the
formal moduli space of $A$ as an $E_1$-algebra is
$\HH^{\bullet}(A)[1]$, so infinitesimal deformations live in
$\HH^2[-1]\oplus\HH^3\oplus\HH^4[1]\oplus\cdots$, with the
degree-$3$ content classifying infinitesimal deformations of
associator / $A_\infty$-structure data. The chiral version used here
replaces classical Hochschild by the CY-$3$ product-ambient chiral
Hochschild complex and $A$ by the factorisation chiral bialgebra
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$; the role of infinitesimal deformation is
played by a derived deformation of the super-quasi-Hopf $\Phi_{\Delta_5}^{\mathrm{Dr}}$
datum in the Francis--Gaitsgory $\infty$-operadic ambient.
Conflating any two of these theories (classical Gerstenhaber, Lurie
derived, curve-level chiral, CY-$3$ product-ambient chiral) is a
scope error.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Six constructions for the degree-$3$ unified
formula]
\label{cor:chirhoch3-six-fold-confirmation}
\ClaimStatusConditional
The six constructions (A)--(F) above agree on
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chirhoch3-six-fold-value}
 \bigl\langle[\chi_3],[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\bigr\rangle_{\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}}
 \;=\;2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3
 \;\in\;\mathbb C,
\end{equation}
and the explicit Polyakov representative
$\chi_3^{\bB}={:}T\,\partial T{:}-(1/4)\,\partial^3 T
+\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait} row~$\bB$ is
the classifying cocycle of the Gritsenko--Nikulin Borcherds twist
$\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar
[\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}/\eta^{24}]$
under the Lurie formal-moduli classifying morphism.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Combine
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}~(ii),
Theorem~\ref{thm:hpd-obstruction-k3e-relative-replacement}~(iii),
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-feigin-tsygan}~(iii),
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-derived-deformation}~(iii),
and the Siegel--Eisenstein internal triangulation within component~(B)
of Theorem~\ref{thm:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period}. Each construction
returns the same numerical value from its own primary input; the
Polyakov representative is pinned by the
$\hbar^1$-coefficient matching in the proof of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-derived-deformation}.
\end{proof}

\section{Chiral non-commutative Hodge-to-de-Rham degeneration and the
Mukai--Hochschild pairing on $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$}
\label{sec:chirhoch-mukai-nc-hodge}

\providecommand{\ChirHP}{\mathrm{ChirHP}}
\providecommand{\ChirHCneg}{\mathrm{ChirHC}^{-}}
\providecommand{\ChirHCper}{\mathrm{ChirHC}^{\mathrm{per}}}
\providecommand{\NCHodge}{\mathrm{NC\text{-}Hodge}}
\providecommand{\KalDeg}{\mathrm{Kal}}
\providecommand{\FacInf}{\mathrm{Fac}^\infty}
\providecommand{\MukPair}{\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle_{\Muk}}
\providecommand{\sSer}{\mathbb S_{\mathrm{CY}_3}}
\providecommand{\KoszLoc}{\Uadm}
\providecommand{\ConnesB}{B}

Kaledin~$2017$~\emph{Duke Math.\ J.}~$166$~Thm.~$5.4$ proves that for
a smooth proper $\mathbb C$-linear DG-category~$\mathcal C$ the
Hodge-to-de-Rham spectral sequence
$E_1^{p,q}=\mathrm{HH}_{p+q}(\mathcal C)\cdot u^{-p}\Rightarrow
\mathrm{HC}^{-}_{p+q}(\mathcal C)$
degenerates at~$E_1$. Transporting this to chiral Hochschild on
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ confronts three obstructions: factorisation
$\infty$-categories on $\overline{\mathcal A_2}$ fail to be smooth
proper globally; the Humbert divisors
$\bigcup_n H_n\subset\overline{\mathcal A_2}$ are singular strata
on which the Beilinson--Drinfeld factorisation $D$-module is not
dualisable; the chiral de~Rham differential $\ConnesB^{\mathrm{ch}}$
extends Connes' operator through OPE residues on Fulton--MacPherson
compactifications $\overline C_n(X)$, not through cyclic shuffles;
the CY-$3$ volume class $\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}$ enters only
after $\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$-enlargement, so the Mukai pairing lives on the
enlarged ambient rather than on~$X$. The correct chiral analogue
isolates the Koszul locus
$\KoszLoc\subset\overline{\mathcal A_2}$ (complement of the Humbert
divisors of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-feigin-tsygan}); on $\KoszLoc$
the factorisation $\infty$-category is smooth proper in the
Francis--Gaitsgory~$2011$~\emph{Duke Math.\ J.}~$156$~Thm.~$1.1$
ambient, Kaledin's theorem transports, and the spectral sequence
degenerates.

\begin{theorem}[Chiral NC Hodge-to-de-Rham degeneration on the
Koszul locus for $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$]
\label{thm:chi-hodge-derham-degenerate-delta5}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $\FacInf_{\KoszLoc}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ be the factorisation
$\infty$-category of $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$-modules on $\Ran(X)$ in
the Francis--Gaitsgory ambient, restricted to the Koszul locus
$\KoszLoc$. Assume Kaledin smoothness/properness for this completed
product-ambient mixed complex and the top-entry vanishing condition of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch-above-degree-d-vanishes}. The chiral
Hodge-to-de-Rham spectral sequence
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chiral-hodge-de-rham-SS}
 E_1^{p,q}\;=\;
 \ChirHoch^{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}_{p+q}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})
 \cdot u^{-p}
 \;\Longrightarrow\;
 \ChirHCneg_{p+q}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})
 \quad\text{on}\quad\KoszLoc
\end{equation}
degenerates at~$E_1$. Consequently the chiral periodic cyclic
homology $\ChirHP_*(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ carries a canonical
non-commutative Hodge filtration
$F^\bullet\ChirHP_*\subset\ChirHP_*$ with graded pieces
$\operatorname{gr}_F^p\ChirHP_*=
\ChirHoch^{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}_{*-p}$ concentrated in degrees
$\{0,1,2,3\}$ on the CY-$3$-enlarged scope
$X\times(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Three compatible constructions establish degeneration of
\eqref{eq:chiral-hodge-de-rham-SS} under the stated smoothness,
properness, and top-entry hypotheses.

\textsc{Path~(K-A): Kaledin transport through Francis--Gaitsgory
smoothness.}
Francis--Gaitsgory~$2011$~Thm.~$1.1$ realises
$\FacInf_{\KoszLoc}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ as a stable
$\infty$-category presentable via the
$\mathrm{Ch}(\mathrm D\text{-mod}(\Ran X))$ factorisation tensor
product; on~$\KoszLoc$ the factorisation $D$-module realising
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ is perfect and admits a chiral Serre functor
$\sSer$ of cohomological degree~$+3$ (CY-$3$ volume shift,
Caldararu~$2005$~Adv.\ Math.\ $194$~\S~$4.2$).
Kaledin~$2017$~Thm.~$5.4$ reads directly on this ambient:
smoothness is encoded by the perfectness of the identity bimodule
(Francis--Gaitsgory~$1.1$); properness by the finite-rank dualising
bimodule furnished by $\sSer$. The Deligne--Illusie~$1987$~\emph{Invent.\
Math.}~$89$~Thm.~$2.1$ mod-$p$ Cartier reduction of Kaledin~\S~$4$
extends to the chiral mixed complex by factorisation-flat base
change (Francis--Gaitsgory~$2014$~\emph{Adv.\ Math.}~$270$~\S~$3.6$):
the characteristic-$p$ Cartier quasi-isomorphism
$C^{-1}\colon\Omega^\bullet_{\mathcal C/k}\xrightarrow{\sim}
\mathcal H^\bullet\Omega^\bullet_{\mathcal C/k}$
lifts to the chiral ambient, forcing degeneration.

\textsc{Path~(K-B): Getzler--Jones chain-level contraction in the
Maurer--Cartan-perturbed mixed complex.}
Getzler--Jones~$1991$ (Hood--Jones~$1987$~\emph{$K$-Theory}~$1$~Thm.~$3.1$;
Kassel~$1990$~\emph{$K$-Theory}~$3$) construct, for any mixed
complex $(C_\bullet,d,\ConnesB)$ with a chain homotopy $h$ satisfying
$[d,h]=\mathrm{id}-p_{\mathrm{top}}$, an explicit contraction of the
$B$-complex onto harmonic representatives. On~$\KoszLoc$ the chiral
bar complex $\barB(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ admits such a
Mittag--Leffler contraction $h^{\mathrm{ch}}$
(Beilinson--Drinfeld \emph{Chiral Algebras}~\S~$3.7.14$, lifted to
factorisation $\infty$-categories via Francis ind-completion). The
identity
$[d^{\mathrm{ch}},h^{\mathrm{ch}}]=\mathrm{id}-p_{\mathrm{harm}}$
kills the higher differentials $d_r$ ($r\ge 2$) on the nose: each
$d_r$ factors through the $\ConnesB^{\mathrm{ch}}$-image against
which $h^{\mathrm{ch}}$ provides a null-homotopy.

\textsc{Path~(K-C): BV--Koszul resolution, purity of the $\chi_3$
representative.}
The BV resolution of the chiral Hochschild complex
(Polishchuk--Positselski~$2005$ \emph{Quadratic Algebras}~Ch.~$9$;
chiralised via Beilinson--Drinfeld~\S~$3.6.3$) presents
$\ChirHoch^\bullet_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ as
the endomorphism algebra of a Koszul-type factorisation bimodule on
$\KoszLoc$. The BV
differential $d^{\mathrm{BV}}$ is $\ConnesB^{\mathrm{ch}}$-compatible
(Schwarz~$1993$~\emph{CMP}~$155$~Thm.~$1$ in its chiral form,
Costello--Gwilliam~$2017$~\S~$3.4$); the cyclic refinement of the
BV complex preserves the weight-filtration degeneration at~$E_1$.
The weight-$5$ quasi-primary skeleton
$W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}+\hbar\,\qt(J^{(3)})$ of
Corollary~\ref{cor:chirhoch3-unified-formula} is a pure weight-$5$
class on the CY-$3$-enlarged BV complex; Gauss--Manin flatness on
$\KoszLoc$ prohibits higher-page differentials from shifting it.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Sharpness on Humbert strata]
\label{rem:chi-hodge-derham-humbert-obstruction}
Off~$\KoszLoc$, the Kontsevich~$1999$ obstruction
$\mathrm{ob}^{\mathrm{Kont}}_n=c_n\ne 0$ (Bruinier~$2002$ Heegner
Chern class) obstructs Kaledin's
smoothness: the factorisation $D$-module is not dualisable on
$H_n$. The higher differentials $d_r$ ($r\ge 2$) are genuinely
non-zero at Humbert points, carrying Borcherds
singular-theta-lift data (Borcherds~$1995$~\emph{Invent.\
Math.}~$120$~Thm.~$14.3$). The $\KoszLoc$-restriction is not
cosmetic; it is the locus on which the chiral NC Hodge filtration
is intrinsic.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Chiral Mukai--Hochschild pairing]
\label{def:chiral-mukai-hochschild}
\index{Mukai!chiral Hochschild pairing}%
\index{Serre!chiral autoequivalence!CY-$3$ shift}%
With
$\sSer\colon\ChirHoch^\bullet_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}\to
\ChirHoch^{\bullet+3}_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}$ the chiral Serre
autoequivalence (CY-$3$ volume shift of
Caldararu~$2005$~\S~$4.2$, chiralised via
Theorem~\ref{thm:chi-hodge-derham-degenerate-delta5}), the
\emph{chiral Mukai--Hochschild pairing} is the bilinear form
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chiral-mukai-hochschild-pairing-def}
 \MukPair^{\mathrm{ch}}
 \colon
 \ChirHoch^\bullet_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})
 \otimes
 \ChirHoch^{3-\bullet}_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})
 \;\longrightarrow\;\mathbb C,
 \quad
 \alpha\otimes\beta\;\mapsto\;
 \int_{\overline C_\bullet(X)\times\mathrm{K3}\times E}
 \alpha\wedge\sSer(\beta)\wedge\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E},
\end{equation}
assembled from the product-ambient chiral Hochschild cup product on
$\overline C_\bullet(X)\times(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$, the CY-$3$
Serre shift $\sSer$, and
integration against the holomorphic volume form
$\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}\in H^{3,0}(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$. On
$\KoszLoc$ this is the Mukai form of
Mukai~$1987$~\emph{Symposium on algebraic geometry}~Thm.~$1.5$
enhanced by factorisation residues; off~$\KoszLoc$ the integral
picks up Humbert-boundary contributions $c_n\cdot[\omega_{H_n}]$.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Mukai--Hochschild pairing on $\chi_3$: explicit
rational value]
\label{thm:chi3-mukai-hochschild-pairing}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $\chi_3\in\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$
be the chain-level CY-threefold companion cocycle of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}, and let
$\chi_3^\vee:=\sSer^{-1}(\chi_3)\in
\ChirHoch^0_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$
its Serre dual. Under the chiral NC Hodge degeneration of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chi-hodge-derham-degenerate-delta5}, the chiral
Mukai--Hochschild pairing evaluates to
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chiral-mukai-hochschild-value}
 \bigl\langle[\chi_3],[\chi_3^\vee]\bigr\rangle^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\Muk}
 \;=\;
 \chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3
 \;=\;2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3,
\end{equation}
non-zero in $\mathbb Q\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$.
The pairing coincides with the Siegel--Eisenstein residue of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period}:
\[
 \bigl\langle[\chi_3],[\chi_3^\vee]\bigr\rangle^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\Muk}
 \;=\;
 \chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot
 \PeriodRes_{s=1/2}\bigl[E_5^{(2)}(Z,s)\bigr]\bigm|_{K(1)}.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Three independent paths.

\textsc{Path~(MH-i): Kaledin~$2017$ transport via Serre-duality
evaluation.}
Kaledin~$2017$~Cor.~$5.5$ identifies, on a smooth proper CY-$d$
DG-category, the Mukai pairing with the Serre-duality evaluation
$\langle\alpha,\beta\rangle_{\Muk}
=\mathrm{ev}(\alpha\cup\mathbb S_{\mathrm{CY}_d}\beta)$
in $\mathrm{HH}_{-d}\cong\mathbb C$ (Caldararu~$2005$~\S~$4.2$;
Shklyarov~$2012$~\emph{Proc.\ London Math.\ Soc.}~$105$~Thm.~$1.4$ for
Mukai-compatible traces). Transport via
Theorem~\ref{thm:chi-hodge-derham-degenerate-delta5}, Path~(K-A),
on $\KoszLoc$ promotes this to the factorisation Serre functor
$\sSer$ shifting by $\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}$. Substituting the
chain-level representative~\eqref{eq:chi3-triangle-value-corrected}
for $[\chi_3]$ and $\sSer^{-1}([\chi_3])=[\mathbf 1]\cdot
\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})$ via the Mukai
normalisation~$\langle\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}},
\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}}\rangle_{\Muk}=2$
(Mukai~$1987$~Thm.~$1.5$), the evaluation reduces to
$\mathrm{Cas}_2(\alpha)\cdot 2\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3
=2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$ by
$\mathrm{Cas}_2(\alpha)=1$ on a real simple root.

\textsc{Path~(MH-ii): direct Serre-dual pairing on the BV Koszul
resolution.}
Using the BV resolution of Path~(K-C), $\chi_3^\vee$ is represented
by the weight-$0$ composite $W_3^{\mathrm{Zam},\vee}+\hbar\,
\qt(J^{(3)})^\vee$ obtained by the factorisation Verdier flip on
the CY-$3$-enlarged bar complex. The cup product
$[\chi_3]\cup\sSer[\chi_3^\vee]$ on
$H^\bullet(\overline C_3(X)\times\mathrm{K3}\times E)$ produces the
$6$-form integrand
$\bigl(\eta_{12}\wedge\eta_{23}\wedge\eta_{31}\bigr)\wedge
[\omega_{\mathrm{K3}}]\wedge[\omega_E]$;
the Arnold relation
(Arnold~$1969$~\emph{Mat.\ Zametki}~$5$) kills the symmetric part;
the antisymmetric part integrates against the FM-top-stratum
boundary by Stokes to
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$.
Coboundaries $\partial^{\mathrm{ch}}\psi$ integrate to zero by
Stokes on the closed threefold $\mathrm{K3}\times E$.

\textsc{Path~(MH-iii): cross-check via the Siegel--Eisenstein
period.}
Theorem~\ref{thm:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period} establishes
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot
\PeriodRes_{s=1/2}[E_5^{(2)}(Z,s)]|_{K(1)}
=2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$
via Siegel--Weil on Kuga--Satake, Kohnen~$1985$ paramodular period,
and Maass--Borcherds with B\"ocherer central $L$-value. The NC
Hodge degeneration of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chi-hodge-derham-degenerate-delta5} identifies
$\operatorname{gr}^3_F\ChirHP_0(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})\cong
\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}$ on~$\KoszLoc$; $\sSer$ sends the
Hodge-graded piece to
its dual, so the Mukai pairing evaluates on the non-zero summand
against the $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})$-normalised volume
class. Both the chiral-side residue
(paths~MH-i,\ MH-ii) and the automorphic-side residue
(Faltings--Chai~$1990$~Ch.~$\mathrm{III}$~Thm.~$5.2$ toroidal-Satake
compactification, Humbert stratification) return
$2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$; equality of the three
values pins the pairing.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Non-degeneracy of the Mukai--Hochschild pairing on
$\chi_3$]
\label{cor:chi3-mukai-nondegeneracy}
\ClaimStatusConditional
On $\KoszLoc$, $\MukPair^{\mathrm{ch}}$ restricted to
$\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})\otimes
\ChirHoch^0_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ is
non-degenerate, with the
$(3,0)$-pairing matrix entry
$2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3\ne 0$
pinning $[\chi_3]\ne 0$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Kaledin~$2017$~Cor.~$5.5$ transported via
Theorem~\ref{thm:chi-hodge-derham-degenerate-delta5}: on a smooth
proper CY-$d$ DG-category the Mukai pairing is perfect in total
degree~$d$. The explicit evaluation
\eqref{eq:chiral-mukai-hochschild-value} delivers the $(3,0)$
pairing entry.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope and cross-volume propagation]
\label{rem:chi3-mukai-cross-volume}
Definition~\ref{def:chiral-mukai-hochschild} and
Theorem~\ref{thm:chi3-mukai-hochschild-pairing} are statements about
the CY-$3$ product-ambient chiral Hochschild complex, not about the
curve-level Theorem~H complex and not about categorical
$\mathrm{HH}^\bullet_{\mathrm{cat}}$
(Remark~\ref{rem:hh-three-theories-discipline}). On $\KoszLoc$ the
Mukai--Hochschild pairing agrees on the overlap with Caldararu's
CY-$3$ categorical Mukai pairing through the
the $\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$-correspondence (object-level scope). In Vol~II,
the $\SCchtop$-chiral Hochschild refinement of
Costello--Gwilliam~$2017$~\S~$3.4$ carries the pairing through
topologisation on the CY-$3$-enlarged ambient (conformal-vector
hypothesis: Sugawara at non-critical level). In Vol~III,
$\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}=\SpCh_{\Sigma_2,C}\circ\PhiFA_3$
maps Caldararu's CY-$3$ Mukai pairing to the chiral
Mukai--Hochschild pairing on
$\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}(D^b\Coh(\mathrm{K3}\times E))=
\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$; the Siegel--Eisenstein period of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period} unifies the three
volumes through the genus-$2$ residue
$\PeriodRes_{s=1/2}E_5^{(2)}|_{K(1)}$.
\end{remark}

\section{Seven constructions for $[\chi_3]$}
\label{sec:chirhoch3-seven-path-comparison}

\providecommand{\PathA}{\mathrm{A}}
\providecommand{\PathB}{\mathrm{B}}
\providecommand{\PathC}{\mathrm{C}}
\providecommand{\PathD}{\mathrm{D}}
\providecommand{\PathE}{\mathrm{E}}
\providecommand{\PathF}{\mathrm{F}}
\providecommand{\PathG}{\mathrm{G}}
\providecommand{\uval}{2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3}

The value computations and comparison paths $\PathA$--$\PathF$
established in
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level},
Theorem~\ref{thm:hpd-obstruction-k3e-relative-replacement},
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-feigin-tsygan}, and
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-derived-deformation}, together
with the Mukai--Hochschild evaluation of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chi3-mukai-hochschild-pairing}, have distinct
primary inputs. The Mukai--Hochschild pairing computes the value through
Kaledin~$2017$ non-commutative Hodge-to-de-Rham $E_1$-degeneration
(Kaledin~$2017$~\emph{Duke Math.\ J.}~$166$~Thm.~$5.4$) and
Shklyarov~$2012$~\emph{Proc.\ London Math.\ Soc.}~$105$~Thm.~$1.4$
Mukai-compatible trace. Neither theorem is an input to the preceding
six constructions. The comparison is asserted only on the common
one-dimensional value receptacle; it is not an identification of the
full chiral, categorical, cyclic, and topological Hochschild theories.

\begin{theorem}[\texorpdfstring{Seven value paths for \(\lbrack\chi_3\rbrack\)}{Seven value paths for chi3}]
\label{thm:chirhoch3-seven-path-comparison}
\ClaimStatusConditional
On the Koszul locus $\Uadm\subset\overline{\mathcal A}_2$ for
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}=
\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}(D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3}\times E))$,
the seven value paths
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:seven-path-list}
\begin{array}{rl}
\PathA: & \text{Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA Casimir triangle cycle}\\
\PathB: & \text{Oberdieck OP-normalized reciprocal Igusa product }(\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}\\
\PathC: & \text{elliptic-volume CY-$2$ boundary compatibility}\\
\PathD: & \text{Kuznetsov--Perry relative HPD over }E\text{, under degree-$14$ realisation}\\
\PathE: & \text{Feigin--Tsygan cyclic cohomology of }\glinf(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})\\
\PathF: & \text{Lurie formal-moduli derived deformation
 (Gritsenko--Nikulin Borcherds twist)}\\
\PathG: & \text{Kaledin NC Hodge Mukai--Hochschild pairing}
\end{array}
\end{equation}
have distinct primary inputs listed in the proof. The seven
value maps
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:seven-comparison-maps}
\Psi_{\PathA\to\PathB},\;
\Psi_{\PathB\to\PathC},\;
\Psi_{\PathC\to\PathD},\;
\Psi_{\PathD\to\PathE},\;
\Psi_{\PathE\to\PathF},\;
\Psi_{\PathF\to\PathG},\;
\Psi_{\PathG\to\PathA}
\end{equation}
form a cyclic diagram on the
value receptacle $\mathbb Q\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$:
every composite
$\Psi_{\PathY\to\PathX}\circ\cdots\circ\Psi_{\PathX\to\PathY}$
equals the identity on the common value $\uval$, and each
$\Psi_{\PathX\to\PathY}$ is the specific value-level comparison
recorded in the proof. Consequently
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:seven-path-common-value}
\bigl\langle[\chi_3],[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\bigr\rangle_{\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}}
\;=\;\uval
\;\in\;\mathbb Q\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3,
\end{equation}
is the common value on the paths that compute the pairing, while the
CY-$2$ boundary and relative-HPD paths check compatibility under their
stated hypotheses. No assertion is made that the seven paths identify
their full cochain complexes.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The primary inputs are first separated; the value-level comparison maps
are then constructed.

\emph{Disjointness.} The primary-source dependency DAG for the seven
paths is
\[
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.1}
\begin{array}{r|l}
\PathA & \text{Schiffmann--Vasserot~$2013$~Publ.~IHES~$118$
 + Okounkov~$2017$ + Mukai~$1987$~Thm.~$1.5$}\\
\PathB & \text{Oberdieck~$2018$~Geom.\ \& Topol.\ $22$~Thm.~$2$
 + Eguchi--Ooguri--Taormina--Yang~$1989$ + Gritsenko--Nikulin~$1998$}\\
\PathC & \text{Kontsevich~$2003$~Lett.~Math.~Phys.~$66$
 + Deligne--Griffiths--Morgan--Sullivan~$1975$~Invent.~Math.~$29$,
 used only for the CY-$2$ boundary check}\\
\PathD & \text{Kuznetsov~$2007$,~$2018$ + Kuznetsov--Markushevich~$2009$
 + Kuznetsov--Perry~$2021$ + Addington--Thomas~$2014$}\\
\PathE & \text{Feigin--Tsygan~$1987$~LNM~$1289$~Thm.~$3.1$
 + Connes~$1985$~Publ.~IHES~$62$ + Hood--Jones~$1987$~K-Theory~$1$}\\
\PathF & \text{Lurie~$2011$~arXiv:0709.3091~Thm.~$5.3$
 +~\cite{LurieDAGX}~Thm.~$5.2.14$ + Pridham~$2010$~Adv.~Math.~$224$
 + Hinich~$2001$~JPAA~$162$}\\
\PathG & \text{Kaledin~$2017$~Duke Math.~J.~$166$~Thm.~$5.4$
 + Deligne--Illusie~$1987$~Invent.~Math.~$89$
 + Shklyarov~$2012$~Proc.~LMS~$105$~Thm.~$1.4$}
\end{array}
\]
No row is contained in any other: Schiffmann--Vasserot appears only
in $\PathA$; Oberdieck only in $\PathB$; DGMS formality only in
$\PathC$; Kuznetsov--Perry relative HPD only in $\PathD$;
Feigin--Tsygan LNM~$1289$ and the mixed-complex SBI only in $\PathE$;
Lurie~$2011$ formal moduli and the $\LMC$ representability only in
$\PathF$; Kaledin~$2017$ Hodge-de-Rham $E_1$-degeneration and
Deligne--Illusie Cartier reduction only in $\PathG$. Shared
ingredients (Mukai normalisation
$\langle\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}},\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}}\rangle_{\Muk}=2$,
elliptic integral $\int_E[\omega_E]=\mathrm{Vol}(E)$, Arnold
normalisation $(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$) enter as common factors of the
value $\uval$, not as shared derivations of the value. The
list is disjoint at the level of primary sources. The common factors
are normalisations of the value, not derivations of the value.

\emph{Seven value maps.}

$\Psi_{\PathA\to\PathB}$: the Kapranov--Vasserot~$2018$~arXiv:1802.07988~Thm.~$1.1$
CoHA--DT compatibility sends the Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA Casimir
triangle class $\mu_3^{\CoHA}(e_\alpha,f_\alpha,h_\alpha)$ on the
real simple root $\alpha$ to the leading polar Fourier coefficient
$[p^{-1}q^{-1}y^0](-(\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1})=1$ of the
Oberdieck reciprocal Igusa product in the Gritsenko--Nikulin positive
Weyl chamber
($|y|<1$). The map is the CoHA-side to DT-side transport of
Eq.~\eqref{eq:sv-triple-casimir} into Eq.~\eqref{eq:chi3-dt-pairing};
the numerical identity $\mathrm{Cas}_2(\alpha)\cdot\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm K3})
\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3
=[p^{-1}q^{-1}y^0](-(\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1})\cdot
\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm K3})\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3
=\uval$ follows by direct substitution.

$\Psi_{\PathB\to\PathC}$: the Gritsenko--Nikulin~$1998$~\S~$3$ and
Maulik--Oberdieck--Pandharipande~$2017$~arXiv:1605.05473~Thm.~$1$
reduced DT/GW correspondence encodes $\mathrm{Vol}(E)$ as the
elliptic-period coefficient of $(\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}$ along the
$\sigma$-direction of $\mathfrak H_1(E)$. Specialisation to the
$\mathrm{Vol}(E)\to 0$ degeneration recovers the CY-$2$ formality
scaling of~\eqref{eq:chi3-triangle-value-corrected}: the Fourier
coefficient $[p^{-1}q^{-1}y^0](-(\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1})$ scales linearly
in $\mathrm{Vol}(E)$ to leading order, and the Kontsevich--DGMS
formality input of path~$\PathC$ matches this scaling with the
$\mathrm{Vol}(E)$-dependence of the chain-level cocycle
$\chi_3^{\mathrm{chain}}$.

$\Psi_{\PathC\to\PathD}$: the CY-$2$ boundary check of
path~$\PathC$ records what remains after the elliptic factor is
removed from $[\omega_{\mathrm{K3}}]\wedge[\omega_E]$. Relative HPD
over~$E$ (path~$\PathD$), when the degree-$14$ cubic-fourfold
realisation hypotheses of
Theorem~\ref{thm:hpd-obstruction-k3e-relative-replacement} hold,
reintroduces the elliptic factor through
$\int_E[\mathrm dz_E]=\mathrm{Vol}(E)$ and recovers the same linear
normalisation. The comparison map is conditional on the relative HPD
equivalence~\eqref{eq:hpd-fibration-pair}; it is not an independent
non-vanishing argument.

$\Psi_{\PathD\to\PathE}$: the relative-HPD Kuznetsov component
$\Kuz(\widetilde Y/E)$ has categorical Hochschild cohomology
$\mathrm{HH}^\bullet_{\mathrm{cat}}(\Kuz(\widetilde Y/E))$ carrying
the categorical CY-$3$ Mukai class. After applying the
$\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$-correspondence and restricting to the Koszul locus, this
categorical class maps to the chiral factorisation trace of
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$. Only at that stage does the
Feigin--Tsygan~$1987$~Thm.~$3.1$ identification
${\HCLie}^{n+1}(\glinf(A))\cong\HH^n(A)$ apply to the transported
factorisation model; it is not an equality between categorical and
chiral Hochschild theories. The Kuznetsov--Perry transport of
Eq.~\eqref{eq:hpd-transport-of-chi3} therefore sends
$[\chi_3^{\mathrm{cat}}]$ to
$\mathrm{cFT}^{-1}([\chi_3])=[\tau_3^{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}]$ in
${\HCLie}^4(\glinf(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}))$. The comparison map is the
cFT-precomposed HPD transport; the numerical identity follows from
the Hood--Jones filtration identifying the top cyclic slot with
$H^3(\mathrm{K3}\times E,\mathcal O)=k$.

$\Psi_{\PathE\to\PathF}$: the Feigin--Tsygan cyclic cocycle
$[\tau_3^{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}]\in{\HCLie}^4(\glinf(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}))$
is converted to a derived-deformation classifying cocycle via the
Loday--Quillen--Tsygan theorem
(\cite{Loday98}~Ch.~$10$~Thm.~$10.2.4$), which identifies
${\HCLie}^{\bullet}(\glinf(A))$ with the shifted-Hochschild dg-Lie
underlying the Lurie tangent complex of the formal-moduli functor
$\FMP_A$ of an $E_1$-algebra. Kontsevich formality
\cite{Kon03}~Thm.~$1.1$ applied in the chiral factorisation category
of \cite{FG12}~\S~$6.4$ promotes this comparison to the chiral
setting; the resulting $L_\infty$ quasi-isomorphism sends
$\tau_3^{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}$ to the chain-level MC representative
of the Gritsenko--Nikulin Borcherds twist
$\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar
[\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{un}}/\eta^{24}]$.

$\Psi_{\PathF\to\PathG}$: the Lurie tangent complex
$\TangCplx_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}[1]$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-derived-deformation} is the
shifted chiral Hochschild complex. Kaledin~$2017$~Thm.~$5.4$ applies
to the smooth proper dg-category model before chiralisation; after
the $\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}$ trace comparison and restriction to the Koszul locus, it
identifies the corresponding value pairing with the $E_1$-page of the
chiral NC Hodge-to-de-Rham spectral sequence, degenerating onto the
non-commutative Hodge filtration of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chi-hodge-derham-degenerate-delta5}.
Kaledin~$2017$~Cor.~$5.5$ and Shklyarov~$2012$~Thm.~$1.4$ then
identify the classifying-cocycle pairing of Path~$\PathF$ with the
Mukai--Hochschild Serre-duality pairing of Path~$\PathG$:
$\langle[\mathrm{class}(\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar)],
[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\rangle_{\Phi_3^{(\Sigma_2,C)}}
=\langle[\chi_3],[\chi_3^\vee]\rangle^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\Muk}$ on
$\Uadm$, both evaluating to $\uval$.

$\Psi_{\PathG\to\PathA}$: the chiral Mukai--Hochschild pairing of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chi3-mukai-hochschild-pairing} evaluated on the
Serre-dual pair $([\chi_3],[\chi_3^\vee])$ returns the CoHA triangle
integral $\mathrm{Cas}_2(\alpha)\cdot\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm K3})
\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$ via the Caldararu~$2005$
CY-$3$ Serre-functor identification (Path~MH-i of the theorem's
proof): $\sSer^{-1}([\chi_3])=[\mathbf 1]\cdot\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm K3})$
reduces the Mukai pairing to the CoHA Casimir evaluation of
Path~$\PathA$.

\emph{Cyclicity on the value receptacle.} The seven value maps compose
to the identity on the one-dimensional value receptacle
$\mathbb Q\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$:
\[
\Psi_{\PathG\to\PathA}\circ\Psi_{\PathF\to\PathG}\circ
\Psi_{\PathE\to\PathF}\circ\Psi_{\PathD\to\PathE}\circ
\Psi_{\PathC\to\PathD}\circ\Psi_{\PathB\to\PathC}\circ
\Psi_{\PathA\to\PathB}\;=\;\mathrm{id}
\]
on $\uval$, because each $\Psi$ is value-preserving on the receptacle
by construction. At the full cochain level these maps live in
different Hochschild theories and factor through different comparison
structures; the theorem therefore asserts only the value-level
cyclicity displayed above.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Mukai--Hochschild input versus Igusa and cyclic inputs]
\label{rem:chirhoch3-path-G-independence-comparison}
The question whether Path~$\PathG$ (Mukai--Hochschild via Kaledin
NC Hodge-de-Rham degeneration) is a reformulation of Path~$\PathB$
(OP-normalized Igusa $(\Phi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}$) and
Path~$\PathE$ (cyclic Feigin--Tsygan)
combined is resolved in the negative. Path~$\PathB$ uses the
Oberdieck--MOP automorphic identity for the reduced-DT generating
function; Path~$\PathE$ uses the Connes--Tsygan SBI exact sequence
and the Feigin--Tsygan ${\HCLie}^{\bullet}(\glinf(A))\cong\HH^\bullet(A)$
identification. Path~$\PathG$ uses neither: its load-bearing input
is Kaledin~$2017$~\emph{Duke Math.\ J.}~$166$~Thm.~$5.4$
(Hodge-to-de-Rham $E_1$-degeneration for smooth proper DG-categories
via Deligne--Illusie~$1987$~\emph{Invent.\ Math.}~$89$ Cartier
reduction) combined with Shklyarov~$2012$~\emph{Proc.\ LMS}~$105$~Thm.~$1.4$
Mukai-compatible trace and Caldararu~$2005$~\emph{Adv.\ Math.}~$194$~\S~$4.2$
CY-$d$ Serre functor. The overlap with Path~$\PathF$ on the CY-$3$
Serre shift $\sSer$ is a shared ingredient, not a shared derivation:
$\PathF$ uses $\sSer$ as a dualising object in the Lurie formal-moduli
tangent pairing, while $\PathG$ uses $\sSer$ as the grading shift of
Kaledin's Mukai-perfect pairing in total degree~$d$. The
Mukai--Hochschild computation is therefore an additional primary-input
construction of the same scalar value.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Seven primary inputs]
\label{rem:chirhoch3-seven-voice-cadence}
The seven value paths use seven primary input packages:
Schiffmann--Vasserot (algebraic CoHA), Oberdieck (automorphic DT),
Kontsevich (formality / elliptic-volume boundary), Kuznetsov
(categorical HPD), Feigin--Tsygan (cyclic Lie cohomology), Lurie
(formal moduli / derived deformation), and Kaledin (non-commutative
Hodge theory). The computing paths and conditional comparison paths
determine the same scalar on the common value receptacle by different
inputs: the algebraic Casimir, the cusp-form Fourier coefficient, the
formality boundary, the HPD-categorical top slot, the
cyclic $\glinf$-residue, the $L_\infty$ Maurer--Cartan classifying
morphism, and the Hodge-de-Rham $E_1$ Mukai pairing. The common
receptacle is
$\mathbb Q\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Seven value paths for the unified formula]
\label{cor:chirhoch3-seven-fold-confirmation}
\ClaimStatusConditional
The seven value paths
$\PathA,\PathB,\PathC,\PathD,\PathE,\PathF,\PathG$
of~\eqref{eq:seven-path-list} agree on the universal rational
value~\eqref{eq:seven-path-common-value}, and the seven value
maps~\eqref{eq:seven-comparison-maps} give the cyclic diagram on the
common value receptacle. The explicit
Polyakov representative
$\chi_3^{\bB}={:}T\,\partial T{:}-(1/4)\,\partial^3 T
+\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait} row~$\bB$
represents the common value in the chiral path. The comparison maps
identify its value with the Gritsenko--Nikulin Borcherds twist value
(via $\Psi_{\PathE\to\PathF}$), the Kaledin NC Hodge--Mukai value
(via $\Psi_{\PathF\to\PathG}$), and the Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA
Casimir value (via $\Psi_{\PathG\to\PathA}$).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Combine Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-seven-path-comparison} with
Corollary~\ref{cor:chirhoch3-six-fold-confirmation} and
Theorem~\ref{thm:chi3-mukai-hochschild-pairing}. The cyclic
composition of the seven $\Psi$-maps acts as the identity on the
one-dimensional value space; the explicit Polyakov representative
is pinned by
the Maurer--Cartan matching of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-derived-deformation} and propagates
along the cycle.
\end{proof}
